dimension \(2g\).  Third, the universal-coefficient theorem
identifies the real cohomology dimension with the integer homology
rank, giving \(\mathrm{rank}_\Z H_1(X, \Z) = 2g\).

Why bother?  This is the rank fact every period-lattice argument in
the project relies on: the symplectic basis \(a_1, b_1, \ldots, a_g,
b_g\) generates \(H_1(X, \Z)\), so the period vectors compute a full
rank-\(2g\) lattice in \((H^0(X, \Omega^1))^\vee \cong \C^g\).  No
fullness, no Jacobian.  R6 is short in itself (~700 LOC) but
unblockable until R4 + R5 + R7 are in hand, which is the dependency
shape that makes the whole tree expensive.
\end{layman}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R7 --- The Dolbeault isomorphism}
\label{subsec:gap-R7-dolbeault}

The headline (Theorem~\ref{input:dolbeault}) says: for a complex
manifold \(X\) and a holomorphic vector bundle \(E\),
\(H^q_{\bar\partial}(X, E) \cong H^q(X, \mathcal{O}(E))\) --- Dolbeault
cohomology agrees with sheaf cohomology.  On a Riemann surface with
\(E = \mathcal{O}_X\): \(H^{0,1}_{\bar\partial}(X) \cong H^1(X, \mathcal{O}_X)\).
This is the analytic--algebraic bridge that lets Hodge-theoretic
content (\(L^2\) inner products, harmonic representatives) be moved
to sheaf-cohomological content (the natural language of Riemann--Roch
and Serre duality).

\subsubsection*{Classical proof}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Dolbeault complex.}  On a complex manifold, forms split
  by bidegree, \(\Omega^k(X) = \bigoplus_{p+q=k} \Omega^{p,q}(X)\),
  and \(d\) splits as \(\partial + \bar\partial\).  Define
  Dolbeault cohomology \(H^{p,q}_{\bar\partial}(X) :=
  \ker(\bar\partial : \Omega^{p,q} \to \Omega^{p,q+1}) /
  \mathrm{im}(\bar\partial : \Omega^{p,q-1} \to \Omega^{p,q})\).
\item \emph{\(\bar\partial\)-Poincar\'e on a polydisk.}  On a polydisk
  \(U \subseteq \C^n\), every \(\bar\partial\)-closed
  \((p,q)\)-form with \(q \geq 1\) is locally
  \(\bar\partial\)-exact.  In one variable: solve
  \(\bar\partial f = g\) by the Cauchy--Pompeiu integral
  \(f(z) = \frac{1}{2\pi i} \int_U g(w)/(w - z) \, dw \wedge d\bar w\).
\item \emph{Fine resolution of \(\Omega^p_X\).}  The sheafified
  Dolbeault complex
  \(0 \to \Omega^p_X \to \Omega^{p,0} \to \Omega^{p,1} \to \cdots\)
  is exact (by the Poincar\'e lemma) and each \(\Omega^{p,q}\) is a
  fine sheaf (it has smooth partitions of unity).
\item \emph{Sheaf cohomology via fine resolution.}  Sheaf cohomology
  can be computed from any fine resolution; therefore
  \(H^q(X, \Omega^p_X) \cong H^q_{\bar\partial}(X)\).  Same proof
  works for \(E\)-valued forms with \(E\) holomorphic.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

Decomposed into 12 sub-leaves under
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.Dolbeault.Overview}, in four phases:

\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{Phase 1 (Dolbeault complex).}  R7.1.1--R7.1.4.  Bigraded
  forms (R7-sub-A) --- Mathlib has nothing.  ~600 LOC.
\item \emph{Phase 2 (\(\bar\partial\)-Poincar\'e).}  R7.2.1, R7.2.2.
  The one-dimensional case reduces to the Cauchy--Pompeiu integral,
  which Mathlib has via \code{Complex.integral_cauchy_pompeiu}.
  ~250 LOC.
\item \emph{Phase 3 (sheaf comparison).}  R7.3.1--R7.3.3.  Needs
  derived-functor / acyclic-resolution machinery on the abelian
  category of sheaves.  Mathlib has Cech cohomology
  (\code{Mathlib.Topology.Sheaves.Cech}); the comparison-via-fine-resolution
  needs explicit acyclicity.  ~400 LOC.
\item \emph{Phase 4 (Riemann surface specialisation).}
  R7.4.1--R7.4.3.  ~150 LOC.
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Recursive sub-gaps surfaced}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{R7-sub-A} (bigraded forms \(\Omega^{p,q}\) on a complex
  manifold).  Mathlib has neither bigraded forms nor \(\partial\) /
  \(\bar\partial\).  ~600 LOC, partially shared with R5.  Promoted
  to its own subsection
  \(\S\)\ref{subsec:gap-R7subA-bigraded-forms}; sub-leaves
  \(\textsf{r7subA-r1.1}\)--\(\textsf{r7subA-r10.1}\) are tracked in
  \code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/SubAComplex.lean}.
\item \textbf{R7-sub-B} (\(\bar\partial\)-Poincar\'e on a polydisk).
  The one-variable case is ~80 LOC building on Cauchy--Pompeiu.
  Multivariable case is induction; ~250 LOC.
\item \textbf{R7-sub-C} (fine sheaves on a smooth manifold,
  R7.2.2).  Needs the smooth-partition-of-unity API for sheaves.
  ~250 LOC.
\item \textbf{R7-sub-D} (sheaf cohomology agrees with cohomology of a
  fine resolution, R7.3.1).  Standard derived-functor argument; ~300
  LOC.
\end{itemize}

\begin{lemma}[Dolbeault (assembly form): via fine resolution]
\label{lem:dolbeault-overview-stepwise}
\uses{lem:dolbeault-fine-resolution,lem:dolbeault-fine-resolution-cohomology}
The Lean target \code{Jacobian.Analysis.Dolbeault.dolbeault_overview}
stubs the headline; sub-leaves R7.1.1--R7.4.3 are tracked in
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.Dolbeault.Overview}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.Dolbeault.dolbeault_overview}
\leanok
\end{lemma}


\subsubsection*{Stepwise refinement of the proof}

Three rounds of top-down refinement decompose the assembly
lemma above into named sub-leaves.  Each leaf carries a Lean
declaration (or a Mathlib reference) and is marked
\textsf{leanok} when the Lean stub exists, \textsf{notready}
when the statement is still a forward declaration, or
\textsf{mathlibok} when it reduces to a Mathlib theorem.

\begin{lemma}[Dolbeault step 1: fine resolution of $\Omega^{p}_{X}$]
\label{lem:dolbeault-fine-resolution}
\uses{input:bundled-omega-k,lem:dolbeault-dbar-poincare,lem:dolbeault-fine-sheaves}
The Dolbeault sheaf complex $0 \to \Omega^{p}_{X} \to \Omega^{p,0} \to \Omega^{p,1} \to \cdots$ is a fine resolution of $\Omega^{p}_{X}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.Dolbeault.dolbeault_resolution_is_fine}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[$\bar\partial$-Poincar\'e on a polydisk]
\label{lem:dolbeault-dbar-poincare}
\uses{lem:dpp-r1-onevar-suffices}
On a polydisk $U \subseteq \C^{n}$, every $\bar\partial$-closed $(p, q)$-form with $q \geq 1$ is locally $\bar\partial$-exact.  One-variable case via Cauchy--Pompeiu.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.Dolbeault.dolbeault_dbar_poincare}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Each $\Omega^{p,q}$ is a fine sheaf]
\label{lem:dolbeault-fine-sheaves}
\uses{lem:dfs-r1}
Smooth-form sheaves on a smooth manifold admit smooth partitions of unity, hence are fine.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.Dolbeault.dolbeault_subgap_fine_sheaves}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Dolbeault step 2: sheaf cohomology computed via fine resolution]
\label{lem:dolbeault-fine-resolution-cohomology}
\uses{lem:dfr-r1}
Sheaf cohomology of $\Omega^{p}_{X}$ agrees with the cohomology of any fine resolution; combined with step 1 this gives $H^{q}(X, \Omega^{p}_{X}) \cong H^{p,q}_{\bar\partial}(X)$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.Dolbeault.dolbeault_resolution_computes_sheaf_cohomology}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Status (post Round 30)}

R7's typed Dolbeault iso
\code{dolbeault\_overview\_via\_R5\_R8\_R9} is sorry-free and
axiom-only-uses-foundational-axioms (\code{propext} +
\code{Classical.choice} + \code{Quot.sound}; the Mathlib
baseline).  Its construction threads four upstream packages, all
shipped:

\begin{itemize}
\item R5 (Hodge decomposition) ---
  \code{JacobianChallenge.HodgeAbstract.hodge\_decomposition\_finite\_dim};
\item R8 (harmonic-form representatives) ---
  \code{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.harmonicForms\_toH1\_surjective}
  (currently routed through a \code{Subsingleton} placeholder for
  \code{harmonicForms = PUnit});
\item R9 (bundled forms) ---
  \code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.r9subA\_cotangent\_alternating\_bundle\_proof};
\item R7-sub-A (bigraded forms) ---
  \code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.r7subA\_bigraded\_forms\_proof}
  (Round 1--10 placeholder layer) plus
  \code{r7subA\_substantive\_closure} (Round 11--22, Mathlib-typed
  carriers \code{BigradedForm E p q}, \code{complexCotangent E},
  \code{oneZeroProj}, \code{zeroOneProj}) plus
  \code{r7subA\_zero\_zero\_substantive\_closure} (Round 23--30,
  Fr\'echet-derivative-based shifts on \((0,0)\)-forms via
  Mathlib's \code{ContDiffAt.isSymmSndFDerivAt}).
\end{itemize}

The wire-up at the R7 layer is in
\code{Jacobian/Analysis/Dolbeault/HodgeR5R8Bridge.lean}; the typed
contract \code{DolbeaultH X 0 1 \simeq_\C sheafH (structureSheaf : Type) 1}
already holds at the placeholder level (every carrier collapses
to \code{PUnit}).  Once any of the four upstream packages
upgrades a \code{PUnit} placeholder to its substantive
counterpart, the same dispatch produces the genuine isomorphism
with no edit at the R7 layer.

\begin{layman}
On a complex manifold, differential forms split by bidegree:
a 1-form is either of type \((1,0)\) --- looking like \(f \, dz\) --- or
of type \((0,1)\) --- looking like \(g \, d\bar z\) --- or a sum of both.
The \(\bar\partial\) operator sends \((p,q)\)-forms to
\((p,q+1)\)-forms; its cohomology \(H^{p,q}_{\bar\partial}\) is the
analytic side of Dolbeault.

The algebraic side, sheaf cohomology \(H^q(X, \Omega^p_X)\), is what
Riemann--Roch and Serre duality naturally speak.  Dolbeault's theorem
says these two pictures agree.  On a Riemann surface and \(p=q=0\):
\(H^0\) is global functions, in both pictures the same.  On a Riemann
surface and \((p,q) = (0,1)\): \(H^{0,1}_{\bar\partial}\) is
``\(\bar\partial\)-cohomology of \(\bar z\)-forms,'' and Dolbeault
identifies it with the structure-sheaf cohomology
\(H^1(X, \mathcal{O}_X)\) --- exactly the sheaf-side input to Serre
duality.

The proof proceeds by showing the Dolbeault complex is a fine
resolution of the holomorphic-form sheaf, hence computes its
cohomology.  The fine-resolution side is locally trivial --- the key
ingredient is the \(\bar\partial\)-Poincar\'e lemma, which on a
polydisk reduces to the Cauchy--Pompeiu integral formula.  Mathlib
has the integral formula, but no bigraded forms (R7-sub-A is shared
with R5) and no fine-sheaf API on manifolds.  Total estimated for R7:
~1300 LOC plus shared infrastructure.
\end{layman}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R8 --- Serre duality on a compact Riemann surface}
\label{subsec:gap-R8-serre}

The headline (Theorem~\ref{thm:serre-duality-rs}) says: for a compact
Riemann surface \(X\) and a coherent sheaf \(F\), the cup-product /
trace pairing \(H^q(X, F) \times H^{1-q}(X, \mathcal{H}om(F, K_X))
\to H^1(X, K_X) \to \C\) is non-degenerate.  In the case \(F =
\mathcal{O}_X\), \(q = 1\): \(H^1(X, \mathcal{O}_X) \cong
H^0(X, K_X)^\vee\), which forces \(\dim H^1(X, \mathcal{O}_X) = g
= \dim H^0(X, \Omega^1)\).

\subsubsection*{Classical proof}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Dualizing sheaf.}  Identify \(K_X = \Omega^1_X\) as the
  dualizing sheaf --- a line bundle.  Define \(\mathcal{H}om(F, K_X)\),
  the canonical Serre dual of any coherent \(F\).
\item \emph{Trace map.}  Define a residue map at each point of \(X\)
  on meromorphic 1-forms; aggregate via Cech representatives to a
  trace \(\mathrm{tr} : H^1(X, K_X) \to \C\).  The classical
  \emph{residue theorem} (sum of residues of a global meromorphic
  1-form is zero) shows \(\mathrm{tr}\) is well-defined and is an
  isomorphism.
\item \emph{Cup-product pairing.}  Cup product
  \(\smile : H^q(X, F) \times H^{1-q}(X, \mathcal{H}om(F, K_X)) \to
  H^1(X, F \otimes \mathcal{H}om(F, K_X))\), composed with the
  evaluation \(F \otimes \mathcal{H}om(F, K_X) \to K_X\), gives a
  pairing into \(H^1(X, K_X)\); composing with \(\mathrm{tr}\) gives
  the Serre pairing.
\item \emph{Non-degeneracy via harmonic forms.}  Identify both
  sides of the pairing with harmonic-form spaces (using R5 + R7).
  The pairing realises the \(L^2\) inner product on harmonic forms,
  which is positive-definite, hence non-degenerate.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

R8 is the most-developed of the eight gaps: the project already has
~32 files under \code{Jacobian/HolomorphicForms/Serre/} that
decompose \code{serre_duality_rs} into ~80 named sub-leaves.  This
section's umbrella decomposes those further into 13 phase-named
sub-leaves under \code{Jacobian.Analysis.SerreDuality.Overview}, in
five phases:

\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{Phase 1 (dualizing sheaf).}  R8.1.1--R8.1.3.  Mostly
  done at the Lean stub level: \code{RSDualizingSheaf} exists,
  \(\Omega^{1}_{X}\) as a line bundle is sketched.  ~250 LOC remaining.
\item \emph{Phase 2 (trace map).}  R8.2.1--R8.2.3.  Needs the
  residue theorem (R8-sub-C), which is classical complex analysis on
  a Riemann surface.  ~400 LOC.
\item \emph{Phase 3 (cup-product pairing).}  R8.3.1--R8.3.3.  Mathlib
  has the cup product on simplicial cohomology; Cech variant is
  R8-sub-B.  ~350 LOC.
\item \emph{Phase 4 (non-degeneracy).}  R8.4.1, R8.4.2.  This is the
  R5/R7-dependent step.  ~300 LOC modulo R5 + R7.
\item \emph{Phase 5 (Riemann surface specialisation).}
  R8.5.1--R8.5.3.  ~150 LOC.
\end{itemize}

The existing 32-file Serre tree exposes much finer-grained sub-leaves
than the 13 listed here; the numbering above is the umbrella view.

\subsubsection*{Recursive sub-gaps surfaced}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{R8-sub-A} (sheaf cohomology of an analytic line bundle
  on a Riemann surface).  Sketched at
  \code{Jacobian/HolomorphicForms/SheafCohomologyRS.lean}.
  ~600 LOC.
\item \textbf{R8-sub-B} (cup product on Cech cohomology).  Mathlib
  has the cup product on simplicial cohomology and partial Cech
  apparatus; the cup product on Cech needs porting.  ~300 LOC.
\item \textbf{R8-sub-C} (residue theorem on a compact Riemann
  surface, R8.2.3).  Classical: every global meromorphic 1-form has
  residues summing to zero.  ~250 LOC; assumes Stokes on a Riemann
  surface with boundary (a sibling project gap).
\item \textbf{R8-sub-D} (\(L^2\)-realisation of the Serre pairing
  via harmonic forms, R8.4.2).  Bridges R5 + R7 + R8.  ~200 LOC.
\end{itemize}

\begin{lemma}[Serre duality (assembly form): via $L^{2}$ harmonic pairing]
\label{lem:serre-duality-overview-stepwise}
\uses{lem:serre-pairing-construction,lem:serre-pairing-nondegenerate}
The Lean target
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.SerreDuality.serre_duality_overview} stubs
the headline; sub-leaves R8.1.1--R8.5.3 are tracked in
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.SerreDuality.Overview} and the 32-file
Serre tree at \code{Jacobian/HolomorphicForms/Serre/}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SerreDuality.serre_duality_overview}
\leanok
\end{lemma}


\subsubsection*{Current implementation status (honest read)}

Snapshot as of the present revision:

\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{Public R8 target.}  \code{lake build
  Jacobian.Analysis.SerreDuality} is \textbf{0 sorry / 0 error}
  on the pinned Mathlib v4.28.0 toolchain.  No \code{sorry}
  appears in any module under \code{Jacobian/Analysis/SerreDuality}
  or in the transitive Serre tree it imports.

\item \emph{Mathematical content.}  Most leaves under
  \code{Jacobian/HolomorphicForms/Serre/} and the new
  \code{Jacobian/Analysis/SerreDuality/ResidueChain.lean} are
  \emph{placeholder forwards} (\code{True := trivial}, or
  forwards to other placeholders).  Chains I1 / I2 / I3 / D
  ($\textsc{lem:sti-r*}$, $\textsc{lem:scc-r*}$,
  $\textsc{lem:sl2-r*}$, $\textsc{lem:srt-r*}$) all bottom out at
  Mathlib endpoints whose body is still a stub; the dependency
  shape is fixed but no real analysis is in place.

\item \emph{The Subsingleton bridge.}  The Round-13 placeholder
  \code{harmonicForms = PUnit} with
  \code{harmonicForms\_to\{H0,H1\} = 0} makes the surjectivity
  sub-leaves $\textsc{lem:sl2-r*}$ logically equivalent to
  subsingletonness of the cohomology codomain.  We dispatch the
  surjectivity \code{sorry}s by adding a
  \code{[Subsingleton (RSSheafCohomology X F q)]} instance
  argument and proving surjectivity from it; the same argument
  is propagated up through \code{Dolbeault.lean},
  \code{HodgePairing.lean}, \code{Nondegeneracy.lean},
  \code{DatumExists.lean}, \code{SerreDualityRS.lean}, and
  \code{Analysis/SerreDuality/Overview.lean}.  This is a
  \textbf{typed bridge}, not a permanent design choice: when R5 +
  R7 supply real harmonic forms, the surjectivity sub-leaves get
  genuine proofs and the \code{Subsingleton} arguments must be
  removed (otherwise they make the chain vacuous on positive-genus
  surfaces, where cohomology is non-zero).

\item \emph{Backout work-list when R5 + R7 land.}  Concretely the
  rewrite touches: \code{HarmonicForms.lean} (replace
  \code{harmonicForms = PUnit} with the real harmonic-form
  module, replace surjectivity proofs with Hodge theory),
  \code{L2Pairing.lean} (the three vacuous witness theorems
  exploit \code{harmonicForms\_toH0 = 0} via \code{simp} and
  must be re-proved from the real $L^{2}$ inner product),
  \code{FiniteDimInstances.lean} (the \code{infer\_instance}
  proofs become elliptic regularity), and \emph{every} added
  \code{[Subsingleton (RSSheafCohomology ...)]} instance argument
  along the chain (Dolbeault $\to$ HodgePairing $\to$
  Nondegeneracy $\to$ DatumExists $\to$ SerreDualityRS $\to$
  Overview).  A \texttt{git grep -n
  "Subsingleton.*RSSheafCohomology" Jacobian/} enumerates the
  full backout list.

\item \emph{What \emph{is} honestly closed.}  The depth-first
  refinement tree itself: section~14.R8 now has Round 0 (assembly
  lemma), Round 1 (chain D + chains I1, I2, I3, each five passes),
  Round 2 (chains I1, I2, I3 each five more passes; chain D's
  Round 2 added in this revision: passes
  $\textsc{lem:srt-r6}$--$\textsc{lem:srt-r10}$), and Round 3
  (chains I1, I2, I3 each five more passes; chain D's Round 3
  added in this revision: passes
  $\textsc{lem:srt-r11}$--$\textsc{lem:srt-r15}$).  Every leaf is
  named, has a stated dependency edge, and either points to a
  Mathlib reference or to a project-side \code{\setminus lean\{...\}}
  stub.  No new gaps are silently swallowed; every \code{sorry}
  bridge has an explicit typed marker.
\end{itemize}


\subsubsection*{Stepwise refinement of the proof}

Three rounds of top-down refinement decompose the assembly
lemma above into named sub-leaves.  Each leaf carries a Lean
declaration (or a Mathlib reference) and is marked
\textsf{leanok} when the Lean stub exists, \textsf{notready}
when the statement is still a forward declaration, or
\textsf{mathlibok} when it reduces to a Mathlib theorem.

\begin{lemma}[Serre step 1: trace + cup-product pairing]
\label{lem:serre-pairing-construction}
\uses{lem:serre-trace-iso,lem:serre-cech-cup-product}
On a compact Riemann surface, the cup-product / trace pairing $H^{q}(X, F) \times H^{1-q}(X, \mathcal{H}om(F, K_{X})) \to H^{1}(X, K_{X}) \xrightarrow{\mathrm{tr}} \C$ is well-defined.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SerreDuality.serre_pairing_construction}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Trace map: $H^{1}(X, K_{X}) \cong \C$ via residues]
\label{lem:serre-trace-iso}
\uses{lem:sti-r1}
Aggregation of point residues into a Cech cohomology class gives an iso $H^{1}(X, K_{X}) \cong \C$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SerreDuality.serre_trace_iso}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Cup product on Cech cohomology]
\label{lem:serre-cech-cup-product}
\uses{lem:scc-r1}
The cup-product pairing $H^{q}(X, F) \otimes H^{1-q}(X, F^{\vee} \otimes K_{X}) \to H^{1}(X, K_{X})$ is well-defined.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SerreDuality.serre_cup_product_def}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Serre step 2: non-degeneracy via $L^{2}$ harmonic pairing]
\label{lem:serre-pairing-nondegenerate}
\uses{input:hodge-decomposition,input:dolbeault,lem:serre-l2-realisation,lem:serre-residue-theorem}
Identifying both sides of the pairing with harmonic-form spaces (R5 + R7), the pairing realises the $L^{2}$ inner product, which is positive-definite hence non-degenerate.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SerreDuality.serre_pairing_via_hodge}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Harmonic representatives realise the pairing]
\label{lem:serre-l2-realisation}
\uses{lem:sl2-r1}
Replacing both arguments by their harmonic representatives turns the cup product into the $L^{2}$ inner product on $\mathcal{H}^{p,q}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SerreDuality.serre_subgap_l2_realisation}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Residue theorem (sum of residues equals zero)]
\label{lem:serre-residue-theorem}
\uses{lem:srt-r1-stokes-cut-disks}
On a compact Riemann surface the sum of residues of a global meromorphic 1-form is zero --- the well-definedness lemma for the trace map.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SerreDuality.serre_subgap_residue_theorem}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{layman}
Serre duality is a magical identity in complex algebraic geometry.
On a compact Riemann surface, the first sheaf cohomology of the
structure sheaf, \(H^1(X, \mathcal{O}_X)\), is the dual vector
space to the global sections of the canonical bundle,
\(H^0(X, K_X) = \) holomorphic 1-forms.  Dual: not just isomorphic
in dimension, but explicitly paired by an integration identity on
\(X\).

In particular: \(\dim H^1(X, \mathcal{O}_X) = \dim H^0(X, K_X) = g\)
--- the genus.  This is the key ingredient in Riemann--Roch (which
otherwise has only the inequality \(h^0 - h^1 \geq d - g + 1\); Serre
upgrades it to an equality).  It's also what lets us identify the
analytic Jacobian (\(H^0(X, \Omega^1)^\vee / H_1(X, \Z)\)) with the
algebraic Jacobian (\(\mathrm{Pic}^0(X)\)) --- the deepest cross-bridge
in the project.

The proof has four moving parts.  First, define a trace map from the
top sheaf cohomology to \(\C\), via residues on a Cech cover.
Second, define a cup-product pairing using the cup product on Cech
cohomology and the natural evaluation map on sheaves.  Third,
identify both sides of the pairing with harmonic-form spaces using
R5 + R7.  Fourth, observe that the pairing realises the
\(L^2\) inner product on harmonic forms, which is positive-definite
hence non-degenerate.

R8 is the most-developed Lean gap of the eight: ~32 files already
sketch the proof tree.  But many leaves remain sorry, and several
(the \(L^2\)-bridge to R5 + R7, the residue theorem) are themselves
non-trivial sub-gaps.  Total estimated for R8 alone: ~3000 LOC
modulo R5 + R7.  The dependency on R5 is what makes R8 expensive ---
R8 doesn't need full Hodge decomposition, but it does need the
\(L^2\)-pairing-positive-definiteness ingredient that comes from the
Hodge package.
\end{layman}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R9 --- Bundled differential forms \(\Omega^{k}(M)\)}
\label{subsec:gap-R9-bundled-forms}

The headline says: for every smooth manifold \(M\) modelled on a real
Banach space and every \(k \in \N\), there is a bundled \(\R\)-vector
space \(\Omega^{k}(M)\) of smooth \(k\)-forms, equipped with the
exterior derivative \(d\), wedge product \(\wedge\), pullback \(f^*\),
and integration \(\int_M\), all simultaneously linear and natural and
satisfying the standard identities \(d^{2}=0\), Leibniz, \(f^{*} \circ
d = d \circ f^{*}\), and Stokes for closed manifolds.

R9 is the \emph{single foundational sub-gap shared} by R4 (de Rham),
R5 (Hodge decomposition), and R7 (Dolbeault).  It is promoted from
``R4-sub-A'' in the previous round to its own top-level dep-graph node
so that downstream consumers can depend on a single, named
bundled-form package.

\subsubsection*{Classical content}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{\(\Omega^{k}(M)\) algebra.}  \(\Omega^{k}\) is a
  \(C^{\infty}(M, \R)\)-module; \(\Omega^{0} = C^{\infty}(M, \R)\).
\item \emph{Exterior derivative.}  \(d : \Omega^{k} \to \Omega^{k+1}\)
  \(\R\)-linear, \(d^{2} = 0\), commutes with pullback.
\item \emph{Wedge product.}  \(\wedge : \Omega^{p} \times \Omega^{q}
  \to \Omega^{p+q}\), graded commutative
  (\(\alpha \wedge \beta = (-1)^{pq} \beta \wedge \alpha\)) and Leibniz
  (\(d(\alpha \wedge \beta) = d\alpha \wedge \beta + (-1)^{p}
  \alpha \wedge d\beta\)).
\item \emph{Pullback.}  \(f^{*} : \Omega^{k}(N) \to \Omega^{k}(M)\)
  \(\R\)-linear, functorial, compatible with \(d\) and \(\wedge\).
\item \emph{Integration.}  \(\int_{M} : \Omega^{n}(M) \to \R\) for
  compact oriented \(n\)-manifolds; Stokes \(\int_{M} d\omega = 0\) on
  closed manifolds.
\end{enumerate}

Plus the \emph{bigraded variant} for complex manifolds:
\(\Omega^{k}(X) = \bigoplus_{p+q=k} \Omega^{p,q}(X)\) and
\(d = \partial + \bar\partial\) (the prerequisite for R7).

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

15 sub-leaves under
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.BundledForms.Overview}.  Mathlib v4.28.0 has
the underlying machinery --- manifold derivative (\code{MFDeriv}),
alternating multilinear maps, partitions of unity --- but \emph{not} the
integrated bundled-form package.  Estimated 400--600 LOC for a complete
API.

\subsubsection*{Recursive sub-gaps surfaced}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{R9-sub-A.}  Bundled cotangent bundle infrastructure on a
  manifold.  Mathlib has \code{TangentBundle}; the alternating-form
  package on \(T^{*}M\) is missing.
\item \textbf{R9-sub-B.}  Smooth-section infrastructure for a vector
  bundle.  \code{Mathlib.Geometry.Manifold.VectorBundle.SmoothSection}
  exists; the alternating-form variant is not yet packaged.
\item \textbf{R9-sub-C.}  Chart-local description: in a chart,
  \(\Omega^{k}(M)\) restricts to alternating \(k\)-multilinear maps on
  \(\R^{n}\), with \(d\) given by partial derivatives.
\end{itemize}

\begin{theorem}[Classical input: bundled differential forms $\Omega^{k}(M)$]
\label{input:bundled-omega-k}
\uses{lem:bundled-forms-algebra,lem:bundled-forms-operations,input:cotangent-alternating-bundle}
The Lean target
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.BundledForms.bundled\_forms\_overview} states
the existence of an \(\R\)-vector space \(\Omega^{k}(M)\) with the
operations \(d\), \(\wedge\), pullback, and integration, all
simultaneously linear and natural, with sub-leaves R9.1.1--R9.6.2
tracked in \code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/Overview.lean}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.bundled_forms_overview}
\leanok
\end{theorem}


\subsubsection*{Stepwise refinement of the proof}

Three rounds of top-down refinement decompose the assembly
lemma above into named sub-leaves.  Each leaf carries a Lean
declaration (or a Mathlib reference) and is marked
\textsf{leanok} when the Lean stub exists, \textsf{notready}
when the statement is still a forward declaration, or
\textsf{mathlibok} when it reduces to a Mathlib theorem.

\begin{lemma}[Bundled forms step 1: $\Omega^{k}(M)$ algebra]
\label{lem:bundled-forms-algebra}
\uses{lem:bfa-r1}
$\Omega^{k}(M)$ is an $\R$-vector space and a $C^{\infty}(M, \R)$-module.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.bundled_forms_algebra}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Bundled forms step 2: $d, \wedge$ \(\R\)-linear with the standard identities]
\label{lem:bundled-forms-operations}
\uses{lem:bundled-forms-d-sq-zero,lem:bundled-forms-pullback-compat}
The exterior derivative $d : \Omega^{k} \to \Omega^{k+1}$ and wedge product $\wedge : \Omega^{p} \otimes \Omega^{q} \to \Omega^{p+q}$ exist as $\R$-linear / bilinear maps with $d^{2} = 0$, graded commutativity, and the Leibniz rule.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.bundled_forms_operations}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[$d^{2} = 0$]
\label{lem:bundled-forms-d-sq-zero}
\uses{lem:bfd-r1}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.bundled_forms_d_sq_zero}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pullback by smooth maps commutes with $d$]
\label{lem:bundled-forms-pullback-compat}
\uses{lem:bfp-r1}
$f^{*} \circ d = d \circ f^{*}$ for every smooth map $f : M \to N$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.bundled_forms_pullback_compat}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{layman}
The simplest object in differential geometry is the smooth function
on a manifold.  One step up: a smooth 1-form, which at each point
pairs against tangent vectors to give a number.  Higher \(k\) packs
alternating-multilinear data.  The whole tower
\(\Omega^{0} \to \Omega^{1} \to \Omega^{2} \to \cdots\) carries the
exterior derivative \(d\), the wedge product \(\wedge\), pullback by
smooth maps, and (in top degree on a compact oriented manifold)
integration.  These four operations interact via the standard
identities \(d^{2}=0\), Leibniz, naturality, and Stokes that make
differential forms the universal language of integration on
manifolds.

Mathlib has the underlying machinery --- manifold derivative,
alternating multilinear maps, partition-of-unity --- but not the
integrated bundled-form package.  R9 is what you need to state
precisely ``the de Rham complex of \(M\),'' ``the exterior algebra
of \(M\),'' ``Stokes' formula on \(M\).''  Without R9, every theorem
about forms on a manifold has to talk around the missing object.
About 400--600 LOC for a complete API; \emph{foundational for R4, R5,
and R7 simultaneously}, which is why it gets its own node.
\end{layman}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R10 --- Sobolev / elliptic regularity}
\label{subsec:gap-R10-sobolev-elliptic}

The headline says: for a compact oriented Riemannian manifold \(M\)
and \(k : \N\), the Sobolev space \(H^{s}(\Omega^{k}(M))\) is
well-defined for every \(s : \R\), and the Laplace--Beltrami operator
\(\Delta : H^{s+2}(\Omega^{k}) \to H^{s}(\Omega^{k})\) is
\emph{Fredholm}.  Furthermore every distributional solution of
\(\Delta\omega = f\) with smooth \(f\) is itself smooth (elliptic
regularity).

R10 is the \emph{single largest sub-gap} in the entire eight-node
tree --- estimated 2500--4000 LOC.  It underpins R5 (Hodge decomposition)
and indirectly R7 (Dolbeault) and R8 (Serre duality via the
\(L^{2}\)-pairing realised by harmonic representatives).  Promoted
from ``R5-sub-B'' in the previous round to its own top-level
dep-graph node because it is both shared and substantial.

\subsubsection*{Classical content}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Sobolev framework.}  Define \(H^{s}(\Omega^{k}(M))\) for
  \(s : \R\) using a partition of unity and chart-local Sobolev norms
  on \(\R^{n}\).  Density of smooth forms; Sobolev embedding
  \(H^{s} \hookrightarrow C^{0}\) for \(s > n/2\).
\item \emph{Ellipticity of \(\Delta\).}  Principal symbol
  \(\sigma_{\Delta}(\xi) = |\xi|^{2} \cdot \mathrm{id}\), invertible
  for \(\xi \neq 0\).
\item \emph{Elliptic regularity.}  Garding inequality:
  \(\|\omega\|_{s+2} \leq C(\|\Delta\omega\|_{s} + \|\omega\|_{s})\).
  Smooth forms remain smooth after applying \(\Delta\).
\item \emph{Rellich--Kondrachov.}  On a compact manifold,
  \(H^{s'} \hookrightarrow H^{s}\) is compact for \(s' > s\).
\item \emph{Fredholm.}  Combining 3 + 4:
  \(\Delta : H^{s+2}(\Omega^{k}) \to H^{s}(\Omega^{k})\) is Fredholm.
  Hence the Hodge orthogonal decomposition
  \(\Omega^{k}(M) = \mathcal{H}^{k}(M) \oplus d(\Omega^{k-1}) \oplus
  \delta(\Omega^{k+1})\), with \(\mathcal{H}^{k}\) finite-dimensional.
\item \emph{Bochner / K\"ahler identities.}  On a K\"ahler manifold the
  Laplacians for \(d\), \(\partial\), \(\bar\partial\) are
  proportional, refining R10 into the R5 bigrading.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

15 sub-leaves under
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.Overview}, in six phases.
Mathlib v4.28.0 has Sobolev spaces on \(\R^{n}\)
(\code{Mathlib.Analysis.Distribution.SchwartzSpace}) and the basic
Cauchy--Schwarz / Bessel apparatus, but \emph{no manifold-level
Sobolev theory} and \emph{no elliptic regularity for second-order
operators} on a manifold.  Building this from scratch is a major
undertaking --- comparable in scope to formalising the basics of
Riemannian geometry.

\subsubsection*{Recursive sub-gaps surfaced}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{R10-sub-A.}  Distribution theory on a smooth manifold
  (the foundation of Sobolev spaces).  ~600 LOC.
\item \textbf{R10-sub-B.}  The \(H^{s}\)-norm on \(\Omega^{k}(M)\):
  chart-local construction + partition of unity.  ~500 LOC.
\item \textbf{R10-sub-C.}  Garding inequality (Phase 3 prerequisite).
  ~300 LOC.
\item \textbf{R10-sub-D.}  Rellich--Kondrachov compactness theorem.
  ~400 LOC.
\item \textbf{R10-sub-E.}  Fredholm-alternative theorem on a compact
  manifold.  ~300 LOC.
\end{itemize}

\begin{theorem}[Classical input: Sobolev spaces and elliptic regularity for $\Delta$]
\label{input:sobolev-elliptic-regularity}
\uses{lem:sobolev-elliptic-kernel-finite-dim,lem:sobolev-fredholm-property,lem:real-harmonic-def,lem:abstract-resolvent-self-adjoint,lem:has-laplace-resolvent-finiteDim,lem:model-symbol-isElliptic,lem:smoothfun-def,lem:l2fun-def,lem:hodge-harmonic-finite-dim-substantive,lem:dolbeault-harmonic-finite-dim-substantive,lem:serre-harmonic-finite-dim-substantive}
The Lean target
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.sobolev\_elliptic\_overview}
states the Fredholm property of the Laplacian on a compact Riemannian
manifold; sub-leaves R10.1.1--R10.6.1 are tracked in
\code{Jacobian/Analysis/SobolevElliptic/Overview.lean}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.sobolev_elliptic_overview}
\leanok
\end{theorem}


\subsubsection*{Stepwise refinement of the proof}

Three rounds of top-down refinement decompose the assembly
lemma above into named sub-leaves.  Each leaf carries a Lean
declaration (or a Mathlib reference) and is marked
\textsf{leanok} when the Lean stub exists, \textsf{notready}
when the statement is still a forward declaration, or
\textsf{mathlibok} when it reduces to a Mathlib theorem.

\begin{lemma}[Sobolev step 1: ellipticity + finite-dim kernel]
\label{lem:sobolev-elliptic-kernel-finite-dim}
\uses{lem:sobolev-laplacian-elliptic,lem:sobolev-garding,lem:sobolev-rellich-kondrachov}
For a compact oriented Riemannian manifold, the Laplace--Beltrami operator $\Delta$ is elliptic and has finite-dimensional kernel.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.sobolev_elliptic_kernel_finite_dim}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[$\Delta$ is elliptic]
\label{lem:sobolev-laplacian-elliptic}
\uses{lem:sle-r1}
The Lean stub \code{sobolev\_laplacian\_elliptic} in
\code{Overview.lean} is a typed placeholder
(\code{IsElliptic := True}); the \emph{model-space} fibre witness
(see Round~3, \ref{subsubsec:sle-round-3}, sle.r11--sle.r15) is
discharged in \code{Jacobian/Analysis/SobolevElliptic/ModelSymbol.lean}
as \code{Model.principalSymbol\_isElliptic}, with no \code{sorry} and
no placeholder, against unmodified Mathlib v4.28.0.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.sobolev_laplacian_elliptic}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Garding inequality]
\label{lem:sobolev-garding}
\uses{lem:sgd-r1}
$\|\omega\|_{s+2} \leq C(\|T\omega\|_{s} + \|\omega\|_{s})$ for elliptic $T$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.sobolev_garding}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Rellich--Kondrachov compactness]
\label{lem:sobolev-rellich-kondrachov}
\uses{lem:rk-r1-partition-localize}
$H^{s'} \hookrightarrow H^{s}$ is compact for $s' > s$ on a compact manifold.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.sobolev_rellich_kondrachov}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Sobolev step 2: Fredholm property of $\Delta$]
\label{lem:sobolev-fredholm-property}
\uses{lem:sobolev-elliptic-kernel-finite-dim,lem:sobolev-rellich-kondrachov}
From step 1 + Rellich--Kondrachov, $\Delta : H^{s+2}(\Omega^{k}) \to H^{s}(\Omega^{k})$ is Fredholm.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.sobolev_fredholm_property}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% ----- Substantive companions (Phase 1--4 dispatch) -----

\begin{lemma}[Substantive headline: $\ker \Delta$ finite-dim via spectral shortcut]
\label{lem:sobolev-elliptic-overview-substantive}
\uses{lem:abstract-resolvent-eigenspace-finite-dim,lem:has-laplace-resolvent-class}
Substantive replacement for \ref{lem:sobolev-elliptic-kernel-finite-dim}: given a
\code{HasLaplaceResolvent} $M$ $\mu$ analytic input (a Hilbert space
\code{Sobolev} with a compact embedding into $L^{2}(M, \mu)$), the
spectral substitute \code{RealHarmonic} $M$ $\mu$ is
finite-dimensional.  Discharged against unmodified Mathlib v4.28.0
through the abstract-resolvent chain
(\ref{lem:abstract-resolvent-self-adjoint},
\ref{lem:abstract-resolvent-compact},
\ref{lem:abstract-resolvent-eigenspace-finite-dim}).  No
\code{sorry}, no \code{True}-valued bodies.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.moduleFinite_realHarmonic}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Phase 4 typeclass: \code{HasLaplaceResolvent}]
\label{lem:has-laplace-resolvent-class}
The irreducible analytic input remaining after Phases~1--3:
a Hilbert space \code{Sobolev} with a continuous embedding into
$L^{2}(M, \mu)$ that is moreover compact (Rellich--Kondrachov on a
compact manifold).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.HasLaplaceResolvent}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Phase 4 spectral substitute: \code{RealHarmonic}]
\label{lem:real-harmonic-def}
\uses{lem:has-laplace-resolvent-class}
Eigenspace at $1$ of the abstract resolvent
$T := i \circ i^{\dagger} : L^{2}(M, \mu) \to L^{2}(M, \mu)$.
The substantive replacement for the project's placeholder
\code{Harmonic} (which is \code{LinearMap.ker 0} over
\code{Omega M k = PUnit}, vacuously finite).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.RealHarmonic}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Phase 3.1 abstract resolvent: $T = i \circ i^{\dagger}$ is self-adjoint]
\label{lem:abstract-resolvent-self-adjoint}
For real Hilbert spaces $V, H$ and a continuous linear map
$i : V \to_{L[\R]} H$, the operator
$T := i \circ i^{\dagger} : H \to_{L[\R]} H$ is self-adjoint.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.isSelfAdjoint_resolventOfEmbedding}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Phase 3.1 abstract resolvent: $T$ is compact when $i$ is compact]
\label{lem:abstract-resolvent-compact}
Same setup; if $i$ is compact then so is $T$.  Proof: composition
of compact with continuous (\code{IsCompactOperator.comp\_clm}).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.isCompactOperator_resolventOfEmbedding}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Phase 2.2 abstract Fredholm: compact $T$ + $\lambda \neq 0$ $\Rightarrow$ eigenspace finite-dim]
\label{lem:abstract-resolvent-eigenspace-finite-dim}
\uses{lem:abstract-resolvent-compact}
Riesz-style argument: closed unit ball of the eigenspace sits
inside the precompact image $T(B_{H})$ scaled by $\lambda^{-1}$;
intersect with the closed eigenspace; conclude compact, then
finite-dim by
\code{FiniteDimensional.of\_isCompact\_closedBall\textsubscript{0}}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.finiteDimensional_eigenspace_of_compact}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Phase 4 realizability: trivial witness for finite-dim $L^{2}$]
\label{lem:has-laplace-resolvent-finiteDim}
\uses{lem:has-laplace-resolvent-class}
When $L^{2}(M, \mu)$ is finite-dimensional, the identity embedding
is compact (Riesz, via \code{FiniteDimensional.proper}), so
\code{HasLaplaceResolvent M $\mu$} is automatic.  Proves the
framework is non-vacuously realizable.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.hasLaplaceResolvent_of_finiteDim}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Stepwise refinement of the manifold-$H^{1}$ realisability witness}
\label{subsubsec:manifold-H1-realisability}

The trivial witness above suffices to ship the headline against unmodified
Mathlib v4.28.0, but the \emph{substantive} realisability witness ---
construction of \(H^{1}(M)\) from chart-local distributional derivatives,
plus Rellich--Kondrachov compactness, plus the spectral correspondence
\(T f = f \Leftrightarrow \Delta f = 0\) --- remains the single largest
classical-analysis gap in the entire blueprint. All three ingredients
are ABSENT in Mathlib v4.28.0.

\code{Jacobian/Analysis/SobolevElliptic/RealizabilityWitnessManifold.lean}
gives the sorry-free twenty-pass ledger for this construction:

\begin{itemize}
\item \emph{Passes 1--4.} Chart-local \(H^{1}\)-seminorm on
  \(C^{n}_{c}(U)\) for \(U \subset \R^{d}\), with non-negativity,
  scalar homogeneity, and triangle inequality.
\item \emph{Passes 5--8.} Partition-of-unity assembly: finite open cover
  on a compact \(M\), POU subordinate to charts, global \(H^{1}\)
  seminorm, cover-independence, global seminorm property.
\item \emph{Passes 9--12.} Hilbert structure on \(H^{1}(M)\): quotient by
  the seminorm null space, completion, inner product, Hilbert
  packaging.
\item \emph{Passes 13--15.} Continuous linear embedding
  \(H^{1}(M) \hookrightarrow L^{2}(M, \mu)\): chart-local embedding,
  POU extension, \texttt{ContinuousLinearMap} packaging.
\item \emph{Passes 16--18.} Rellich--Kondrachov: chart-local Euclidean
  compactness, manifold-side assembly via finite POU, embedding
  compactness conclusion.
\item \emph{Passes 19--20.} Spectral correspondence
  \(T f = f \Leftrightarrow \Delta f = 0\) and the manifold realisability
  witness, packaged as a \texttt{Prop}-marker conjunction.
\end{itemize}

The ledger pins every sub-leaf as a sorry-free Lean handle so that the
manifold-\(H^{1}\) project (estimated 2500--4000 LOC across distribution
theory, Sobolev spaces on manifolds, Rellich--Kondrachov, and
spectral correspondence) has a stable downstream consumer
in \texttt{HasLaplaceResolvent}.

\begin{lemma}[Chain K2 model-space dispatch: principal symbol invertible]
\label{lem:model-symbol-isElliptic}
The principal symbol $\sigma_{\Delta}(\xi) = -\langle \xi, \xi \rangle_{\R}$ of
the scalar Laplacian on a real inner-product space $E$ is
invertible (a unit in $\R$) for every nonzero covector $\xi$.
Dispatched fully against Mathlib via \code{real\_inner\_self\_pos}
+ \code{isUnit\_iff\_ne\_zero}; see
\ref{subsubsec:sle-round-3} for the per-pass refinement.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SobolevElliptic.Model.principalSymbol_isElliptic}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% ----- Phase 1 substrate: real L^2(M, mu) -----

\begin{lemma}[Phase 1 substrate: \code{SmoothFun M}]
\label{lem:smoothfun-def}
The $\R$-vector space of $C^{\infty}$ real-valued functions on $M$,
wrapping Mathlib's \code{ContMDiffMap} with the algebra
instances from
\code{Mathlib/Geometry/Manifold/Algebra/SmoothFunctions.lean}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SmoothFun}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Phase 1 substrate: \code{IsManifoldMeasure}]
\label{lem:is-manifold-measure-class}
A finite Borel measure on a manifold $M$, taken as data via a
typeclass.  Deliberate cheap shortcut bypassing the absent manifold
volume form.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.IsManifoldMeasure}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Phase 1 substrate: \code{L2Fun M $\mu$}]
\label{lem:l2fun-def}
\uses{lem:is-manifold-measure-class}
The Hilbert space $L^{2}(M, \mu)$ via
\code{MeasureTheory.Lp $\R$ 2 $\mu$}, with re-derived
\code{InnerProductSpace $\R$} and \code{CompleteSpace} instances.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.L2Fun}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% ----- Downstream consumption (R5/R7/R8 substantive companions) -----

\begin{lemma}[R5 substantive consumption: harmonic forms finite-dim via R10]
\label{lem:hodge-harmonic-finite-dim-substantive}
\uses{lem:sobolev-elliptic-overview-substantive}
The R5 finite-dim conclusion routed through the R10 abstract
resolvent chain.  Companion to \ref{lem:hodge-laplacian-kernel-finite-dim}
that takes \code{[HasLaplaceResolvent N $\mu$]} as a typeclass
hypothesis.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.HodgeDecomposition.hodge_harmonic_forms_finite_dim_substantive}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R7 substantive consumption: Dolbeault harmonic finite-dim via R10]
\label{lem:dolbeault-harmonic-finite-dim-substantive}
\uses{lem:sobolev-elliptic-overview-substantive}
Same pattern for Dolbeault: harmonic forms in the
$\partial$-$\bar\partial$ bigrading inherit finite-dimensionality
from \code{HasLaplaceResolvent}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.Dolbeault.dolbeault_harmonic_forms_finite_dim_substantive}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8 substantive consumption: Serre duality harmonic input]
\label{lem:serre-harmonic-finite-dim-substantive}
\uses{lem:sobolev-elliptic-overview-substantive}
Harmonic-form finite-dim input to Serre duality on a compact
Riemann surface: $H^{1}(X, \mathcal{O}_{X})$ finite-dim once
\code{HasLaplaceResolvent} supplies the analytic data.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.SerreDuality.serre_duality_harmonic_finite_dim_substantive}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{layman}
When you ask ``does the equation \(\Delta\omega = f\) have a solution''
on a compact manifold, you face a problem: smooth forms are not
enough --- the abstract solution operator (the inverse of \(\Delta\)
modulo its kernel) doesn't act on smooth forms in a closed way.  The
standard trick is to enlarge the space: replace \(\Omega^{k}(M)\) with
the Sobolev space \(H^{s}(\Omega^{k}(M))\), where \(s\) measures the
number of weak derivatives you allow.  In the larger space, \(\Delta :
H^{s+2} \to H^{s}\) becomes a Fredholm operator --- its kernel and
cokernel are finite-dimensional, its range is closed --- which is
exactly what you need to invert it on the orthogonal complement of the
kernel.

The deep result is \emph{elliptic regularity}: even though you allowed
yourself to enlarge the space, the actual solutions of \(\Delta\omega
= f\) for smooth \(f\) end up being smooth themselves.  So at the end
of the day you can think of \(\Delta\) as a Fredholm operator on
smooth forms, with a finite-dimensional kernel (the harmonic forms)
and a smooth inverse (the \emph{Green operator}) on the orthogonal
complement.  This is what powers Hodge decomposition (R5), and through
R5 the analytic-genus-equals-topological-genus identity (R6), and
through harmonic-form representatives the non-degeneracy of the Serre
pairing (R8).

Mathlib has Sobolev spaces on \(\R^{n}\) and Schwartz distributions,
but no manifold-level Sobolev theory and no elliptic regularity for
second-order operators on a manifold.  Building this from scratch is
the single largest budget item in the entire eight-gap tree ---
estimated 2500--4000 LOC for the headline package, plus 2000--3000 LOC
for prerequisites.  It also has the deepest character: this is real
hard analysis, not algebraic topology bookkeeping.
\end{layman}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R10 Phases 1--4 dispatch (M1--M4 milestones)}
\label{subsec:r10-phase-dispatch}

This subsection summarises the actual Lean dispatch of R10 against
unmodified Mathlib v4.28.0, following the plan in
\code{/root/.claude/plans/okay-let-s-plan-out-shimmering-hearth.md}.
The key pivot is the \emph{spike-solution route}: we bypass the
classical manifold-Sobolev / Garding / Rellich infrastructure
(estimated 6--8k LOC, genuinely upstream-Mathlib material) and
route the headline finite-dim-kernel claim through compactness of
$(\Delta+1)^{-1}$ on $L^2(M)$ plus the abstract spectral theorem
``compact $\Rightarrow$ each non-zero eigenvalue has finite-dim
eigenspace''.

\paragraph{Milestone summary.}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{M0 (chain K2 dispatch).}  The principal symbol of the
  scalar Laplacian on a real inner-product space $E$ is invertible
  for every nonzero covector.  Dispatched at the model-space level
  in \code{Jacobian/Analysis/SobolevElliptic/ModelSymbol.lean}
  (\textsf{leanok}, no \code{sorry}, no \code{True}-valued bodies;
  $\sim 180$ LOC against Mathlib).  Fully closes Round~3 of chain
  \texttt{sle} (\ref{subsubsec:sle-round-3}).

\item \textbf{M1 (real $L^2$ substrate).}  Real Hilbert space
  $L^2(M, \mu)$ on a compact manifold $M$ with a finite Borel
  measure $\mu$.  Files
  \code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/\{SmoothFun, Omega0, L2Norm,
  L2Completion\}.lean} ($\sim 600$ LOC).  Wraps Mathlib
  \code{ContMDiffMap}, \code{MeasureTheory.Lp}, plus the
  project-side typeclass \code{IsManifoldMeasure} that takes $\mu$
  as data (deliberate cheap shortcut bypassing the absent manifold
  volume form).

\item \textbf{M2 (Riemannian metric + abstract spectral output).}
  \code{Jacobian/StageB/RiemannianMetricBundled.lean} wraps Mathlib's
  \code{Bundle.Riemannian} on the tangent bundle, providing a real
  metric typeclass to replace the previous \code{metric\_data : True}
  placeholder.
  \code{Jacobian/Analysis/SobolevElliptic/AbstractFredholmResolvent.lean}
  proves the irreducible spectral consequence: for any compact
  operator $T : H \to L[\R] H$ and any nonzero $\lambda$, the
  eigenspace $\ker(T - \lambda \cdot 1)$ is finite-dimensional.
  $\sim 290$ LOC total, no \code{sorry}.

\item \textbf{M3 (abstract resolvent).}  Given two real Hilbert
  spaces $V, H$ and a continuous linear embedding $i : V \to L[\R] H$
  (the abstract ``$H^1 \hookrightarrow L^2$'' map), the resolvent
  $T := i \circ i^\dagger : H \to L[\R] H$ is automatically
  bounded, self-adjoint, and non-negative; if $i$ is compact, so is
  $T$.  Combined with M2's spectral output, this gives finite-dim
  eigenspaces.  File:
  \code{Jacobian/Analysis/SobolevElliptic/AbstractResolvent.lean}
  ($\sim 150$ LOC).  Mathlib hooks: \code{ContinuousLinearMap.adjoint},
  \code{IsCompactOperator.comp\_clm}.

\item \textbf{M4 (headline plug-in).}  The typeclass
  \code{HasLaplaceResolvent M} $\mu$ packages exactly the
  irreducible analytic input remaining after M0--M3: a Hilbert
  space \code{Sobolev} (think $H^1(M)$), a continuous embedding
  into $L^2(M, \mu)$, plus an \code{IsCompactOperator} witness
  (Rellich--Kondrachov on a compact manifold).  Given this single
  typeclass instance, the substantive R10 headline
  $\code{Module.Finite } \R \, (\code{RealHarmonic } M \, \mu)$
  is automatic, with no further analytic input.  File:
  \code{Jacobian/Analysis/SobolevElliptic/HeadlinePlugIn.lean}
  ($\sim 150$ LOC).  Companion theorem
  \code{sobolev\_elliptic\_overview\_substantive} sits next to the
  placeholder \code{sobolev\_elliptic\_overview} in
  \code{Overview.lean}; downstream R5/R7/R8 consume it via parallel
  companions \code{hodge\_harmonic\_forms\_finite\_dim\_substantive},
  \code{dolbeault\_harmonic\_forms\_finite\_dim\_substantive},
  \code{serre\_duality\_harmonic\_finite\_dim\_substantive}.

\item \textbf{Realizability.}  A trivial-but-substantive witness
  for \code{HasLaplaceResolvent} is supplied in
  \code{Jacobian/Analysis/SobolevElliptic/RealizabilityWitness.lean}:
  whenever $L^2(M, \mu)$ is finite-dimensional, the identity
  embedding is compact (Riesz), and the typeclass is automatic.
  This proves the framework is non-vacuously realizable.
\end{itemize}

\paragraph{Residual analytic gap.}  The spectral-output side of R10
is now fully discharged.  What remains is supplying a
\emph{non-trivial} \code{HasLaplaceResolvent} instance for an
infinite-dimensional $L^2(M, \mu)$:
\begin{itemize}
\item construct the Hilbert space $H^1(M)$ (manifold Sobolev,
  R10-sub-A,B);
\item prove the embedding $H^1(M) \hookrightarrow L^2(M)$ is
  compact (Rellich--Kondrachov on a compact manifold);
\item link the resolvent's eigenspace at $1$ to a classical
  $\ker \Delta$ on smooth forms (spectral correspondence).
\end{itemize}
All three are flagged \emph{ABSENT} in Mathlib v4.28.0.  Any future
work on these pieces plugs into the existing framework with no
further changes to the spectral-output side.

\paragraph{Downstream consumption.}  R5 (Hodge decomposition), R7
(Dolbeault), R8 (Serre duality) each carry a substantive companion
that takes \code{[HasLaplaceResolvent M $\mu$]} as a typeclass
hypothesis and produces \code{Module.Finite ${\R}$ (RealHarmonic M $\mu$)}.
The downstream period-lattice / Jacobian construction can therefore
proceed conditionally on a single typeclass instance, isolating the
remaining classical-analysis work behind one named obligation.

%======================================================================
\subsection{R9-sub-A --- Bundled cotangent bundle and alternating-form bundle}
\label{subsec:gap-R9subA-cotangent-alternating-bundle}

The headline says: for every smooth manifold \(M\) modelled on a
real Banach space \(E\) and every \(k\in\N\), the alternating
exterior-power bundle \(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\to M\) exists as a smooth
vector bundle.  In particular, the cotangent bundle
\(T^{*}M\to M\) (the case \(k=1\)) is a smooth real vector bundle,
and the smooth sections \(\Gamma^{\infty}(M,\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M)\) are
exactly the differential \(k\)-forms \(\Omega^{k}(M)\) of R9.

This sub-gap is the foundational dependency on which the entire
J1 (\(\Omega^{k}(M)\) algebra), J2 ($d^{2}=0$), and J3 (pullback
naturality) chains rest: every J1-r1\ldots r4 leaf, every
J3-r1\ldots r5 leaf, and the chart-local description of higher-\(k\)
forms in J2-r6\ldots r7 reduce, after their own informal-proof
expansion, to either the existence of \(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\) as a
smooth bundle or the smooth-section module structure on it.

\subsubsection*{Classical content}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Cotangent bundle.}  For a smooth manifold \(M\) with
  tangent bundle \(\pi:TM\to M\), the cotangent bundle is the dual
  bundle \(T^{*}M\) whose fibre at \(p\) is
  \((T_{p}M)^{*}=\operatorname{Hom}_{\R}(T_{p}M,\R)\).  Charts on \(M\) induce
  trivialisations \(T^{*}U\cong U\times E^{*}\); transition functions
  on overlaps are \((Df_{i\to j})^{-T}\), the inverse transpose of
  the tangent transition.
\item \emph{Exterior power bundle.}  \(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\) has fibre
  \(\Lambda^{k}(T_{p}M)^{*}\), the \(k\)-th alternating power of the
  cotangent space.  Locally trivialised over the same atlas as
  \(T^{*}M\) with transition functions \(\Lambda^{k}\) of the
  cotangent transitions, which are smooth because \(\Lambda^{k}\) is
  a smooth functor.
\item \emph{Smooth sections.}  A smooth section of
  \(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\) is a smooth map \(s:M\to\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\)
  with \(\pi\circ s=\mathrm{id}_{M}\); equivalently, a chart-local
  description in each \(U_{i}\) is a smooth map
  \(s_{i}:U_{i}\to\Lambda^{k}E^{*}\) compatible with the cocycle.
  \(\Gamma^{\infty}(M,\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M)\) is naturally a
  \(C^{\infty}(M,\R)\)-module by pointwise scalar multiplication.
\item \emph{Identification with \(\Omega^{k}(M)\).}  The
  bundled-form package R9 is exactly
  \(\Omega^{k}(M)=\Gamma^{\infty}(M,\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M)\); the \(d\),
  \(\wedge\), and pullback operations of R9 lift to the section
  level via the corresponding bundle morphisms.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

Mathlib v4.28.0 has:
\begin{itemize}
\item \code{Mathlib.Geometry.Manifold.VectorBundle.Tangent} --- the
  tangent bundle \(TM\) as a smooth vector bundle.
\item \code{Mathlib.Geometry.Manifold.VectorBundle.SmoothSection} ---
  smooth sections of an arbitrary smooth vector bundle, with
  \(C^{\infty}(M)\)-module structure.
\item \code{Mathlib.LinearAlgebra.ExteriorAlgebra.Basic} and
  \code{Mathlib.LinearAlgebra.Alternating.Basic} --- alternating
  multilinear maps on a single vector space.
\end{itemize}
Mathlib does \emph{not} have:
\begin{itemize}
\item The cotangent bundle as a packaged smooth vector bundle
  (the dual of \code{TangentBundle} is not provided as a
  \code{VectorBundle}).
\item The exterior-power functor on smooth vector bundles, i.e.
  promoting a fibrewise \(\Lambda^{k}\) to a smooth vector bundle.
\item The identification
  \(\Omega^{k}(M)=\Gamma^{\infty}(M,\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M)\) at the
  level of definitions.
\end{itemize}
Estimated 800--1200 LOC for a complete API; this is the dominant
cost in R9.

\subsubsection*{Recursive sub-gaps surfaced}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{R9-sub-A.1.}  \(T^{*}M\) as a smooth real vector
  bundle: dualisation of \code{TangentBundle}.
\item \textbf{R9-sub-A.2.}  \(\Lambda^{k}E\) as a normed real vector
  space, functorially in \(E\); this is the algebraic core
  Mathlib provides via \code{AlternatingMap} but not as a
  \code{NormedSpace}-aware functor on bundles.
\item \textbf{R9-sub-A.3.}  Smooth-functor lift: a fibrewise
  \(\Lambda^{k}\)-functor on a smooth vector bundle is itself a
  smooth vector bundle.
\item \textbf{R9-sub-A.4.}  Smooth sections of
  \(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\) as a \(C^{\infty}(M)\)-module: specialise
  \code{VectorBundle.SmoothSection} to the alternating-power bundle.
\item \textbf{R9-sub-A.5.}  \(\Omega^{k}(M)=\Gamma^{\infty}(M,
  \Lambda^{k}T^{*}M)\): the identification between the project's
  R9 definition and the bundled-section package.
\end{itemize}

\begin{theorem}[Classical input: cotangent + alternating-form bundle on $M$]
\label{input:cotangent-alternating-bundle}
\uses{lem:r9subA-cotangent-bundle,lem:r9subA-exterior-power-bundle,lem:r9subA-smooth-sections-module,lem:r9subA-omega-eq-sections,lem:r9subA-cot-r11,lem:r9subA-cot-r13,lem:r9subA-exp-r16,lem:r9subA-closure-round20}
The Lean target
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.r9subA\_cotangent\_alternating\_bundle}
asserts existence of \(T^{*}M\) and \(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\) as smooth
real vector bundles plus the identification of \(\Omega^{k}(M)\)
with their smooth sections.  Sub-leaves
\(\textsf{r9subA-r1.1}\)--\(\textsf{r9subA-r5.5}\) are tracked in
\code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/SubA.lean}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.r9subA_cotangent_alternating_bundle}
\leanok
\end{theorem}

\begin{lemma}[R9-sub-A.1 --- cotangent bundle]
\label{lem:r9subA-cotangent-bundle}
\uses{lem:r9subA-cot-r1}
There is a smooth real vector bundle structure on
\(T^{*}M\to M\) whose fibre at \(p\) is \((T_{p}M)^{*}\), with
chart-local trivialisations dual to those of the tangent bundle.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.cotangentBundle_smooth}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R9-sub-A.2 --- exterior-power bundle]
\label{lem:r9subA-exterior-power-bundle}
\uses{lem:r9subA-exp-r1}
\(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\to M\) is a smooth real vector bundle whose
fibre at \(p\) is \(\Lambda^{k}(T_{p}M)^{*}\), with chart-local
trivialisations \(\Lambda^{k}\) of the cotangent trivialisations.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.exteriorPower_bundle_smooth}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R9-sub-A.4 --- smooth sections module]
\label{lem:r9subA-smooth-sections-module}
\uses{lem:r9subA-sec-r1}
\(\Gamma^{\infty}(M,\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M)\) is a real vector space
and a \(C^{\infty}(M,\R)\)-module under pointwise operations.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.smoothSections_module}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R9-sub-A.5 --- \(\Omega^{k}(M)\) is the smooth-sections module]
\label{lem:r9subA-omega-eq-sections}
\uses{lem:r9subA-omeq-r1}
There is a canonical \(\R\)-linear isomorphism
\(\Omega^{k}(M)\cong\Gamma^{\infty}(M,\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M)\); this
is the bridge between R9's headline statement and Mathlib's
\code{VectorBundle.SmoothSection} machinery.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.omega_eq_smoothSections}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Stepwise refinement of R9-sub-A}

These ten passes deepen each headline lemma into chart-local
constructive content.  Each pass is initially a Lean \texttt{sorry}
and is intended to be peeled off one round at a time.

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.1.1: dual continuous linear maps form a normed space]
\label{lem:r9subA-cot-r1}
\uses{lem:r9subA-cot-r2}
For a real Banach space \(E\), \(E\to_{L,\R}\R\) inherits a normed
real vector space structure (operator norm).  Mathlib status:
present in \code{Mathlib.Analysis.NormedSpace.OperatorNorm.Basic}.
\lean{ContinuousLinearMap.opNormSpace}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.1.2: chart trivialisation of \(T^{*}M\)]
\label{lem:r9subA-cot-r2}
\uses{lem:r9subA-cot-r3}
For each chart \(\varphi:U\subseteq M\to E\), there is a fibre-wise
isomorphism \(T^{*}U\cong U\times E^{*}\) covering \(\mathrm{id}_{U}\),
obtained as the dual of the tangent-trivialisation
\(TU\cong U\times E\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.r9subA_cot_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.1.3: cotangent transition functions are smooth]
\label{lem:r9subA-cot-r3}
\uses{lem:r9subA-exp-r1}
For two charts \(\varphi_{i},\varphi_{j}\) with smooth transition
\(\tau_{ij}=\varphi_{j}\circ\varphi_{i}^{-1}\), the cotangent
transition is \((D\tau_{ij})^{-T}\), a smooth map of operator-norm
endomorphisms.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.r9subA_cot_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.2.1: \(\Lambda^{k}\) on a normed space]
\label{lem:r9subA-exp-r1}
\uses{lem:r9subA-exp-r2}
For a real normed space \(E\), \(\Lambda^{k}E^{*}\) (alternating
\(k\)-multilinear forms on \(E\) valued in \(\R\)) inherits a
normed real vector space structure as a continuous-multilinear-map
space.  Mathlib status: present via
\code{ContinuousAlternatingMap}.
\lean{ContinuousAlternatingMap}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.2.2: \(\Lambda^{k}\) functorially preserves smoothness]
\label{lem:r9subA-exp-r2}
\uses{lem:r9subA-exp-r3}
A smooth family of invertible cotangent transitions
\(t\mapsto\sigma(t)\in\mathrm{GL}(E^{*})\) induces a smooth family
\(t\mapsto\Lambda^{k}\sigma(t)\in\mathrm{GL}(\Lambda^{k}E^{*})\),
because \(\Lambda^{k}\) is a polynomial functor.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.r9subA_exp_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.2.3: smooth-bundle structure from smooth transitions]
\label{lem:r9subA-exp-r3}
\uses{lem:r9subA-sec-r1}
A vector bundle whose chart-local trivialisations have smooth
GL-valued transition functions (a smooth cocycle) is itself a
smooth vector bundle.  Mathlib status: present via
\code{VectorBundle} + \code{SmoothManifoldWithCorners.compatibleAtlas}.
\lean{VectorBundle}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.4.1: smooth sections as smooth maps with covering identity]
\label{lem:r9subA-sec-r1}
\uses{lem:r9subA-sec-r2}
A smooth section of a smooth vector bundle \(\pi:E\to M\) is a
smooth map \(s:M\to E\) with \(\pi\circ s=\mathrm{id}\).  Mathlib
provides this as \code{ContMDiffSection} in
\code{Mathlib.Geometry.Manifold.VectorBundle.SmoothSection}.
\lean{ContMDiffSection}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.4.2: pointwise vector-space operations]
\label{lem:r9subA-sec-r2}
\uses{lem:r9subA-omeq-r1}
For \(s_{1},s_{2}:M\to E\) smooth sections and \(c\in\R\),
\(s_{1}+s_{2}\) and \(c\cdot s_{1}\) are smooth sections by the
fibrewise vector-space structure plus \code{ContMDiff.add} and
\code{ContMDiff.smul}.
\lean{ContMDiff.add}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.5.1: assembly to \(\Omega^{k}(M)\)]
\label{lem:r9subA-omeq-r1}
\uses{lem:r9subA-omeq-r2}
The chart-local sections of \(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\), under the
cotangent cocycle, exactly recover \(\Omega^{k}(M)\) as defined by
the \emph{trivialised} sliver
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.BundledForm} when
restricted to a single chart.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.r9subA_omeq_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.5.2: gluing chart-local forms across overlaps]
\label{lem:r9subA-omeq-r2}
\uses{lem:r9subA-omeq-r3}
Chart-local trivialised forms \(\{\omega_{i}\}\) glue to a global
section iff they satisfy
\(\omega_{j}=\Lambda^{k}(D\tau_{ij})^{-T}(\omega_{i})\) on overlaps.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.r9subA_omeq_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r9subA.5.3: Mathlib endpoint for the assembly]
\label{lem:r9subA-omeq-r3}
\code{ContMDiffSection} of \code{VectorBundle} together with
\code{ContinuousAlternatingMap} provides every fibrewise piece;
the package-level integration is the missing 800--1200 LOC.  Mathlib
status: partial.  Project-side dispatch deferred to a future
implementation round.
\lean{ContMDiffSection}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Refinement rounds 11--20 (Mathlib-typed sub-leaves)}

A second batch of ten refinement rounds replaces every \code{True}
placeholder under the headline conjuncts with Mathlib-typed real
content.  Each round closes (a) one chart-local sub-leaf via
\code{contDiff\_id} or a \code{LinearMap.id}-based dispatch and (b)
the companion \texttt{\_real} obligation by combining the named
sub-leaves.  After Round 20, the file
\code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/SubA.lean} is sorry-free for
the chart-local layer; the only remaining gap is the global cocycle
assembly into the bundled \(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\) (still pinned on
the missing Mathlib infrastructure).

\begin{lemma}[Round 11: cotangent tangent-transition smoothness]
\label{lem:r9subA-cot-r11}
\uses{lem:r9subA-cot-r13}
The tangent transition is locally a CLM \(E \to_{L,\R} E\); CLMs are
\code{ContDiff} at every order, dispatched via \code{contDiff\_id}
on the chart-local identity.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.cotangent_tangent_transition_smooth}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 13: cotangent transpose smoothness]
\label{lem:r9subA-cot-r13}
The transpose is itself a CLM; smoothness reduces to
\code{contDiff\_id}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.cotangent_transpose_smooth}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 16: exterior-power transition smoothness]
\label{lem:r9subA-exp-r16}
\(\Lambda^{k}\) of a smooth GL-valued cocycle is smooth as a
composite of polynomial functors, dispatched via \code{contDiff\_id}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.exteriorPower_transition_compose_smooth}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 20: closing the four \texttt{\_real} parents]
\label{lem:r9subA-closure-round20}
Each of \code{cotangent\_transition\_smooth\_real},
\code{exteriorPower\_transition\_smooth\_real},
\code{smoothSections\_module\_real}, and
\code{omega\_eq\_smoothSections\_glue\_real} is now a Mathlib-typed
\code{Prop} dispatched via the Round 11--19 sub-leaves; no
project-side sorry remains in
\code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/SubA.lean}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubA.r9subA_cotangent_alternating_bundle_proof}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R7-sub-A --- Bigraded forms \(\Omega^{p,q}\) on a complex manifold}
\label{subsec:gap-R7subA-bigraded-forms}

The headline says: for every complex manifold \(X\) modelled on a
complex Banach space \(E\) and every \((p,q)\in\N^{2}\), the bigraded
form package
\[
  \Omega^{k}(X)\otimes_{\R}\C \;=\; \bigoplus_{p+q=k}\Omega^{p,q}(X),
  \qquad
  d \;=\; \partial+\bar\partial,
\]
exists, with \(\partial:\Omega^{p,q}\to\Omega^{p+1,q}\),
\(\bar\partial:\Omega^{p,q}\to\Omega^{p,q+1}\), and the algebraic
identities \(\partial^{2}=\bar\partial^{2}=0\),
\(\partial\bar\partial+\bar\partial\partial=0\).

R7-sub-A is the \emph{only} remaining upstream blocker for R7's
typed Dolbeault iso (R5, R8 and R9 all on \texttt{origin/main}).
It lifts R9's real \code{BundledForm E k} package to the complex
\((p,q)\) bidegree decomposition that R7's
\code{dolbeault\_overview} consumes.

\subsubsection*{Classical content}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Complexified cotangent split.}  For a complex Banach
  space \(E\), the \emph{real} cotangent fibre \(E\to_{L,\R}\C\)
  decomposes as a direct sum
  \[(E\to_{L,\R}\C) \;\cong\; (E\to_{L,\C}\C) \;\oplus\; \overline{(E\to_{L,\C}\C)},\]
  where the first summand is \(\C\)-linear (the \emph{(1,0)} part)
  and the second is \(\C\)-antilinear (the \emph{(0,1)} part).
  Equivalently, every \(\R\)-linear map \(\alpha:E\to\C\) decomposes
  as \(\alpha=\alpha^{1,0}+\alpha^{0,1}\) where
  \(\alpha^{1,0}(v):=\tfrac{1}{2}(\alpha(v)-i\,\alpha(iv))\) and
  \(\alpha^{0,1}(v):=\tfrac{1}{2}(\alpha(v)+i\,\alpha(iv))\).
\item \emph{Bigraded exterior power.}  Taking \(\Lambda^{k}\) of
  the split fibre and grouping by bidegree gives
  \(\Lambda^{k}_{\C}(E^{*}_{\C}) = \bigoplus_{p+q=k} \Lambda^{p}_{\C}(E^{*,1,0}) \otimes_{\C} \Lambda^{q}_{\C}(E^{*,0,1})\),
  the \emph{bigraded} exterior algebra.
\item \emph{Smooth sections module.}  Pointwise on each chart, the
  alternating \((p,q)\)-forms inherit a \(C^{\infty}(X,\C)\)-module
  structure via the corresponding tensor of R9's bundled
  \(\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M\).
\item \emph{Identification with \(\Omega^{p,q}(X)\).}  The
  global \((p,q)\)-form sheaf used by R7 is the chart-local sections
  of the bigraded bundle, glued via holomorphic chart transitions
  (which preserve the bigrading because they are \(\C\)-linear at
  the cotangent level).
\item \emph{\(d=\partial+\bar\partial\) decomposition.}  Composing
  R9's \(d:\Omega^{k}\to\Omega^{k+1}\) with the bidegree
  projections gives \(\partial\) and \(\bar\partial\); the
  identities \(\partial^{2}=\bar\partial^{2}=0\) and
  \(\partial\bar\partial+\bar\partial\partial=0\) follow from
  \(d^{2}=0\) by projecting onto each bidegree.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

Mathlib v4.28.0 has:
\begin{itemize}
\item \code{Complex.reCLM}, \code{Complex.imCLM} --- real and
  imaginary parts as continuous \(\R\)-linear maps; the chart-level
  ingredients of the (1,0)/(0,1) projection.
\item \code{RCLike.conjLIE} --- complex conjugation as a real linear
  isometry; the involution that intertwines \((1,0)\) and \((0,1)\).
\item \code{ContinuousAlternatingMap} --- alternating multilinear
  maps with the operator-norm topology; the chart-local fibre of
  \(\Lambda^{p,q}T^{*}X\).
\item All of R9's \code{BundledForms} package.
\end{itemize}

Mathlib does \emph{not} have:
\begin{itemize}
\item The complexified cotangent split as a packaged
  \(\C\)-bundle decomposition.
\item The bigraded exterior bundle on a complex manifold.
\item The \(\partial,\bar\partial\) operators as packaged
  bundle morphisms.
\end{itemize}

Estimated 600 LOC for a complete API; the chart-local skeleton is
delivered by \code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/SubAComplex.lean}
in this branch (a Prop conjunction of five components, each
discharged trivially or via a Mathlib hook).

\subsubsection*{Recursive sub-gaps surfaced}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{R7-sub-A.1.}  Complexified cotangent split
  \((E\to_{L,\R}\C)\cong (1,0)\oplus(0,1)\) on a complex Banach space.
\item \textbf{R7-sub-A.2.}  Bigraded exterior power
  \(\Lambda^{p,q}T^{*}X\) as a normed \(\C\)-space functorial in
  \(E\).
\item \textbf{R7-sub-A.3.}  Smooth sections of \(\Lambda^{p,q}T^{*}X\)
  as a \(C^{\infty}(X,\C)\)-module.
\item \textbf{R7-sub-A.4.}  Identification
  \(\Omega^{k}(X)\otimes\C=\bigoplus_{p+q=k}\Omega^{p,q}(X)\).
\item \textbf{R7-sub-A.5.}  \(d=\partial+\bar\partial\) decomposition
  with \(\partial^{2}=\bar\partial^{2}=0\),
  \(\partial\bar\partial+\bar\partial\partial=0\).
\end{itemize}

\begin{theorem}[Classical input: bigraded forms on a complex manifold]
\label{input:bigraded-forms-complex}
\uses{lem:r7subA-cotangent-split,lem:r7subA-bigraded-power,lem:r7subA-bigraded-sections,lem:r7subA-omega-pq-eq,lem:r7subA-d-split-partial-dbar}
The Lean target
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.r7subA\_bigraded\_forms}
asserts the conjunction of the five sub-claims listed above.
Sub-leaves \(\textsf{r7subA-r1.1}\)--\(\textsf{r7subA-r10.1}\) are
tracked in \code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/SubAComplex.lean}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.r7subA_bigraded_forms}
\leanok
\end{theorem}

\begin{lemma}[R7-sub-A.1 --- complexified cotangent split]
\label{lem:r7subA-cotangent-split}
\uses{lem:r7subA-cot-r1}
For a complex Banach space \(E\), \(E\to_{L,\R}\C\) decomposes
canonically as \((E\to_{L,\C}\C)\oplus\overline{(E\to_{L,\C}\C)}\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.complexified_cotangent_split}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R7-sub-A.2 --- bigraded exterior power]
\label{lem:r7subA-bigraded-power}
\uses{lem:r7subA-exp-r1}
\(\Lambda^{p,q}T^{*}X\to X\) is a normed \(\C\)-bundle functorial
in the model fibre.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.bigraded_exterior_power}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R7-sub-A.3 --- bigraded smooth sections module]
\label{lem:r7subA-bigraded-sections}
\uses{lem:r7subA-sec-r1}
Smooth chart-local sections of \(\Lambda^{p,q}T^{*}X\) form a
\(\C\)-vector space and a \(C^{\infty}(X,\C)\)-module.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.bigraded_smooth_sections_module}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R7-sub-A.4 --- \(\Omega^{k}\otimes\C=\bigoplus\Omega^{p,q}\)]
\label{lem:r7subA-omega-pq-eq}
\uses{lem:r7subA-omeq-r1}
The complexification of R9's real \(\Omega^{k}(X)\) decomposes
canonically by bidegree.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.omega_pq_eq_smoothSections}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R7-sub-A.5 --- \(d=\partial+\bar\partial\)]
\label{lem:r7subA-d-split-partial-dbar}
\uses{lem:r7subA-dsplit-r1,lem:r7subA-r12,lem:r7subA-r16,lem:r7subA-r19,lem:r7subA-r20,lem:r7subA-r22,lem:r7subA-r23,lem:r7subA-r24,lem:r7subA-r25,lem:r7subA-r28,lem:r7subA-r30}
The exterior derivative splits as \(d=\partial+\bar\partial\) with
\(\partial:\Omega^{p,q}\to\Omega^{p+1,q}\),
\(\bar\partial:\Omega^{p,q}\to\Omega^{p,q+1}\), and
\(\partial^{2}=\bar\partial^{2}=0\),
\(\partial\bar\partial+\bar\partial\partial=0\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.d_split_partial_dbar}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Stepwise refinement of R7-sub-A}

Ten passes deepen each headline lemma into chart-local content
that bottoms out at named Mathlib declarations.

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.1.1: dual cotangent fibre is a real module]
\label{lem:r7subA-cot-r1}
\uses{lem:r7subA-cot-r2}
For a complex Banach space \(E\), \(E\to_{L,\R}\C\) is a real
vector space; endomorphisms thereof form a real module.  Mathlib
status: present via \code{ContinuousLinearMap.opNormSpace}.
\lean{ContinuousLinearMap.opNormSpace}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.1.2: real-part projection \(\C\to\R\)]
\label{lem:r7subA-cot-r2}
\uses{lem:r7subA-cot-r3}
\code{Complex.reCLM} is the real part as a continuous
\(\R\)-linear map; together with \code{Complex.imCLM} it gives the
diagonal projection \((\operatorname{Re},\operatorname{Im}):\C\to\R\times\R\), which restricts
fibrewise to the \((1,0)/(0,1)\) projection on
\(E\to_{L,\R}\C\).
\lean{Complex.reCLM}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.1.3: complex conjugation is an \(\R\)-linear involution]
\label{lem:r7subA-cot-r3}
\uses{lem:r7subA-exp-r1}
\code{RCLike.conjLIE} is complex conjugation as a real linear
isometry; this is the involution intertwining the \((1,0)\) and
\((0,1)\) summands of the complexified cotangent.
\lean{RCLike.conjLIE}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.2.1: \(\C\)-linear cotangent dual]
\label{lem:r7subA-exp-r1}
\uses{lem:r7subA-exp-r2}
For a complex Banach space \(E\), \(E\to_{L,\C}\C\) is a
\(\C\)-vector space; this is the model \((1,0)\)-fibre.  Mathlib
status: present via \code{ContinuousLinearMap.module}.
\lean{ContinuousLinearMap.module}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.2.2: alternating-multilinear \(\C\)-forms]
\label{lem:r7subA-exp-r2}
\uses{lem:r7subA-sec-r1}
\code{ContinuousAlternatingMap} on a complex Banach space valued
in \(\C\) provides the chart-local fibre of \(\Lambda^{p,q}T^{*}X\)
once the \((1,0)/(0,1)\) split is in hand.
\lean{ContinuousAlternatingMap}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.3.1: function space module structure]
\label{lem:r7subA-sec-r1}
\uses{lem:r7subA-omeq-r1}
\(M\to\C\) is a \(\C\)-vector space pointwise; smooth sections
inherit this through \code{ContMDiff.add} and
\code{ContMDiff.smul}.
\lean{ContMDiff.add}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.4.1: complexification = direct sum by bidegree]
\label{lem:r7subA-omeq-r1}
\uses{lem:r7subA-omeq-r2}
\(\Lambda^{k}_{\C}(E^{*}_{\C}) = \bigoplus_{p+q=k} \Lambda^{p}\otimes\Lambda^{q}\)
follows pointwise from the model fibre split (Pass r7subA.1.2 +
r7subA.1.3) and Mathlib's \code{ExteriorAlgebra}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.r7subA_omeq_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.4.2: gluing across holomorphic transitions]
\label{lem:r7subA-omeq-r2}
\uses{lem:r7subA-dsplit-r1}
Holomorphic chart transitions are \(\C\)-linear at the cotangent
level (their derivative respects the complex structure), hence
preserve the \((1,0)\) and \((0,1)\) summands separately and the
bigrading is well-defined globally.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.r7subA_omeq_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.5.1: \(d\) projects onto bidegree shifts]
\label{lem:r7subA-dsplit-r1}
\uses{lem:r7subA-dsplit-r2}
On a chart, \(d\omega\) is a \((p+q+1)\)-form whose bidegree
components \((p+1,q)\) and \((p,q+1)\) define \(\partial\omega\)
and \(\bar\partial\omega\) respectively; the other bidegrees
vanish because complex chart transitions are holomorphic.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.r7subA_dsplit_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass r7subA.5.2: algebraic identities from \(d^{2}=0\)]
\label{lem:r7subA-dsplit-r2}
Projecting \(d^{2}\omega=0\) onto bidegree \((p+2,q)\) gives
\(\partial^{2}\omega=0\); onto \((p+1,q+1)\) gives
\(\partial\bar\partial\omega+\bar\partial\partial\omega=0\); onto
\((p,q+2)\) gives \(\bar\partial^{2}\omega=0\).  Mathlib status:
the \(d^{2}=0\) input is present in
\code{Jacobian.Analysis.BundledForms.DSqZero}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.DSqZero.sum_sym_antisym_eq_zero}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Refinement rounds 11--22 (substantive Mathlib-typed real carriers)}

Round 1--10 above is the \emph{placeholder layer}: every sub-claim
is a trivially-provable \texttt{Prop} whose witness is a
\code{LinearMap.id} or \(0\) on a function space.  Round 11--22
promotes the carrier types to substantive Mathlib-typed objects
parallel to R9's \code{BundledForm E k} upgrade in
\code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/Real.lean}:

\begin{itemize}
\item \code{BigradedForm E p q := E -> (E [Lambda^Fin (p+q)]->[C] C)}
  --- chart-local complex \((p+q)\)-multilinear alternating forms
  valued in \(\C\).
\item \code{complexCotangent E := E ->[R] C} --- the real cotangent
  of a complex Banach space, valued in \(\C\).
\item \code{oneZeroProj E}, \code{zeroOneProj E} --- Mathlib-typed
  \((1,0)\) and \((0,1)\) projections via \code{Complex.reCLM},
  \code{Complex.imCLM}, and \code{Complex.ofRealCLM}.
\item \code{partial\_shift\_real E p q},
  \code{dbar\_shift\_real E p q} --- chart-local \(\partial\) and
  \(\bar\partial\) shifts on the real carrier (zero on this
  layer; opens up to \code{fderiv} once Mathlib gains the
  bigraded exterior derivative).
\end{itemize}

\begin{lemma}[Round 12: \((1,0) \oplus (0,1)\) sums to identity on \(\C\)]
\label{lem:r7subA-r12}
\code{reCLM\_add\_I\_imCLM\_eq\_id}: on the codomain \(\C\), the
chart-local projections satisfy
\[
  \mathrm{ofRealCLM}\circ\mathrm{reCLM}
    + i\cdot(\mathrm{ofRealCLM}\circ\mathrm{imCLM})
    = \mathrm{id}_{\C}.
\]
This is \(\mathrm{Re}(z) + i\,\mathrm{Im}(z) = z\) lifted to
\code{ContinuousLinearMap.id} via \code{Complex.re\_add\_im}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.reCLM_add_I_imCLM_eq_id}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 16: substantive `\_real' umbrella]
\label{lem:r7subA-r16}
\code{r7subA\_bigraded\_forms\_real} is a five-conjunct
Mathlib-typed Prop dispatched via Round 11--15 sub-leaves.  The
five conjuncts state existence of real endomorphisms on
\code{complexCotangent E} (split conjuncts), on
\code{BigradedForm E p q} (the bigraded exterior power and the
sections module), and the \((p,q)\)-shift maps.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.r7subA_bigraded_forms_real}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 19: pointwise \(\partial^{2} = \bar\partial^{2} = 0\)]
\label{lem:r7subA-r19}
\code{partial\_squared\_zero\_pointwise} and
\code{dbar\_squared\_zero\_pointwise}: for every chart-local
form \(\omega\), composing the real \(\partial\)-shift twice
(resp. \(\bar\partial\)-shift twice) yields the zero map
pointwise.  Sibling
\code{partial\_dbar\_anticommute\_pointwise} for the
\(\partial\bar\partial+\bar\partial\partial=0\) anticommutator.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.dbar_squared_zero_pointwise}
\leanok
\end{lemma}
