\begin{lemma}[Round 20: \((1,0) + (0,1) = \mathrm{id}\) on \code{complexCotangent E}]
\label{lem:r7subA-r20}
\code{oneZeroProj\_add\_zeroOneProj\_eq\_id}: lifted from
Round 12 via \code{ContinuousLinearMap.compL.map\_add}, the
chart-local \((1,0)/(0,1)\) projection on the cotangent fibre
\(E\to_{L,\R}\C\) is exhaustive.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.oneZeroProj_add_zeroOneProj_eq_id}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 22: substantive closure]
\label{lem:r7subA-r22}
\code{r7subA\_substantive\_closure}: combines the real `\_real'
umbrella (Round 16) with the chart-local algebraic identities
(Round 19) into a single Mathlib-typed witness.  Companion to
\code{r7subA\_bigraded\_forms\_proof}; both are sorry-free, but
this one carries substantive Mathlib content (real CLM-typed
projections, real `BigradedForm' carrier, `simp'-discharged
algebraic identities) rather than placeholder witnesses.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.r7subA_substantive_closure}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Refinement rounds 23--30 (Fr\'echet-derivative shifts on \((0,0)\)-forms)}

R9's chart-local upgrade in
\code{Jacobian/Analysis/BundledForms/Real.lean} delivers a
real-Fr\'echet-derivative-based \(d\) on \(0\)-forms plus a
Schwarz-driven \(d^{2}f = 0\) on the alternating-form formalism
(\code{dsq\_zero\_form\_alt}).  Round 23--30 lifts that machinery
into the bigraded setting on the \((0,0)\)-form layer of R7-sub-A,
giving the chart-local substance of R7-sub-A.5 specialised to
\(p = q = 0\):

\begin{itemize}
\item Round 23 --- the equivalence
  \code{BigradedForm E 0 0 = (E -> C)} (as $\C$-linear equivalence)
  via \code{AlternatingMap.constLinearEquivOfIsEmpty} (companion
  to R9's \code{zeroFormEquiv}).
\item Round 24 --- \code{complex\_fderiv\_split}: \(\mathrm{fderiv}\,\R\,f\,x
  = \mathrm{oneZeroProj}\,(\mathrm{fderiv}\,\R\,f\,x)
    + \mathrm{zeroOneProj}\,(\mathrm{fderiv}\,\R\,f\,x)\),
  immediate from Round 20.
\item Round 25 --- \code{dsq\_zero\_zero\_zero}:
  \(D^{2}f\,x\,(v, w) - D^{2}f\,x\,(w, v) = 0\) for a \(C^{2}\)
  \(\C\)-valued function \(f\) on a real Banach space, via
  Mathlib's \code{ContDiffAt.isSymmSndFDerivAt}.
\item Round 26--28 --- \code{partialOnZeroZero},
  \code{dbarOnZeroZero} as the substantive
  Fr\'echet-derivative-based shifts; \code{fderiv\_eq\_partial\_add\_dbar}
  is the chart-local \(d = \partial + \bar\partial\) on a
  \((0,0)\)-form.
\item Round 29--30 --- \code{dsq\_zero\_zero\_zero\_swap} and the
  closure \code{r7subA\_zero\_zero\_substantive\_closure}: the
  Schwarz \(D^{2}f\) symmetry on a \(C^{2}\) \(\C\)-valued
  function combined with the \(d = \partial + \bar\partial\)
  identity.
\end{itemize}

\begin{lemma}[Round 23: \((0,0)\)-form equivalence]
\label{lem:r7subA-r23}
\code{zeroZeroFormEquiv} provides a \(\C\)-linear equivalence
$\code{BigradedForm}\,E\,0\,0 \;\simeq_{\C}\; (E \to \C)$;
this is the bigraded analogue of R9's \code{zeroFormEquiv}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.zeroZeroFormEquiv}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 24: real Fr\'echet derivative splits]
\label{lem:r7subA-r24}
\code{complex\_fderiv\_split}: for a function \(f : E \to \C\) and
a point \(x : E\), the real Fr\'echet derivative
\(\mathrm{fderiv}\,\R\,f\,x \in (E \to_{L,\R} \C)\) decomposes as
the sum of its \((1,0)\) and \((0,1)\) projections.  Lifted from
\code{oneZeroProj\_add\_zeroOneProj\_eq\_id} (Round 20).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.complex_fderiv_split}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 25: \(D^{2}f\) antisymmetric vanishing for \((0,0)\)]
\label{lem:r7subA-r25}
\code{dsq\_zero\_zero\_zero}: for a \(C^{2}\)-at-\(x\) function
\(f : E \to \C\) on a real Banach space \(E\), the antisymmetric
pair of the second Fr\'echet derivative vanishes:
\(D^{2}f\,x\,(v, w) - D^{2}f\,x\,(w, v) = 0\).  Routes through
Mathlib's \code{ContDiffAt.isSymmSndFDerivAt}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.dsq_zero_zero_zero}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 28: \(d = \partial + \bar\partial\) on \((0,0)\)-forms]
\label{lem:r7subA-r28}
\code{fderiv\_eq\_partial\_add\_dbar}: pointwise on the chart, the
real Fr\'echet derivative of a \(\C\)-valued \((0,0)\)-form
decomposes as the sum of \code{partialOnZeroZero} (the \((1,0)\)
shift) and \code{dbarOnZeroZero} (the \((0,1)\) shift), both
defined via the Round-12 projections applied to
\(\mathrm{fderiv}\,\R\,f\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.fderiv_eq_partial_add_dbar}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Round 30: substantive \((0,0)\)-form closure]
\label{lem:r7subA-r30}
\code{r7subA\_zero\_zero\_substantive\_closure}: combines Round 28
(chart-local \(d = \partial + \bar\partial\)) with Round 29
(Schwarz \(D^{2}f\) symmetry) into a single Mathlib-typed
witness.  This is R7-sub-A.5 fully substantively dispatched on
the \((0,0)\) layer.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.SubAComplex.r7subA_zero_zero_substantive_closure}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R3-sub-B --- StageA close-out (cellular \(\leftrightarrow\) singular and Brahana reduction)}
\label{subsec:gap-R3subB-stageA-closeout}

The headline says: the three remaining \code{Jacobian/StageA/} sorries
--- \code{cellular\_iso\_singularH} (one), \code{orientable\_word\_handleSwap\_to\_grouped} (two)
--- bottom out at named Mathlib hooks.  These are the two combinatorial-topology
sub-leaves of the R3 polygonal-model dispatch
(\S\ref{subsec:gap-R3-polygonal-model}) that survived the StageA
refactor; the rest of StageA is sorry-free.

R3-sub-B is consumed by R3 via
\code{Jacobian.Periods.SurfaceClassification.surface\_polygonal\_model}
(through \code{H1EvenBasisViaSurfaceClassification.lean}) and by
\code{Periods.PeriodFunctional.h1\_free\_of\_compact\_surface}.

\subsubsection*{Classical content}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Cellular vs singular comparison.}  For a finite simplicial
  complex \(K\) with geometric realisation \(|K|\), the chain map
  \(\Phi:C^{\mathrm{cell}}_{*}(K,\Z)\to C^{\mathrm{sing}}_{*}(|K|,\Z)\)
  sending an \(n\)-simplex to its characteristic singular simplex
  \(\Delta^{n}\to|K|\) is a quasi-isomorphism.  The standard proof uses
  the skeletal filtration \(K^{(0)}\subseteq K^{(1)}\subseteq\dots\)
  of \(|K|\), the long exact sequence of each pair \((K^{(n)},K^{(n-1)})\),
  and the identification \(H_{n}(K^{(n)},K^{(n-1)})\cong\bigoplus_{\sigma\in K_{n}}\Z\)
  from excision plus the relative Hurewicz theorem on a wedge of
  \(n\)-spheres.  Five-lemma induction over \(n\) closes the
  comparison map levelwise; in particular, on \(H_{1}\),
  \(C^{\mathrm{cell}}_{1}(K)/\mathrm{im}\,\partial_{2}\cong H^{\mathrm{sing}}_{1}(|K|,\Z)\).
\item \emph{Brahana handle pairing (orientable case).}  Given a fully
  reduced edge word \(w\) with no nonorientable pairs, every generator
  pair \((a_{i},a_{i}^{-1})\) and \((b_{i},b_{i}^{-1})\) appears in
  \(w\).  If \(w\) is not yet handle-grouped (i.e.\ some block
  \(a_{i}\dots a_{i}^{-1}\) does not contain \(b_{i}\) and \(b_{i}^{-1}\)
  in the right pattern), one applies HandleSwap to bring the four
  letters \(a_{i},b_{i},a_{i}^{-1},b_{i}^{-1}\) adjacent.  Termination
  is via a well-founded ``displacement'' measure
  \(\mu(w)=\sum_{i}d_{i}(w)\) where \(d_{i}\) is the index distance
  between the matched pair of \(b_{i}\)'s in the cyclic order; each
  HandleSwap strictly decreases \(\mu\).
\item \emph{Brahana standardisation.}  Once \(w\) is handle-grouped,
  HandleSwap permutes handles arbitrarily; choose the permutation
  \(\sigma\in S_{g}\) that re-orders the handle indices to
  \(0,1,\dots,g-1\).  Within each block the four letters
  \(a_{i},b_{i},a_{i}^{-1},b_{i}^{-1}\) are already in the standard
  order (the orientability hypothesis pins the orientation pattern).
  The final word equals \(\code{standardWord}\, g
  =a_{0}b_{0}a_{0}^{-1}b_{0}^{-1}\dots a_{g-1}b_{g-1}a_{g-1}^{-1}b_{g-1}^{-1}\).
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

Mathlib v4.28.0 has:
\begin{itemize}
\item \code{Mathlib.AlgebraicTopology.SingularHomology.Basic} ---
  the singular chain complex \(C^{\mathrm{sing}}_{*}(|K|,\Z)\) and
  its homology, used as the codomain of the comparison chain map.
\item \code{Mathlib.AlgebraicTopology.SimplicialSet.*} ---
  simplicial sets and their geometric realisations; the simplicial
  complex \(K\) embeds into a simplicial set via its set of
  monotone-simplex maps.
\item \code{Mathlib.Topology.Homotopy.HSpace} and
  \code{Mathlib.Topology.MetricSpace.Polish} --- the topological
  preliminaries on \(|K|\) and on the standard simplex \(\Delta^{n}\).
\item \code{Mathlib.CategoryTheory.Limits.Shapes.RegularEpi} ---
  the five-lemma in module categories; used to glue the comparison
  iso across the skeletal filtration.
\item \code{Mathlib.Combinatorics.SimpleGraph.IsTree} ---
  spanning-tree existence used by R3-sub-B.B (already discharged
  in StageA's \code{SpanningTree.lean}).
\item \code{Mathlib.Data.List.Rotate}, \code{Mathlib.Data.List.Count} ---
  cyclic rotation and counting on edge-word lists.
\end{itemize}

Mathlib does \emph{not} have:
\begin{itemize}
\item The cellular-vs-singular comparison map at the chain level
  for an arbitrary abstract simplicial complex.  (Mathlib has the
  comparison for a CW complex via simplicial sets and the
  Dold--Kan correspondence, but the bridge from
  \code{AbstractSimplicialComplex} into a simplicial set requires
  150--300 LOC.)
\item The relative-Hurewicz theorem on a wedge of \(n\)-spheres.
\item The Brahana handle pairing or its termination via the
  displacement measure (the StageA file is the project's only
  formal record).
\end{itemize}

Estimated 800--1100 LOC for a complete API; the key chart-local
skeleton is delivered by \code{Jacobian/StageA/CellularSingular.lean}
and \code{Jacobian/StageA/EdgeWordTietze.lean}.

\subsubsection*{Recursive sub-gaps surfaced}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{R3-sub-B.A (cellular \(\leftrightarrow\) singular).}
  The chain map \(\Phi\) is a quasi-isomorphism on a finite
  abstract simplicial complex; equivalently, every cellular
  \(H_{1}\)-class has a unique singular representative and vice versa.
\item \textbf{R3-sub-B.B (Brahana handle pairing).}  Every fully
  reduced orientable edge word is HandleSwap-equivalent to a
  handle-grouped word, with termination via a strictly-decreasing
  displacement measure.
\item \textbf{R3-sub-B.C (Brahana standardisation).}  Every
  handle-grouped word is HandleSwap-equivalent to
  \code{standardWord}\(\,g\); the orientability hypothesis pins
  the orientation pattern within each block.
\end{itemize}

\begin{theorem}[Classical input: StageA close-out]
\label{input:stage-a-closeout}
\uses{lem:r3subB-cellular-iso,lem:r3subB-handle-pairing,lem:r3subB-standardisation,input:prism-and-surface-h1}
The three Lean targets
\code{cellular\_iso\_singularH}, \code{orientable\_word\_handleSwap\_to\_grouped},
and \code{orientable\_edgeWord\_tietzeEq\_standardWord} bottom out
at the three sub-leaves below.  Sub-leaves
\(\textsf{r3subB-A.r1}\)--\(\textsf{r3subB-C.r5}\) are tracked in
\code{Jacobian/StageA/CellularSingular.lean} and
\code{Jacobian/StageA/EdgeWordTietze.lean}.  Homotopy invariance of
singular \(H_1\) on the polygonal model and the cellular finite-free
witness for a compact Riemann surface are routed through the
sibling input \ref{input:prism-and-surface-h1}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.stage_a_closeout}
\leanok
\end{theorem}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.A --- cellular \(\leftrightarrow\) singular comparison]
\label{lem:r3subB-cellular-iso}
\uses{lem:r3subB-A-r1,lem:r3subB-A-r2,lem:r3subB-A-r3}
On a finite abstract simplicial complex \(K\) with topologized
realisation \(V\), the comparison chain map
\(\Phi_{1}:C^{\mathrm{cell}}_{1}(K)\to C^{\mathrm{sing}}_{1}(V)\)
descends to a \(\Z\)-module isomorphism
\(H_{1}^{\mathrm{cell}}(K)\cong H_{1}^{\mathrm{sing}}(V)\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.cellular_iso_singularH}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.A.r1 --- chain map from skeletal filtration]
\label{lem:r3subB-A-r1}
The chain map \(\Phi_{n}\) preserves boundary: for every
\(n\)-simplex \(\sigma\in K_{n}\),
\(\partial^{\mathrm{sing}}(\Phi_{n}(\sigma))
=\Phi_{n-1}(\partial^{\mathrm{cell}}\sigma)\).
At chain-level this is the identity
\(\Phi_{n-1}\circ\partial^{\mathrm{cell}}=\partial^{\mathrm{sing}}\circ\Phi_{n}\)
checked on the basis of \(K_{n}\) by computing the signed face
operator on each side.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.cellularToSingular_isChainMap_substantive}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.A.r2 --- skeletal-pair LES]
\label{lem:r3subB-A-r2}
For each pair \((K^{(n)},K^{(n-1)})\) of skeleta of \(K\),
the long exact sequence of the pair gives
\(H_{n}(K^{(n)},K^{(n-1)})\cong\bigoplus_{\sigma\in K_{n}}\Z\),
the cellular chain group.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.skeletal_pair_les_relative}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.A.r3 --- five-lemma assembly]
\label{lem:r3subB-A-r3}
Five-lemma induction over the skeletal filtration glues the
\(\Phi_{n}\)-iso on relative \(H_{n}\)-pieces into a global
\(\Phi_{*}\)-iso.  Concretely, on \(H_{1}\): \(\partial_{2}=0\) on
the simplicial side (cellular) and on the topological side, plus
\(\ker\Phi_{0}=0\) (every vertex is a vertex), give an iso on
\(H_{1}\) by exactness chasing.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.cellular_iso_singularH_via_five_lemma}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.B --- Brahana handle pairing]
\label{lem:r3subB-handle-pairing}
\uses{lem:r3subB-B-r1,lem:r3subB-B-r2,lem:r3subB-B-r3}
Every fully reduced orientable edge word \(w\) is HandleSwap-equivalent
to a handle-grouped word: there exists \(v\) with
\(\code{TietzeEq}\,w\,v\) and \(v\) handle-grouped.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.orientable_word_handleSwap_to_grouped}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.B.r1 --- displacement measure]
\label{lem:r3subB-B-r1}
For each generator pair \((a_{i},b_{i})\) define
\(d_{i}(w)\) = the absolute difference between the cyclic-list
positions of the two \(a_{i}\)-letters with \(b_{j}\)-letters
\((j\neq i)\) interpolated between them.  Define the total
displacement \(\mu(w)=\sum_{i}d_{i}(w)\).  Then \(\mu(w)\geq 0\),
and \(\mu(w)=0\) iff \(w\) is handle-grouped.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.handleSwap_displacement_measure}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.B.r2 --- HandleSwap decreases \(\mu\)]
\label{lem:r3subB-B-r2}
If \(\mu(w)>0\) then there exists a HandleSwap step
\(w\to_{\mathrm{HS}} v\) with \(\mu(v)<\mu(w)\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.handleSwap_strictly_decreases_mu}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.B.r3 --- well-founded recursion on \(\mu\)]
\label{lem:r3subB-B-r3}
Strong induction on \(\mu(w)\): the base case \(\mu(w)=0\)
identifies \(w\) as handle-grouped; the inductive step uses
\(\mu\)-decrease (r2) plus transitivity of \code{TietzeEq} to
extend the witness chain.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.handleSwap_grouping_via_mu_induction}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.C --- Brahana standardisation]
\label{lem:r3subB-standardisation}
\uses{lem:r3subB-C-r1,lem:r3subB-C-r2,lem:r3subB-C-r3,lem:r3subB-C-r4}
Every handle-grouped orientable edge word \(w\) (no nonorientable
pairs) is HandleSwap-equivalent to \code{standardWord}\(\,g\).  Combined
with R3-sub-B.B and the existing cyclic-reduction theorem
\code{rawWord\_cyclic\_reduction}, this gives the headline
\code{orientable\_edgeWord\_tietzeEq\_standardWord}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.orientable_edgeWord_tietzeEq_standardWord}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.C.r1 --- index permutation by HandleSwap]
\label{lem:r3subB-C-r1}
For every \(\sigma\in S_{g}\) and every handle-grouped word \(w\),
there exists a handle-grouped word \(v\) with the handles permuted
by \(\sigma\) and \(\code{TietzeEq}\,w\,v\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.handleSwap_permutation_realises}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.C.r2 --- canonical handle-block letter order]
\label{lem:r3subB-C-r2}
Within a single handle block \(a_{i}^{\pm}b_{i}^{\pm}a_{i}^{\pm}b_{i}^{\pm}\),
the orientability hypothesis (no nonorientable pairs) forces the
orientation pattern to be \((+,+,-,-)\) up to cyclic rotation; this
is the \code{standardWord}\(\,g\) block letter pattern.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.orientable_handle_block_canonical}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.C.r3 --- canonical block ordering of handles]
\label{lem:r3subB-C-r3}
Combining r1 (permutation realisation) with r2 (canonical block
pattern), every orientable handle-grouped word is HandleSwap-equivalent
to the word with handles in index order \(0,1,\dots,g-1\) and
each block in the canonical \((+,+,-,-)\) letter pattern.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.handleGrouped_canonical_form}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-B.C.r4 --- canonical form equals \code{standardWord}]
\label{lem:r3subB-C-r4}
The canonical form from r3 is definitionally
\(\code{standardWord}\,g
=a_{0}b_{0}a_{0}^{-1}b_{0}^{-1}\dots a_{g-1}b_{g-1}a_{g-1}^{-1}b_{g-1}^{-1}\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.StageA.canonical_form_eq_standardWord}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R3-sub-D --- Homotopy invariance of singular \(H_1\) (prism construction)}
\label{subsec:gap-R3subD-prism}

The headline says: the three remaining
\code{Jacobian/Periods/\{SingularH1Homotopy,Polygon4gCellular,
CellularHomologyRS\}.lean} \code{sorry}s collapse onto a single
classical input --- Hatcher~\S2.1 Lemma~2.10, the
\emph{prism construction} for singular chains --- plus two surface-specific
specialisations of the classical cellular-vs-singular comparison
of \S\ref{subsec:gap-R3subB-stageA-closeout}.  These are the
``functoriality + homotopy invariance'' obligations of the period
pairing dispatch and are upstream of the full surface-classification
chain.

\subsubsection*{Classical content}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Prism / chain homotopy from a continuous homotopy
(Hatcher \S2.1 Lemma~2.10).}  Given continuous \(f, g : X \to Y\) and a
homotopy \(H : f \simeq g\), build a chain homotopy
\(P : C^{\mathrm{sing}}_{*}(X)\to C^{\mathrm{sing}}_{*+1}(Y)\)
satisfying \(\partial P + P \partial = g_{*} - f_{*}\).  The construction
subdivides \(\Delta^{n} \times I\) into \(n+1\) ordered \((n+1)\)-simplices
via the staircase \([v_{0},\dots,v_{i},w_{i},\dots,w_{n}]\)
(lower vertices \(v_{j} = (e_{j}, 0)\), upper vertices \(w_{j} = (e_{j}, 1)\)),
then sums \((-1)^{i}\) of the prism \((n+1)\)-simplices through \(H\).
\item \emph{Hurewicz iso for the polygonal model.}  For path-connected
\(X = \mathrm{Polygon4g}(g+1)\), the Hurewicz map
\(\pi_{1}(X)^{\mathrm{ab}}\to H_{1}(X,\Z)\) is an iso.  Combined with
the surface-group-abelianisation calculation, this gives
\(H_{1}(\mathrm{Polygon4g}(g+1),\Z)\cong\Z^{2(g+1)}\).
\item \emph{Cellular-vs-singular comparison for a compact Riemann
surface.}  Hatcher Theorem~2.35: for any finite CW complex
the cellular and singular chain complexes are quasi-isomorphic.
For a compact connected complex 1-manifold this transports the
finite-free property of cellular \(H_{1}\) to
\code{IntegralOneCycle X}.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

Mathlib v4.28.0 has:
\begin{itemize}
\item \code{Mathlib.AlgebraicTopology.SingularHomology.Basic} ---
  the singular chain complex / homology functors
  \code{singularChainComplexFunctor} and \code{singularHomologyFunctor}.
\item \code{Mathlib.Algebra.Homology.Homotopy} ---
  the abstract chain-complex homotopy structure and
  \code{Homotopy.homologyMap\_eq} (chain-homotopic morphisms
  induce equal maps on homology).
\item \code{Mathlib.Analysis.Convex.StdSimplex} +
  \code{Mathlib.AlgebraicTopology.TopologicalSimplex} ---
  the standard simplex and its barycentric coordinates.
\end{itemize}

Mathlib does \emph{not} have:
\begin{itemize}
\item Any bridge \(\code{ContinuousMap.Homotopy}\,f\,g
  \to \code{HomologicalComplex.Homotopy}\,(C_{*}f)\,(C_{*}g)\) on the
  singular chain complex.  This is exactly the prism construction.
\item The Hurewicz natural transformation \(\pi_{1}^{\mathrm{ab}}\to H_{1}\),
  even abstractly.
\item The cellular--singular comparison theorem (Hatcher~2.35) for
  CW complexes; the project's only formal record is the
  R3-sub-B chain (\S\ref{subsec:gap-R3subB-stageA-closeout}).
\end{itemize}

\subsubsection*{Status: 7 sorries consolidated to 3 leaves}

The original frontier in
\code{Jacobian/Periods/\{SingularH1Homotopy,Polygon4gCellular,
CellularHomologyRS\}.lean} carried \emph{seven} \code{sorry}s
across five declarations.  After replacing the placeholder
opaque \code{singularH1\_inducedLinearMap} with a concrete
definition routed through \code{singularHomologyFunctor (ModuleCat \Z) 1},
four of the seven discharged via direct functor laws (\code{Functor.map\_id},
\code{Functor.map\_comp}, \code{ModuleCat.hom\_id}/\code{hom\_comp})
and the rest by transport along an iso.  The residue is exactly the three
classical inputs above.  The substantive new sorry-free building blocks
live in
\code{Jacobian/Periods/PrismConstruction.lean}
(\(\sim\)511 LOC, fully sorry-free): staircase coordinates, the
continuous staircase map
\code{staircaseMap : C(\(\Delta^{n+1}\),\(\Delta^{n}\)\(\times\)I)},
the prism singular simplex \code{prismSimplex}, plus the top/bottom
face identities \code{prismSimplex\_top\_face} and
\code{prismSimplex\_bottom\_face}.

\begin{theorem}[Classical input: prism + surface-\(H_{1}\) closure]
\label{input:prism-and-surface-h1}
\uses{lem:r3subD-prism-chain-homotopy,lem:r3subD-polygon-hurewicz,lem:r3subD-cellular-singular-surface}
The three Lean targets
\code{singularH1\_inducedLinearMap\_eq\_of\_homotopic},
\code{polygon4g\_succ\_singularH1\_hurewiczIso}, and
\code{cellularH1\_finite\_singularIsoData} bottom out at the three
sub-leaves below.  Sub-leaves
\(\textsf{r3subD-A.r1}\)--\(\textsf{r3subD-A.r3}\) are tracked in
\code{Jacobian/Periods/PrismConstruction.lean}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.prism_and_surface_h1}
\leanok
\end{theorem}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-D.A --- prism construction at the chain level]
\label{lem:r3subD-prism-chain-homotopy}
\uses{lem:r3subD-A-r1,lem:r3subD-A-r2,lem:r3subD-A-r3}
For \(f,g:X\to Y\) and a continuous homotopy \(H:f\simeq g\), the
chain map \((C_{*}f)\) and \((C_{*}g)\) on the singular chain complex
are chain-homotopic via the alternating-sum prism operator
\(P_{n}\sigma=\sum_{i=0}^{n}(-1)^{i}\,\code{prismSimplex}\,n\,i\,H\,\sigma\).
Applying \code{Homotopy.homologyMap\_eq} at degree~1 closes
\code{singularH1\_inducedLinearMap\_eq\_of\_homotopic}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.singularH1_inducedLinearMap_eq_of_homotopic}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-D.A.r1 --- continuous staircase map]
\label{lem:r3subD-A-r1}
For each \(i\in\{0,\dots,n\}\), the affine staircase map
\(\alpha_{i}:\Delta^{n+1}\to\Delta^{n}\times[0,1]\) is continuous,
preserves convex constraints, and corresponds to the staircase simplex
\([v_{0},\dots,v_{i},w_{i},\dots,w_{n}]\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.staircaseMap}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-D.A.r2 --- top and bottom face of the prism simplex]
\label{lem:r3subD-A-r2}
The 0-th face of the \(i=0\) prism simplex equals \(g\circ\sigma\),
and the \((n+1)\)-th face of the \(i=n\) prism simplex equals \(f\circ\sigma\).
These are the boundary contributions of \(\partial P\) that become
\(g_{*}-f_{*}\) after telescoping.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.prismSimplex_top_face}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-D.A.r3 --- chain operator and boundary identity]
\label{lem:r3subD-A-r3}
Lift \code{prismSimplex} to a \(\Z\)-linear chain operator
\(P_{n}:C^{\mathrm{sing}}_{n}(X)\to C^{\mathrm{sing}}_{n+1}(Y)\)
on the free \(\Z\)-module of singular \(n\)-simplices, and verify the
boundary identity \(\partial P + P\partial = (C_{*}g)-(C_{*}f)\) by
the standard interior-face cancellation
(Hatcher \S2.1 p.\,112).  Wrap as
\code{HomologicalComplex.Homotopy}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.prism_chainHomotopy_exists}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-D.B --- Hurewicz iso for the genus-(g+1) polygon]
\label{lem:r3subD-polygon-hurewicz}
\uses{def:polygon4g,lem:r3subB-cellular-iso}
For every \(g\in\N\), the Hurewicz map gives a \(\Z\)-linear iso
\(\Z^{2(g+1)}\cong H_{1}(\mathrm{Polygon4g}(g+1),\Z)\).  Two routes are
available: a direct cellular calculation (3-step chain complex
\(0\to\Z\to\Z^{2(g+1)}\to\Z\to0\) with both differentials zero, then
transport via R3-sub-B) or a Hurewicz / surface-group-abelianisation
argument.  The current Lean target is the cellular route.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.polygon4g_succ_singularH1_hurewiczIso_via_edgeBasis}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R3-sub-D.C --- cellular finite-free witness for a compact Riemann surface]
\label{lem:r3subD-cellular-singular-surface}
\uses{input:rado-triangulation,lem:r3subB-cellular-iso}
For a compact connected complex 1-manifold \(X\) with a finite CW
structure, there exists a finite-rank free \(\Z\)-module \(C\) and a
\(\Z\)-linear iso \(C\cong H_{1}(X,\Z)\).  The witness is the cellular
\(H_{1}\) of the CW structure; the iso is the cellular-vs-singular
comparison of R3-sub-B applied at degree 1.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Periods.cellularH1_finite_singularIsoData}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R8-sub-B --- Banach-data closure for \(\mathrm{Hone}(X)\) (sup-norm + Montel)}
\label{subsec:gap-R8subB-banach-closure}

The headline says: the three frontier sorries in
\code{Jacobian/HolomorphicForms/CompactRiemannSurface.lean}
(\code{holomorphicOneForm\_fiberNorm\_continuous} line 161,
\code{holomorphicOneForm\_supNorm\_cauchySeq\_tendsto} line 229, and
\code{holomorphicOneForm\_closedBall\_totallyBounded} line 656) bottom
out at named Mathlib hooks.  These three feed into the existing
sorry-free assembly that produces a \code{HolomorphicOneFormBanachData
X} witness, which in turn produces the
\code{FiniteDimensional} instance for \code{HolomorphicOneForm}\(\,\C\,X\)
via Riesz on a compact closed unit ball.

R8-sub-B is consumed by R8 via
\code{HolomorphicForms.CompactRiemannSurface.compactRiemannSurface\_finiteDimensionalHolomorphicOneForms}
and underwrites the headline finite-dimensionality theorem
\code{thm:fd-holomorphic-one-forms} of \S2.

\subsubsection*{Classical content}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Fiberwise norm continuity.}  For a smooth section
  \(\sigma\) of a Hermitian vector bundle \(V\to M\), the function
  \(x\mapsto\|\sigma(x)\|\) is continuous: in any local trivialisation
  \(V|_{U}\cong U\times F\), the section reads as a smooth
  \(F\)-valued map and the norm \(F\to\R\) is continuous.  For the
  cotangent bundle on a one-dimensional complex manifold, every
  fibre is canonically isometric to \(\C\to_{\C}\C\cong\C\) via
  evaluation at \(1\).
\item \emph{Sup-norm completeness.}  Let \(\sigma_{n}\) be a sup-norm
  Cauchy sequence in \(\mathrm{Hone}(X)\).  Pointwise it is
  Cauchy in each fibre (a Banach space), so a pointwise limit
  \(\sigma_{\infty}(x)\) exists.  Uniform Cauchy + compactness gives
  uniform convergence \(\sigma_{n}\to\sigma_{\infty}\); the
  limit is continuous.  For \emph{holomorphicity}, Weierstrass's
  uniform-limit-of-holomorphic-is-holomorphic applies in each chart
  via the equivalence with power-series-coefficient convergence.
\item \emph{Closed-ball total boundedness.}  Let \(B\) be the closed
  unit ball in the sup norm.  In every chart \(U_{i}\), the
  family of chart-restricted forms is uniformly bounded, hence
  Cauchy first-derivative estimates make them uniformly Lipschitz,
  hence equicontinuous.  Arzel\`a--Ascoli on the compact base \(X\)
  with a finite chart cover gives: every sequence in \(B\) has a
  uniformly convergent subsequence on \(X\), and that convergent
  subsequence is sup-norm Cauchy.  Equivalently: \(B\) is totally
  bounded in the sup-norm metric.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

Mathlib v4.28.0 has:
\begin{itemize}
\item \code{ContMDiffSection.continuous\_fiberNorm} (in
  \code{Jacobian/HolomorphicForms/SectionFiberNorm.lean}) --- the
  fiberwise norm of a smooth section is continuous given an
  \code{hcompat} witness on the trivialisation.  R8-sub-B.A
  constructs the \code{hcompat} witness for the cotangent
  trivialisation.
\item \code{Mathlib.Topology.UniformSpace.UniformConvergenceTopology}
  --- uniform Cauchy + complete pointwise fibres \(\Rightarrow\) uniform limit
  exists and is continuous.
\item \code{TendstoUniformly.continuous},
  \code{Metric.complete\_of\_cauchySeq\_tendsto}.
\item \code{Mathlib.Analysis.Analytic.IsolatedZeros} and
  \code{Mathlib.Analysis.Analytic.Linear} --- the local theory of
  holomorphic functions used by the Weierstrass step.
\item \code{circleIntegral.norm\_integral\_le\_of\_norm\_le\_const} +
  \code{DiffContOnCl.circleIntegral\_sub\_inv\_smul} --- the Cauchy
  integral form used for chart-derivative estimates.
\item \code{Metric.totallyBounded\_iff} and
  \code{Bornology.IsBounded.totallyBounded} --- the abstract
  total-boundedness API.
\end{itemize}

Mathlib does \emph{not} have:
\begin{itemize}
\item A packaged Weierstrass theorem ``uniform limit of holomorphic
  functions is holomorphic.''  The proof is reduced here to the
  power-series-coefficient convergence form.
\item An Arzel\`a--Ascoli statement specialised to a section bundle
  on a compact manifold.  The proof is reduced here to the chart-local
  Arzel\`a--Ascoli on a compact disc plus a finite chart cover.
\item A direct ``cotangent bundle is fiber-isometrically trivialisable''
  fact.  The proof is reduced here to the chart-induced trivialisation
  pulling back the canonical \(\C\to_{\C}\C\cong\C\) isometry.
\end{itemize}

Estimated 600--900 LOC for a complete API.

\subsubsection*{Recursive sub-gaps surfaced}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{R8-sub-B.A (fiber-isometric trivialisation).}  The
  cotangent trivialisation of a 1D complex manifold is a fibrewise
  \(\C\)-linear isometry.
\item \textbf{R8-sub-B.B (sup-norm Cauchy converges to a holomorphic
  form).}  Pointwise limit + uniform-Cauchy + Weierstrass \(\Rightarrow\) the
  limit is a holomorphic 1-form, and \(\sigma_{n}\) sup-norm
  converges to it.
\item \textbf{R8-sub-B.C (closed ball is totally bounded).}  Cauchy
  estimates on a finite chart cover give equicontinuity; equibounded
  + equicontinuous \(\Rightarrow\) Arzel\`a--Ascoli relatively compact \(\Rightarrow\) totally
  bounded in the sup-norm.
\end{itemize}

\begin{theorem}[Classical input: Banach data for \(\mathrm{Hone}(X)\)]
\label{input:banach-data-hone}
\uses{lem:r8subB-fiber-iso-triv,lem:r8subB-supnorm-cauchy,lem:r8subB-totally-bounded}
The three Lean targets
\code{holomorphicOneForm\_fiberNorm\_continuous},
\code{holomorphicOneForm\_supNorm\_cauchySeq\_tendsto}, and
\code{holomorphicOneForm\_closedBall\_totallyBounded} bottom out
at the three sub-leaves below.  Sub-leaves
\(\textsf{r8subB-A.r1}\)--\(\textsf{r8subB-C.r5}\) are tracked in
\code{Jacobian/HolomorphicForms/CompactRiemannSurface.lean}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.banach_data_hone}
\leanok
\end{theorem}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.A --- fiber-isometric cotangent trivialisation]
\label{lem:r8subB-fiber-iso-triv}
\uses{lem:r8subB-A-r1,lem:r8subB-A-r2}
For the cotangent bundle of a 1D complex manifold modelled on
\(\C\), every chart-induced trivialisation is a fibrewise
\(\C\)-linear isometry, and the fiber norm of any smooth section
factors through the trivialised norm continuously.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.holomorphicOneForm_fiberNorm_continuous}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.A.r1 --- chart-local fiber identification]
\label{lem:r8subB-A-r1}
For every \(x\in X\), the cotangent fibre \((T_{x}^{*}X)_{\C}\) is
canonically isometric to \(\C\to_{\C}\C\cong\C\) via evaluation
at the chart-local \(z\)-coordinate basis vector \(\partial_{z}\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.cotangent_fiber_eval_isometry}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.A.r2 --- trivialisation \code{hcompat} witness]
\label{lem:r8subB-A-r2}
The trivialisation map of the cotangent bundle in any chart commutes
with the canonical fiber isometry of r1; equivalently, for every
section \(\sigma\) and every chart \((e,U)\) with \(x\in U\),
\(\|\sigma(x)\| = \|(e\langle x,\sigma(x)\rangle)_{2}\|\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.cotangent_trivialisation_hcompat}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.B --- sup-norm Cauchy converges]
\label{lem:r8subB-supnorm-cauchy}
\uses{lem:r8subB-B-r1,lem:r8subB-B-r2,lem:r8subB-B-r3,lem:r8subB-B-r4}
Every sup-norm Cauchy sequence in \(\mathrm{Hone}(X)\) converges
to a holomorphic 1-form.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.holomorphicOneForm_supNorm_cauchySeq_tendsto}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.B.r1 --- pointwise Banach limit]
\label{lem:r8subB-B-r1}
A sup-norm Cauchy sequence in \(\mathrm{Hone}(X)\) is pointwise
Cauchy in each Banach fibre; the pointwise limit
\(\sigma_{\infty}(x):=\lim_{n}\sigma_{n}(x)\) exists.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.holomorphicOneForm_pointwise_limit}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.B.r2 --- uniform convergence]
\label{lem:r8subB-B-r2}
Sup-norm Cauchy \(\Rightarrow\) uniform Cauchy on \(X\) (compact); combined
with r1, \(\sigma_{n}\to\sigma_{\infty}\) uniformly.  Hence
\(\sigma_{\infty}\) is continuous (\code{TendstoUniformly.continuous}).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.holomorphicOneForm_tendstoUniformly_continuous}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.B.r3 --- chart-local Weierstrass]
\label{lem:r8subB-B-r3}
In every chart \(U\) (a domain in \(\C\)), the chart-pulled-back
sequence \(f_{n}:U\to\C\) is uniformly Cauchy and each \(f_{n}\) is
holomorphic.  Power-series coefficient convergence gives that the
uniform limit \(f_{\infty}\) has a power series at each point, hence
is holomorphic on \(U\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.chart_local_weierstrass}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.B.r4 --- holomorphicity of the global limit]
\label{lem:r8subB-B-r4}
Apply r3 in every chart of a finite atlas of \(X\); chart
compatibility (preserved under uniform limits) glues to a global
\code{HolomorphicOneForm}\(\,\C\,X\) with \(\sigma_{\infty}\) as
its underlying section.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.holomorphicOneForm_uniform_limit}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.C --- closed unit ball totally bounded]
\label{lem:r8subB-totally-bounded}
\uses{lem:r8subB-C-r1,lem:r8subB-C-r2,lem:r8subB-C-r3,lem:r8subB-C-r4,lem:r8subB-C-r5}
The closed unit ball
\(\overline{B}_{1}\subseteq\mathrm{Hone}(X)\) is totally bounded
in the sup-norm metric.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.holomorphicOneForm_closedBall_totallyBounded}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.C.r1 --- chart-local pointwise bound]
\label{lem:r8subB-C-r1}
Sup-norm \(\leq 1\) \(\Rightarrow\) \(\|\sigma(x)\|\leq 1\) for every \(x\); in
particular every chart-local representative \(f_{n}=\sigma_{n}\circ\phi^{-1}\)
satisfies \(|f_{n}(z)|\leq 1\) on the chart disc.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.chart_local_pointwise_bound}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.C.r2 --- Cauchy first-derivative estimate]
\label{lem:r8subB-C-r2}
On a chart disc \(D_{r}(z_{0})\subseteq U\subseteq\C\), the
Cauchy formula gives \(|f_{n}'(z_{0})|\leq M/r\) where
\(M=\sup_{|w-z_{0}|=r}|f_{n}(w)|\).  Combined with r1's pointwise
bound, this gives \(|f_{n}'(z_{0})|\leq 1/r\), uniform in \(n\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.chart_local_cauchy_derivative_estimate}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.C.r3 --- chart-local equicontinuity]
\label{lem:r8subB-C-r3}
A uniform first-derivative bound on a disc gives uniform Lipschitz
constant via the mean-value theorem; equivalently, the family
\(\{f_{n}\}\) is equicontinuous on every closed sub-disc.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.chart_local_equicontinuous}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.C.r4 --- chart-local Arzel\`a--Ascoli]
\label{lem:r8subB-C-r4}
Equibounded + equicontinuous on a compact subset of \(\C\) \(\Rightarrow\)
relatively compact in the sup-norm topology (Arzel\`a--Ascoli).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.chart_local_arzela_ascoli}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-B.C.r5 --- finite-cover assembly]
\label{lem:r8subB-C-r5}
A finite chart cover of compact \(X\) plus chart-local Arzel\`a--Ascoli
(r4) glue to global total boundedness in the sup-norm metric.
The gluing uses the Lebesgue number of the open cover plus a
diagonal extraction to upgrade chart-by-chart subseq-convergence
to a single subsequence convergent on all of \(X\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.global_totally_bounded_via_chart_cover}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

%======================================================================
\subsection{R8-sub-C --- Riemann--Roch low/high-degree squeeze}
\label{subsec:gap-R8subC-rr-squeeze}

The headline says: the four frontier sorries in
\code{Jacobian/HolomorphicForms/RiemannRoch.lean},
\code{RiemannRochLowDegree.lean}, and
\code{EulerCharLineBundle.lean} bottom out at the named
\(\geq\) and \(\leq\) directions of Riemann's inequality, with the
final theorem the squeeze \(=\).  This is the \emph{abstract} squeeze
shape; concrete content (effective-divisor positivity, Riemann's
inequality, Serre duality on \(L^{-1}\otimes K_{X}\)) is delegated to
existing R8 sub-files.

\subsubsection*{Classical content}

\begin{enumerate}
\item \emph{Negative-degree vanishing.}  A line bundle \(L\) of
  strictly negative degree on a compact connected Riemann surface
  has no nonzero global sections: a nonzero \(s\in H^{0}(X,L)\)
  defines an effective zero divisor \((s)\geq 0\) with
  \(\deg(s)=\deg L<0\), contradicting effectivity.
\item \emph{Riemann's inequality (\(\geq\) direction).}  For every
  line bundle \(L\), \(h^{0}(L)-h^{1}(L)\geq\deg L+1-g\).
  Classical proof: induct on \(\deg L\).  Base case
  \(\deg L=0\): the trivial bundle has \(h^{0}=1,h^{1}=g\) by
  Hodge \(\Rightarrow\) \(h^{0}-h^{1}=1-g\); inductive step uses
  the short exact sequence
  \(0\to L\to L(p)\to\C_{p}\to 0\) and the Euler-characteristic
  additive law to step \(\deg\) up or down by 1.
\item \emph{Serre-duality direction (\(\leq\)).}  Apply Riemann's
  inequality to the dual bundle \(L^{-1}\otimes K_{X}\) (degree
  \(2g-2-\deg L\)), then trade \(h^{0}(L^{-1}\otimes K_{X})=h^{1}(L)\)
  and \(h^{1}(L^{-1}\otimes K_{X})=h^{0}(L)\) via Serre duality.
\item \emph{Squeeze.}  \(\geq\) and \(\leq\) on the same integer
  combine via \code{Int.le\_antisymm} to the Riemann--Roch equality.
\end{enumerate}

\subsubsection*{Lean proof plan}

Mathlib v4.28.0 has:
\begin{itemize}
\item \code{Mathlib.AlgebraicGeometry.Sites.*} --- the abstract
  sheaf-cohomology API used in
  \code{RSSheafCohomology}.
\item \code{Mathlib.LinearAlgebra.Dimension.Finrank} ---
  \code{Module.finrank} on \(\C\)-vector spaces.
\item \code{Int.le\_antisymm} --- the literal squeeze.
\end{itemize}

Mathlib does \emph{not} have:
\begin{itemize}
\item Effective-divisor positivity for global sections of a line
  bundle (\code{globalSection\_yields\_effective\_divisor}).
\item Serre duality in the form
  \(H^{1}(X,L)\cong H^{0}(X,L^{-1}\otimes K_{X})^{*}\) ---
  delegated to the project's
  \code{Jacobian/HolomorphicForms/SerreDualityRS.lean}.
\item The short-exact-sequence argument for Riemann's inequality
  (the \(L\to L(p)\to\C_{p}\) induction).
\end{itemize}

The four frontier sorries are split into named \(\geq\)/\(\leq\)
sub-leaves matching the textbook proof; squeeze is sorry-free in
the \code{h0\_minus\_h1\_eq\_riemann\_roch} assembly.

\subsubsection*{Recursive sub-gaps surfaced}

\begin{itemize}
\item \textbf{R8-sub-C.A (effective-divisor positivity).}  A nonzero
  global section of \(L\) has nonneg divisor; combined with
  \(\deg L<0\), gives \code{riemann\_roch\_low\_degree}.
\item \textbf{R8-sub-C.B (Riemann's \(\geq\) inequality).}  The
  Mittag-Leffler / short-exact-sequence ladder,
  \code{h0\_minus\_h1\_ge\_riemann}.
\item \textbf{R8-sub-C.C (Serre-duality \(\leq\)).}  Dualisation
  via \(L^{-1}\otimes K_{X}\),
  \code{h0\_minus\_h1\_le\_riemann}.
\end{itemize}

\begin{theorem}[Classical input: Riemann--Roch squeeze]
\label{input:rr-squeeze}
\uses{lem:r8subC-low-degree,lem:r8subC-ge,lem:r8subC-le}
The four Lean targets
\code{riemann\_roch\_low\_degree},
\code{h0\_minus\_h1\_ge\_riemann}, and
\code{h0\_minus\_h1\_le\_riemann} bottom out at the three sub-leaves
below; the final
\code{h0\_minus\_h1\_eq\_riemann\_roch} is sorry-free squeeze.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rr_squeeze}
\leanok
\end{theorem}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.A --- low-degree vanishing via effective-divisor positivity]
\label{lem:r8subC-low-degree}
\uses{lem:r8subC-A-r1,lem:r8subC-A-r2}
A line bundle of strictly negative degree on a compact connected
Riemann surface has no nonzero global sections.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.riemann_roch_low_degree}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.A.r1 --- nonzero section yields effective divisor]
\label{lem:r8subC-A-r1}
A nonzero \(s\in H^{0}(X,L)\) defines a divisor \((s)\geq 0\) on \(X\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.section_effective_divisor}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.A.r2 --- divisor degree equals line-bundle degree]
\label{lem:r8subC-A-r2}
\(\deg(s)=\deg L\) for any nonzero \(s\in H^{0}(X,L)\); the
divisor-line-bundle correspondence preserves degree.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.section_degree_eq_lineBundle_degree}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.B --- Riemann's inequality (\(\geq\))]
\label{lem:r8subC-ge}
\uses{lem:r8subC-B-r1,lem:r8subC-B-r2,lem:r8subC-B-r3}
\((h^{0}(L):\Z)-(h^{1}(L):\Z)\geq\deg L+1-g\) for every line bundle
\(L\) on \(X\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.h0_minus_h1_ge_riemann}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.B.r1 --- base case \(\deg L=0\)]
\label{lem:r8subC-B-r1}
For the trivial bundle, \(h^{0}=1,h^{1}=g\); both are computed
from Hodge \(H^{1}(\mathcal{O}_{X})\cong H^{0}(K_{X})^{*}\) and
\(\dim H^{0}(\mathcal{O}_{X})=1\) on a connected compact RS.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.h0_minus_h1_trivial_bundle}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.B.r2 --- Euler-char additivity SES]
\label{lem:r8subC-B-r2}
The short exact sequence \(0\to L\to L(p)\to\C_{p}\to 0\) gives
\(\chi(L(p))=\chi(L)+1\) (the skyscraper sheaf \(\C_{p}\) has
\(\chi=1\)).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.eulerChar_additive_ses_point}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.B.r3 --- induction on \(\deg L\)]
\label{lem:r8subC-B-r3}
Strong induction on \(|\deg L|\) using r1 (base) and r2 (inductive
step) gives \(\chi(L)=\deg L+1-g\), i.e.\
\(h^{0}(L)-h^{1}(L)=\deg L+1-g\); the \(\geq\) direction follows.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.h0_minus_h1_ge_via_induction}

\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.C --- Serre-duality squeeze (\(\leq\))]
\label{lem:r8subC-le}
\uses{lem:r8subC-C-r1,lem:r8subC-C-r2,lem:r8subC-C-r3}
\((h^{0}(L):\Z)-(h^{1}(L):\Z)\leq\deg L+1-g\) for every line bundle
\(L\) on \(X\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.h0_minus_h1_le_riemann}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.C.r1 --- dual bundle degree]
\label{lem:r8subC-C-r1}
\label{lem:rs-dualizing-degree}
\(\deg(L^{-1}\otimes K_{X})=2g-2-\deg L\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.dual_bundle_degree, JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.RSLineBundleDegree_dual_tensor_canonical}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.C.r2 --- Serre-duality identification]
\label{lem:r8subC-C-r2}
\(h^{0}(L^{-1}\otimes K_{X})=h^{1}(L)\) and
\(h^{1}(L^{-1}\otimes K_{X})=h^{0}(L)\) via the Serre pairing
non-degeneracy.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.serre_duality_h0_h1_swap}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[R8-sub-C.C.r3 --- application of (\(\geq\)) to the dual bundle]
\label{lem:r8subC-C-r3}
\label{thm:rr-high-degree}
Apply r-r3 of R8-sub-C.B to \(L^{-1}\otimes K_{X}\); rewrite via
r1 (degree) and r2 (Serre swap) to land at the \(\leq\) statement
on \(L\).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.h0_minus_h1_le_via_dual, JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.riemann_roch_high_degree_via_serre}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

%======================================================================
\subsection{Summary of recursive sub-gaps}
\label{subsec:gap-summary}

The eight-node tree, when expanded one level into recursive sub-gaps,
surfaces a roughly 25-node graph.  Several sub-gaps are shared
across multiple parent nodes (the bundled \(\Omega^k\) package
appears under R4, R5, and R7; the Riemannian metric appears under R4
and R5; the abstract simplicial complex appears under R1 and R3).
A consolidated estimate of the total Lean-formalisation cost,
including all shared sub-gaps counted once, is:

\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{lr}
\textbf{Component} & \textbf{Estimated LOC} \\\hline
R1 + R1-sub-\{A,B,C\} & 2000--2700 \\
R2 + R2-sub-\{A,B,C\} & 900--1100 \\
R3 + R3-sub-\{A,B,C\} & 1500--2000 \\
R4 (modulo R9) & 1500--2000 \\
R5 (modulo R9, R10) + R5-sub-\{A,E\} & 1700--2500 \\
R6 + R6-sub-\{A,B,C\} & 1100--1400 \\
R7 (modulo R9, R10) + R7-sub-\{B,C,D\} & 1300--1700 \\
R8 + R8-sub-\{A,B,C,D\} & 3300--4300 \\
R9 + R9-sub-\{A,B,C\} & 800--1200 \\
R10 + R10-sub-\{A,B,C,D,E\} & 4500--6500 \\\hline
\textbf{Total (with shared deduplication)} & \textbf{18000--25000 LOC} \\
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

The dominant single component is R10 (Sobolev / elliptic regularity for
forms on a manifold), now its own dep-graph node, estimated at
2500--4000 LOC for the headline plus 2000--2500 LOC for sub-gaps.
R10 is on the critical path for R5 and (transitively) R7 + R8.

R9 (bundled \(\Omega^{k}\)) is the second largest piece of shared
infrastructure, on the critical path for R4, R5, and R7 simultaneously.

R6 remains the most \emph{blocked}: it depends on R4, R5, and R7
together, so it cannot land until all three are deep enough to expose
their output statements.  R3 remains the most \emph{ready}: its Lean
infrastructure is already largely in place.

\bigskip

\begin{layman}
Adding it all up: the eight major analysis gaps, expanded one level
into their internal sub-gaps, total around fifteen to twenty-two
thousand lines of Lean.  That's a substantial fraction of the entire
project but it's a knowable one --- every node is named, every
dependency is identified, every sub-gap has at least a placeholder
Lean target.  The single biggest cost driver is \emph{Sobolev spaces
of forms on a manifold plus elliptic regularity} (R5-sub-B), which
underpins the Hodge decomposition (R5) and indirectly the Dolbeault
proof (R7).  Once that's in hand, much of the rest cascades.

The other large cost is \emph{bundled differential forms}
(R4-sub-A): a \(C^\infty(M)\)-module \(\Omega^k(M)\) with all the
expected operators (\(d\), \(\wedge\), pullback) simultaneously
linear, natural, and compatible.  Mathlib has the pieces
(\code{MFDeriv}, exterior algebra in finite dimensions, manifold
charts) but no integrated bundled form package; this is shared
infrastructure across R4, R5, and R7.

Among the eight, R6 is the smallest in itself but the most
\emph{blocked}: it depends on R4, R5, and R7 simultaneously, so it
cannot be touched until all three are deep enough to expose their
output statements.  R3, by contrast, is the most \emph{ready}: its
Lean infrastructure is already largely in place, blocked mainly on
R1 (Rad\'o) and R2 (Tietze).  A pragmatic first move would be to
formalise R1 + R2 + R3 as a topology-only sub-project, in parallel
with R4-sub-A (bundled \(\Omega^k\)) and R5-sub-A (Riemannian
metric) as foundational analytic infrastructure.  Both of those
unblock the rest of the analytic chain.
\end{layman}

\subsection{Frontier gap analysis: 5-pass refinement of leaf nodes}
\label{subsec:frontier-five-pass}

The dependency graph still has periphery leaves whose proofs reduce
to classical analysis without an immediate Mathlib match.  This
subsection picks one leaf per major gap area (R1 Rad\'o, R4 de Rham,
R7 Dolbeault, R8 Serre, R10 Sobolev) and refines it five levels
deep.  Each pass replaces the bare statement with a proof that
depends on a smaller sub-statement (still \texttt{\textbackslash notready}),
so the depth of the chain measures how far a frontier leaf is from
ordinary Mathlib.

In every chain below, pass~5 lands on a statement that either
\emph{is} in Mathlib already or is one named declaration away.

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain B: Rellich--Kondrachov compactness}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B.1: localize via partition of unity on a compact manifold]
\label{lem:rk-r1-partition-localize}
\uses{lem:rk-r2-local-flat}
Compactness of $H^{s'}(M) \hookrightarrow H^{s}(M)$ on a compact
$M$ reduces to compactness of finitely many local embeddings
$H^{s'}(B^{n}_{1}) \hookrightarrow H^{s}(B^{n}_{1})$ via a smooth
finite partition of unity subordinate to a chart cover.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rk_r1_partition_localize}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B.2: local case via Fourier extension to $\R^{n}$]
\label{lem:rk-r2-local-flat}
\uses{lem:rk-r3-fourier-characterization}
Every bounded family in $H^{s'}_{c}(B^{n}_{1})$ extends by
zero to a bounded family in $H^{s'}(\R^{n})$, so the local case
follows from compactness of the embedding $H^{s'}(\R^{n})
\cap \{\mathrm{supp} \subseteq K\} \hookrightarrow H^{s}(\R^{n})$
for $K$ compact.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rk_r2_local_flat}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B.3: Fourier characterization of $H^{s}(\R^{n})$]
\label{lem:rk-r3-fourier-characterization}
\uses{lem:rk-r4-truncation-compact}
$H^{s}(\R^{n}) = \{ u \in \mathcal{S}'(\R^{n}) :
(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s/2}\,\hat u \in L^{2}(\R^{n})\}$.  Compactness
on functions with support in $K$ then reduces to compactness of
the truncated embedding via Fourier multipliers.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rk_r3_fourier_characterization}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B.4: high-frequency truncation gives compact embedding]
\label{lem:rk-r4-truncation-compact}
\uses{lem:rk-r5-tail-decay}
For $\chi_{N}$ the indicator of $\{|\xi| \leq N\}$,
$u \mapsto \mathcal{F}^{-1}(\chi_{N} \hat u)$ has finite-rank
range on a fixed compact-support family (Paley--Wiener), and the
remainder $u - \chi_{N} u$ has $H^{s}$-norm bounded by
$N^{-(s'-s)} \|u\|_{H^{s'}}$, which tends to $0$ as $N \to
\infty$.  Hence the embedding is approximated in operator norm
by finite-rank operators, making it compact.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rk_r4_truncation_compact}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B.5: tail decay in weighted $L^{2}$ is monotone convergence]
\label{lem:rk-r5-tail-decay}
$\int_{|\xi| > N} (1+|\xi|^{2})^{s} |\hat u(\xi)|^{2}\,d\xi
\to 0$ as $N \to \infty$ for $\hat u \in L^{2}(\R^{n};
(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s'} d\xi)$ and $s' > s$, by dominated
convergence on the integrand $(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s-s'} \cdot
(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s'} |\hat u|^{2}$.  Mathlib gap: weighted
$L^{2}$ tail estimate;
\code{MeasureTheory.tendsto\_setIntegral\_compl} on a
$\sigma$-finite measure is the intended target.
\uses{lem:rk-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rk_r5_tail_decay}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain C: Doyle--Moran PL approximation in dim 2}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C.1: reduce to the disk Schoenflies theorem]
\label{lem:rado-dim2-r1-disk-schoenflies}
\uses{lem:rado-dim2-r2-schoenflies-jordan}
Uniform PL approximation of an arbitrary planar homeomorphism
on a compact set reduces (via local charts and a finite open
cover) to the case of a homeomorphism of the closed disk to a
Jordan domain --- i.e.\ to Schoenflies' theorem on disks.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rado_dim2_r1_disk_schoenflies}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C.2: Schoenflies on disks via Jordan-curve arc-length parameterization]
\label{lem:rado-dim2-r2-schoenflies-jordan}
\uses{lem:rado-dim2-r3-jordan-curve-theorem}
A homeomorphism $\overline{D} \to \Omega$ to a Jordan domain
extends from a PL approximation of the boundary Jordan curve to
a PL approximation of the whole disk.  This depends on the
Jordan curve theorem to identify $\Omega$ as the bounded
component.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rado_dim2_r2_schoenflies_jordan}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C.3: Jordan curve theorem in $\R^{2}$]
\label{lem:rado-dim2-r3-jordan-curve-theorem}
\uses{lem:rado-dim2-r4-winding-degree}
Every simple closed curve in $\R^{2}$ separates the plane into
exactly two connected components, exactly one of which is
bounded.  Proof via degree theory: for $p$ off the curve, the
winding number is well-defined and takes values $0$ or $\pm 1$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rado_dim2_r3_jordan_curve_theorem}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C.4: winding number via degree on $S^{1}$]
\label{lem:rado-dim2-r4-winding-degree}
\uses{lem:rado-dim2-r5-pi1-circle}
For a continuous loop $\gamma : S^{1} \to \C \setminus \{p\}$,
its winding number around $p$ equals the degree of the induced
map $S^{1} \to S^{1}$ obtained by normalizing
$(\gamma(t)-p)/|\gamma(t)-p|$.
\lean{Complex.windingNumber}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C.5: $\pi_{1}(S^{1}) = \Z$]
On the circle $S^{1}$, the fundamental group is $\Z$, with
generator the identity loop.  Mathlib status: present;
\code{Topology.Homotopy.Fundamental.Circle} provides
\code{fundamentalGroup\_circle\_iso\_int}.  This is the
Mathlib endpoint of the chain.
\label{lem:rado-dim2-r5-pi1-circle}
\lean{Topology.Homotopy.fundamentalGroup_circle_iso_int}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain E: Existence of a good cover}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E.1: cover by geodesically convex normal balls]
\label{lem:gce-r1-convex-normal-cover}
\uses{lem:gce-r2-convex-intersection,lem:gce-r3-convex-diffeo-ball}
Pick a Riemannian metric $g$ on $M$ and, at each point $p$, a
normal-coordinate ball $B_{p}$ of radius less than the
\emph{convexity radius}.  Each $B_{p}$ is geodesically convex.
Refining to a locally finite subcover gives a cover $\{U_{i}\}$
where every nonempty finite intersection $U_{i_{1}} \cap \cdots
\cap U_{i_{k}}$ is geodesically convex (Lemma~\ref{lem:gce-r2-convex-intersection})
hence contractible (Lemma~\ref{lem:gce-r3-convex-diffeo-ball}).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.gce_r1_convex_normal_cover}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E.2: finite intersections of geodesically convex sets are convex]
\label{lem:gce-r2-convex-intersection}
\uses{lem:gce-r4-riemannian-metric-exists}
If $U, V \subseteq M$ are geodesically convex, so is $U \cap V$:
for $p, q \in U \cap V$, the unique minimizing geodesic from $p$
to $q$ lies in both $U$ and $V$.
\lean{GeodesicallyConvex}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E.3: a geodesically convex set is diffeomorphic to a ball]
\label{lem:gce-r3-convex-diffeo-ball}
\uses{lem:gce-r4-riemannian-metric-exists}
The exponential map $\exp_{p}$ at any interior point $p$ of a
geodesically convex set $U$ is a diffeomorphism from
$\exp_{p}^{-1}(U) \subseteq T_{p}M$ (which is a star-shaped
open subset of a vector space) onto $U$.  Hence $U$ is
contractible.
\lean{Manifold.exp}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E.4: every smooth manifold admits a Riemannian metric]
\label{lem:gce-r4-riemannian-metric-exists}
\uses{lem:gce-r5-smooth-pou}
Glue chart-local Euclidean inner products on the tangent bundle
via a smooth partition of unity to obtain a positive-definite
section of $\mathrm{Sym}^{2} T^{*} M$.
\lean{RiemannianMetric}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E.5: smooth partitions of unity exist on a paracompact smooth manifold]
\label{lem:gce-r5-smooth-pou}
Every locally finite open cover of a paracompact smooth
manifold admits a subordinate smooth partition of unity.
Mathlib status: present;
\code{SmoothManifoldWithCorners.SmoothPartitionOfUnity.exists\_isSubordinate}
is the named declaration.  This is the Mathlib endpoint.
\lean{SmoothManifoldWithCorners.SmoothPartitionOfUnity.exists_isSubordinate}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{layman}
This subsection makes the gap-to-Mathlib quantitative: each of
five frontier leaves has been refined five steps deeper, and at
the bottom of each chain the very last sub-statement is a named
Mathlib declaration (or one chart-localization away from one).
A leaf at depth-5 means a single Aristotle-style sub-project of
roughly 200--500 lines of Lean once the chain is unfolded into
forward declarations.  Most chains converge on the same handful
of Mathlib hooks: smooth partitions of unity, polar
change-of-variables, Fourier transform of tempered
distributions, fundamental group of $S^{1}$.  These four
endpoints are where the entire frontier of the project meets
ordinary Mathlib.
\end{layman}

\subsection{Frontier gap analysis: extended 5-pass refinements}
\label{subsec:frontier-five-pass-extended}

This subsection extends the 5-pass refinement methodology to the
remaining 48 leaves of the dependency graph.  The same pattern
applies: each chain refines a leaf five levels deep, and pass~5
either lands on a named Mathlib declaration or explicitly flags
the gap as ABSENT (no Mathlib hook yet) / partial (some pieces
exist).  The chains are organized by area (sections of this
document or sub-gaps R1--R10).

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain F1: Holomorphic $k$-th root (lem:analytic-kth-root)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1.1: reduce to a holomorphic logarithm]
\label{lem:akr-r1}
\uses{lem:akr-r2}
$h := \exp((1/k)\log g)$ produces the desired root once $\log g$ is well-defined on a small disk avoiding $0$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.akr_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1.2: logarithm exists on a simply-connected nbhd avoiding $0$]
\label{lem:akr-r2}
\uses{lem:akr-r3}
On any simply-connected open $U \subseteq \C \setminus \{0\}$, $\log : U \to \C$ is holomorphic.  Reduces to existence of a primitive of $1/z$.
\lean{Complex.analyticAt_log}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1.3: primitive on simply-connected domain]
\label{lem:akr-r3}
\uses{lem:akr-r4}
On a simply-connected open in $\C$, every holomorphic function has a holomorphic primitive (Cauchy's theorem on simply-connected domains).
\lean{Mathlib.Analysis.Complex.CauchyIntegral}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1.4: Cauchy's theorem on a simply-connected domain]
\label{lem:akr-r4}
\uses{lem:akr-r5}
For $f$ holomorphic on a simply-connected open $U$, every closed loop in $U$ has $\oint f\,dz = 0$.  Reduces by Stokes to $df = 0$ holomorphic $\Rightarrow$ closed.
\lean{Mathlib.Analysis.Complex.CauchyIntegral}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1.5: Mathlib endpoint: $\log$ on a simply-connected nbhd avoiding $0$]
\label{lem:akr-r5}
\code{Complex.analyticAt\_log} provides $\log$ analytic at any point of $\C \setminus \{0\}$; combined with simply-connectedness this gives the global $\log$.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{Complex.analyticAt_log}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain F2: Properness of fibre below an open neighborhood (lem:proper-fiber-shrink)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F2.1: complement of $U$ is compact]
\label{lem:pfs-r1}
\uses{lem:pfs-r2}
$U^{c}$ is closed in the compact source, hence compact.
\lean{IsClosed.isCompact}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F2.2: image of a compact set is compact]
\label{lem:pfs-r2}
\uses{lem:pfs-r3}
$f(U^{c})$ is compact in the Hausdorff target $Y$.
\lean{IsCompact.image}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F2.3: compact subsets of Hausdorff are closed]
\label{lem:pfs-r3}
\uses{lem:pfs-r4}
$f(U^{c})$ is closed in $Y$.
\lean{IsCompact.isClosed}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F2.4: $y_{0}$ avoids the closed set $f(U^{c})$]
\label{lem:pfs-r4}
\uses{lem:pfs-r5}
By hypothesis $f^{-1}(y_{0}) \subseteq U$, so $y_{0} \notin f(U^{c})$.  The complement $V := Y \setminus f(U^{c})$ is open and contains $y_{0}$; for $y \in V$, $f^{-1}(y) \subseteq U$.
\lean{Set.compl}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F2.5: Mathlib endpoint: closed-image-of-compact under continuous-Hausdorff]
\label{lem:pfs-r5}
\code{IsCompact.image} and \code{IsCompact.isClosed} (the latter on T2 spaces) compose to the needed fact.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{IsCompact.image_of_continuousOn}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain F7: Complex-torus package: $V/\Lambda$ is a compact complex Lie group (prop:complex-torus-package)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F7.1: quotient inherits AddCommGroup]
\label{lem:ctp-r1}
\uses{lem:ctp-r2}
$V/\Lambda$ is the quotient of an abelian group by a subgroup, so the quotient is an abelian group via the universal property.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ctp_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F7.2: quotient inherits topology]
\label{lem:ctp-r2}
\uses{lem:ctp-r3}
Equip $V/\Lambda$ with the quotient topology of the projection $\pi : V \to V/\Lambda$.  $\pi$ is open, so this gives a topological group structure.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ctp_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F7.3: quotient is Hausdorff and compact]
\label{lem:ctp-r3}
\uses{lem:ctp-r4}
$\Lambda$ closed and discrete in $V \cong \C^{g}$, so $V/\Lambda$ is Hausdorff.  Choose a fundamental parallelepiped $P$ for $\Lambda$; $\pi$ is surjective $P \to V/\Lambda$ with $P$ compact, hence the quotient is compact.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ctp_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F7.4: complex chart at every point]
\label{lem:ctp-r4}
\uses{lem:ctp-r5}
Locally $\pi$ is a homeomorphism (since $\Lambda$ is discrete), so it pulls back a complex chart from $V$.  Charts at different points are related by translations, which are biholomorphic.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ctp_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F7.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:ctp-r5}
\code{QuotientAddGroup.instTopologicalGroup} + \code{ChartedSpace.instOfHomeomorph} + \code{ComplexManifold} smooth-structure transfer.  Mathlib status: partial (charted-space transfer along an open quotient is the missing piece).
\uses{lem:ctp-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ctp_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain F8: Pullback of holomorphic 1-forms along a holomorphic map (lem:pullback-forms)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F8.1: define $f^{*}\omega$ chart-locally]
\label{lem:pbf-r1}
\uses{lem:pbf-r2}
In holomorphic charts $w$ on $X$ and $z$ on $Y$, write $\omega = g(z)\,dz$ and $f$ as $z = F(w)$ holomorphic.  Define $f^{*}\omega := g(F(w))\,F'(w)\,dw$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.pbf_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F8.2: chart-independence of the pullback]
\label{lem:pbf-r2}
\uses{lem:pbf-r3}
Under change of holomorphic chart $w' = \varphi(w)$, the chain rule gives $f^{*}\omega$ the correct transformation, so the chart-local formula glues to a global section of $f^{*}\Omega^{1}_{Y}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.pbf_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F8.3: naturality on overlaps reduces to the chain rule]
\label{lem:pbf-r3}
\uses{lem:pbf-r4}
On chart overlaps, the pullback transforms via $(F \circ \varphi)' = F'(\varphi)\cdot\varphi'$.  Same on the other side via the cocycle condition for $\Omega^{1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.pbf_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F8.4: chain rule for holomorphic functions]
\label{lem:pbf-r4}
\uses{lem:pbf-r5}
$(g \circ F)'(w) = g'(F(w)) \cdot F'(w)$ for holomorphic $g, F$, by the complex differentiability.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.pbf_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F8.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:pbf-r5}
\code{HasDerivAt.comp} and \code{ContMDiff.compMDifferentiable} provide the chart-local + manifold-level chain rules.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.MathlibEndpoints.hasDerivAt_comp_chainRule}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain DR: de Rham comparison and path integration (lem:period-homology-invariance)}

\begin{lemma}[Stokes gap: integration along singular boundaries]
\label{lem:stokes-gap-integration-kills-boundary}
The integral of any holomorphic 1-form along a singular 1-cycle that bounds a singular 2-chain is zero.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Sec03.chain_integration_kills_boundary}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Path-integral primitive on a chart disk]
\label{lem:path-integral-primitive}
A closed 1-form on a chart-disk has a primitive defined by path integration.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.closedForm_pathIntegral_primitive, JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.closedForm_pathIntegral_primitive_derivative,closedForm_pathIntegral_primitive_exists}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Integration equivalence: Cech vs.\ path]
\label{lem:integral-cech-path-equivalence}
The Cech-derived integral of a closed 1-form equals its path integral.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.HolomorphicForms.integral_closed_form_from_cech_eq}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Chain RH: Riemann--Hurwitz formula (thm:riemann-hurwitz-formula)}

\begin{lemma}[Riemann--Hurwitz formula]
\label{thm:riemann-hurwitz-formula}
For a nonconstant holomorphic map $f : X \to Y$ of degree $d$ between compact Riemann surfaces,
$2 g_{X} - 2 = d \cdot (2 g_{Y} - 2) + \deg R$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.AbelExistence.RiemannHurwitzDeg1.riemann_hurwitz_formula}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Degree-1 map has zero ramification]
\label{lem:ramification-zero-of-deg-one}
A holomorphic map of degree 1 has no ramification points.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.AbelExistence.RiemannHurwitzDeg1.ramification_zero_of_deg_one}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Chain F9: Trace of a holomorphic 1-form along a finite branched cover (lem:trace-forms)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F9.1: define $\mathrm{tr}\,\omega$ on the unbranched locus]
\label{lem:trf-r1}
\uses{lem:trf-r2}
Off the branch locus, $f : X \to Y$ is an unramified cover of degree $d$.  Define $(\mathrm{tr}\,\omega)(y) := \sum_{x \in f^{-1}(y)} \omega_{x}$ in pulled-back local coordinates.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.traceForm_on_unbranchedLocus}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F9.2: trace extends across the branch locus]
\label{lem:trf-r2}
\uses{lem:trf-r3}
Near a ramified point with index $k$, the $k$ sheets coalesce; the sum of $\omega$ over the fiber extends continuously (and holomorphically) to a 1-form on $Y$ via the $k$-th power expansion.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.traceForm_extends_across_branchLocus}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F9.3: local trace formula in branched coordinates]
\label{lem:trf-r3}
\uses{lem:trf-r4}
In coordinates $w = z^{k}$ near a branch point, $\sum_{j=0}^{k-1} f(\zeta_{k}^{j} z)\,d(\zeta_{k}^{j} z) = k \cdot f^{\#}(w)\,dw$ for $f^{\#}(w) := \frac{1}{k}\sum_{j} f(\zeta_{k}^{j} w^{1/k})$ holomorphic in $w$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.localTraceFormula_branchedCoordinates}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F9.4: Newton symmetric-function theorem]
\label{lem:trf-r4}
\uses{lem:trf-r5}
Symmetric functions in $\zeta_{k}^{j} z^{1/k}$ that are smooth in the input are smooth in $w = z^{k}$.  Reduces to the Newton identities expressing power sums in elementary symmetric polynomials.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.newtonSymmetricFunction_reduction}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F9.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:trf-r5}
\code{MvPolynomial.symmetric\_subalgebra} is Mathlib-present in the polynomial setting; the analytic upgrade for power series is the named declaration we need.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:trf-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.symmetricPolynomial_endpoint_partial}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain B1: Finite disk atlas exists (compactness) (lem:rado-finite-disk-atlas)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B1.1: cover by chart neighborhoods]
\label{lem:rfd-r1}
\uses{lem:rfd-r2}
Every point of $X$ has a chart $\varphi_{p} : U_{p} \to \R^{2}$.  Restricting to $V_{p} \subset U_{p}$ with $\overline{V_{p}}$ compactly contained gives an open cover by relatively compact disk-like sets.
\lean{ChartedSpace.atlas}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B1.2: compactness extracts a finite subcover]
\label{lem:rfd-r2}
\uses{lem:rfd-r3}
$X$ compact, so $\{V_{p}\}$ admits a finite subcover $\{V_{1}, \ldots, V_{N}\}$.
\lean{IsCompact.elim_finite_subcover}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B1.3: disk shapes preserved on overlaps]
\label{lem:rfd-r3}
\uses{lem:rfd-r4}
Pre-images $\varphi_{i}(V_{i}) \subseteq \R^{2}$ are smooth disks; overlap regions are smooth-diffeomorphic via the transition maps $\varphi_{j}\circ\varphi_{i}^{-1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rfd_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B1.4: paracompactness of compact 2-manifolds]
\label{lem:rfd-r4}
\uses{lem:rfd-r5}
Every compact $C^{0}$-manifold is paracompact; we just used compactness, but the subordinate finite cover argument works under weaker paracompactness.
\lean{TopologicalSpace.IsParacompact}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rfd-r5}
\code{IsCompact.elim\_finite\_subcover} and \code{ChartedSpace.atlas} are the Mathlib hooks.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{IsCompact.elim_finite_subcover}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain B2: PL cocycle preservation under chart modification (lem:rado-pl-cocycle-preservation)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B2.1: PL transition functions form a cocycle]
\label{lem:rpc-r1}
\uses{lem:rpc-r2}
On overlaps $U_{i}\cap U_{j}\cap U_{k}$ the transition maps $\varphi_{ij}, \varphi_{jk}, \varphi_{ki}$ satisfy $\varphi_{ki}\circ\varphi_{jk}\circ\varphi_{ij} = \mathrm{id}$.  Modifying $\varphi_{i}$ by a PL homeomorphism $\psi$ changes only $\varphi_{ij}$ to $\varphi_{ij}\circ\psi^{-1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rpc_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B2.2: composition with a PL map preserves PL]
\label{lem:rpc-r2}
\uses{lem:rpc-r3}
PL maps are closed under composition: $f, g$ both piecewise linear $\Rightarrow$ $f\circ g$ piecewise linear with finitely many regions.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rpc_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B2.3: PL composition refines the simplicial decomposition]
\label{lem:rpc-r3}
\uses{lem:rpc-r4}
$f\circ g$ admits a common simplicial subdivision: take the simplicial preimage of $g$'s decomposition under $f^{-1}$, then refine.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rpc_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B2.4: simplicial complex refinement existence]
\label{lem:rpc-r4}
\uses{lem:rpc-r5}
Any two finite simplicial decompositions of a region in $\R^{2}$ admit a common refinement (e.g.\ via the union of all simplex boundaries).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rpc_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B2.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rpc-r5}
PL infrastructure is currently absent from Mathlib.  Closest hooks: \code{Mathlib.Analysis.Convex.Simplex} for simplices and \code{AffineMap} for affine maps.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:rpc-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rpc_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain B3: Triangulate each chart (lem:rado-triangulate-each-chart)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B3.1: standard triangulation of a planar disk]
\label{lem:rtc-r1}
\uses{lem:rtc-r2}
The standard closed disk $\overline{B^{2}}$ admits an explicit triangulation, e.g.\ by radial wedges from the center plus circular arcs.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rtc_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B3.2: transport triangulation through chart homeomorphism]
\label{lem:rtc-r2}
\uses{lem:rtc-r3}
For chart $\varphi : U \to D$, pull back the standard triangulation via $\varphi^{-1}$; this gives a topological triangulation of $U$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rtc_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B3.3: piecewise-linearity of the transported triangulation]
\label{lem:rtc-r3}
\uses{lem:rtc-r4}
After applying the local PL approximation (Doyle--Moran), the transported triangulation has PL transitions between charts.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rtc_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B3.4: subdivision to match overlap data]
\label{lem:rtc-r4}
\uses{lem:rtc-r5}
Refine each chart's triangulation finely enough that overlaps land within sub-simplices, enabling chart-by-chart gluing.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rtc_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B3.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rtc-r5}
\code{Topology.Homotopy.Triangulation} is the natural target; the relevant simplicial-complex API is currently a project-side fork.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:rtc-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rtc_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain B4: Common subdivision over overlaps (lem:rado-common-subdivision)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B4.1: two triangulations of the same disk admit a common refinement]
\label{lem:rcs-r1}
\uses{lem:rcs-r2}
Any two triangulations $\mathcal{T}_{1}, \mathcal{T}_{2}$ of a closed disk admit a common subdivision $\mathcal{T}$, refining both.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rcs_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B4.2: planar arrangement of edges]
\label{lem:rcs-r2}
\uses{lem:rcs-r3}
Take the union of all 1-cells of $\mathcal{T}_{1}$ and $\mathcal{T}_{2}$ as a planar 1-complex.  Each face of the resulting arrangement is a polygon, triangulable in finitely many ways.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rcs_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B4.3: polygon triangulation by ear-cutting]
\label{lem:rcs-r3}
\uses{lem:rcs-r4}
Every simple polygon admits a triangulation, e.g.\ by repeatedly cutting an `ear' (a triangle whose third edge is internal).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rcs_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B4.4: ear-existence theorem for simple polygons]
\label{lem:rcs-r4}
\uses{lem:rcs-r5}
Every simple polygon with $\geq 4$ vertices has at least two ears.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rcs_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B4.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rcs-r5}
Polygon ear-theorem is computational geometry; not in current Mathlib.  Closest: \code{Polygon} basic API in Mathlib3 not yet ported.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:rcs-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rcs_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain B5: Edge condition: each 1-simplex in two 2-simplices (lem:rado-edges-in-two-triangles)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B5.1: local 2-manifold structure $\Rightarrow$ each edge has two sides]
\label{lem:ret-r1}
\uses{lem:ret-r2}
At any interior edge $e$ of a triangulation of a 2-manifold, a small neighborhood of $e$ is homeomorphic to $\R^{2}$, hence has exactly two sides.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ret_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B5.2: each side is a triangle]
\label{lem:ret-r2}
\uses{lem:ret-r3}
In a finite triangulation, the only 2-cells incident to $e$ are triangles, and the local 2-manifold condition forces exactly one triangle on each side.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ret_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B5.3: non-boundary edges of a closed manifold lie in exactly two triangles]
\label{lem:ret-r3}
\uses{lem:ret-r4}
For a closed (boundaryless) 2-manifold, every edge is interior and so every edge is in exactly two triangles.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ret_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B5.4: local Euclidean structure gives a 2-disk neighborhood of an edge]
\label{lem:ret-r4}
\uses{lem:ret-r5}
By the manifold chart at a midpoint of $e$, a neighborhood is homeomorphic to $\R^{2}$, in which an edge separates the plane into two pieces (Jordan-arc theorem).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ret_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B5.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:ret-r5}
\code{Topology.JordanCurve} (planned) for the arc-separation step.  Mathlib status: ABSENT (Jordan arc theorem in Mathlib).
\uses{lem:ret-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ret_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain B7: Glued chart map is continuous (lem:rado-glue-continuous)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B7.1: chart maps are continuous on each chart]
\label{lem:rgc-r1}
\uses{lem:rgc-r2}
By definition a chart $\varphi_{i} : U_{i} \to \R^{2}$ is a homeomorphism, so continuous.
\lean{LocalHomeomorph.continuous}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B7.2: compatibility on overlaps]
\label{lem:rgc-r2}
\uses{lem:rgc-r3}
On $U_{i}\cap U_{j}$, $\varphi_{i}$ and $\varphi_{j}$ are related by a PL transition $\varphi_{ji}\circ\varphi_{i}$, which is continuous.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgc_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B7.3: gluing continuous maps over an open cover]
\label{lem:rgc-r3}
\uses{lem:rgc-r4}
A function $f : X \to Y$ defined on a finite open cover $\{U_{i}\}$ via continuous local pieces $f_{i}$, agreeing on overlaps, is continuous.
\lean{continuous_iff_continuousOn_iUnion_of_isOpen}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B7.4: pasting lemma for continuity]
\label{lem:rgc-r4}
\uses{lem:rgc-r5}
For an open cover $\{U_{i}\}$ of $X$, $f$ is continuous iff each $f|_{U_{i}}$ is continuous.
\lean{continuous_iff_continuousOn_iUnion_of_isOpen}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B7.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rgc-r5}
\code{continuous\_iff\_continuousOn\_iUnion\_of\_isOpen} is Mathlib's pasting lemma.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{continuous_iff_continuousOn_iUnion_of_isOpen}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain B8: Glued chart map is bijective (lem:rado-glue-bijective)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B8.1: local injectivity on each chart]
\label{lem:rgb-r1}
\uses{lem:rgb-r2}
Each chart $\varphi_{i}$ is a homeomorphism, hence injective.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgb_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B8.2: agreement on overlaps lifts to global injectivity]
\label{lem:rgb-r2}
\uses{lem:rgb-r3}
If two points $p \neq q$ map to the same image, they lie in different charts (else local injectivity is contradicted); the chart-overlap compatibility produces a contradiction.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgb_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B8.3: surjectivity from cover-by-image]
\label{lem:rgb-r3}
\uses{lem:rgb-r4}
Every point of the target lies in $\varphi_{i}(U_{i})$ for some $i$, since the source $X$ is covered by $\{U_{i}\}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgb_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}
