\begin{lemma}[Pass B8.4: disjoint-overlap analysis]
\label{lem:rgb-r4}
\uses{lem:rgb-r5}
On overlaps the glued map agrees by construction, so the map is well-defined as a quotient of the disjoint union of charts modulo the cocycle relation.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgb_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass B8.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rgb-r5}
\code{Equiv.coe\_iUnion} for piecing together bijections from disjoint pieces; the cover-with-overlap variant requires a coproduct argument.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:rgb-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgb_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain C1: Cyclic reduction to fully-reduced form (lem:tietze-cyclic-reduction)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C1.1: identify cancellable adjacent pairs]
\label{lem:tcr-r1}
\uses{lem:tcr-r2}
In an edge word $w = a_{1}\cdots a_{n}$ over $\{a, a^{-1}, b, b^{-1}, \ldots\}$, cancellable pairs are adjacent letters $a_{i} a_{i+1}$ with $a_{i+1} = a_{i}^{-1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C1.2: cancel iteratively]
\label{lem:tcr-r2}
\uses{lem:tcr-r3}
While a cancellable pair exists, remove it.  Process terminates because word length strictly decreases.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C1.3: cyclic cancellability]
\label{lem:tcr-r3}
\uses{lem:tcr-r4}
Also cancel $a_{1}$ and $a_{n}$ if they are inverses (cyclic adjacency).  The cyclically-reduced form is unique up to rotation.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C1.4: uniqueness of reduced form (Stallings--Tietze)]
\label{lem:tcr-r4}
\uses{lem:tcr-r5}
Free groups have unique reduced words; cyclic reduction extends this uniqueness up to rotation.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:tcr-r5}
\code{FreeGroup} has \code{FreeGroup.reduce} for word reduction.  Mathlib status: present (free group reduce); cyclic version is partial.
\uses{lem:tcr-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain C3: Tietze moves preserve orientability (lem:tietze-moves-preserve-orientability)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C3.1: orientability via consistent edge labeling]
\label{lem:tmo-r1}
\uses{lem:tmo-r2}
A polygon edge word represents an orientable surface iff each letter and its inverse appear with consistent signs (no $aa$ pattern).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tmo_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C3.2: Tietze moves do not introduce same-orientation pairs]
\label{lem:tmo-r2}
\uses{lem:tmo-r3}
The basic Tietze moves (relator manipulation, generator addition/removal) preserve the consistent-sign property.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tmo_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C3.3: inductive proof on move count]
\label{lem:tmo-r3}
\uses{lem:tmo-r4}
By induction on the number of Tietze moves, the orientability invariant propagates.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tmo_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C3.4: equivalence of polygon-word orientability and surface orientability]
\label{lem:tmo-r4}
\uses{lem:tmo-r5}
The combinatorial orientability of the polygon word matches the topological orientability of the resulting surface.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tmo_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C3.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:tmo-r5}
Surface orientability is currently absent from Mathlib.  Closest: \code{Manifold.Orientable} (planned).  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:tmo-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tmo_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain C4: Orientable handle-grouped is concatenation of standard blocks (lem:tietze-orientable-is-handle-concat)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C4.1: structure theorem for handle-grouped words]
\label{lem:toh-r1}
\uses{lem:toh-r2}
A handle-grouped word has the form $\prod_{i=1}^{g} W_{i}$ where each $W_{i}$ is a 4-letter handle block.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.toh_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C4.2: each handle block is in standard form $a_{i}b_{i}a_{i}^{-1}b_{i}^{-1}$]
\label{lem:toh-r2}
\uses{lem:toh-r3}
By renaming generators within each block, $W_{i}$ takes the standard form.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.toh_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C4.3: concatenation preserves orientability]
\label{lem:toh-r3}
\uses{lem:toh-r4}
The product structure is preserved under the standard surface concatenation operation.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.toh_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C4.4: uniqueness of the standard form up to genus]
\label{lem:toh-r4}
\uses{lem:toh-r5}
Two orientable surface words are equivalent iff their handle counts agree.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.toh_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C4.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:toh-r5}
Genus classification of orientable surfaces is currently absent from Mathlib.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:toh-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.toh_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain C5: Handle blocks may be permuted within a word (lem:tietze-handle-swap)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C5.1: two handles commute up to Tietze moves]
\label{lem:ths-r1}
\uses{lem:ths-r2}
Two adjacent handle blocks $H_{i}H_{i+1}$ in a word can be swapped to $H_{i+1}H_{i}$ via a sequence of Tietze moves.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ths_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C5.2: explicit swap via auxiliary moves]
\label{lem:ths-r2}
\uses{lem:ths-r3}
Use cyclic permutation + relator conjugation to move one block past another, preserving the underlying group presentation.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ths_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C5.3: conjugation in free product groups]
\label{lem:ths-r3}
\uses{lem:ths-r4}
In the free group, conjugating one factor by another doesn't change the underlying group, only the relator presentation.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ths_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C5.4: permutations generated by adjacent transpositions]
\label{lem:ths-r4}
\uses{lem:ths-r5}
Any permutation of $\{1, \ldots, g\}$ is a product of adjacent transpositions, so handle ordering is fully arbitrary.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ths_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C5.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:ths-r5}
\code{Equiv.Perm} for permutations; conjugation in \code{FreeGroup} is partial.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:ths-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ths_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain C6: Strip-one-handle (induction) (lem:tietze-strip-one-handle)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C6.1: isolate the first handle block]
\label{lem:tsh-r1}
\uses{lem:tsh-r2}
Use cyclic reduction + handle swap to isolate one handle block at the start of the word.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tsh_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C6.2: strip the handle via free-product factorization]
\label{lem:tsh-r2}
\uses{lem:tsh-r3}
The word decomposes as $W = H \cdot W'$ where $H$ is the first handle block, $W'$ has $g-1$ handles.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tsh_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C6.3: inductive hypothesis on $W'$]
\label{lem:tsh-r3}
\uses{lem:tsh-r4}
By induction on $g$, $W'$ is a concatenation of $g-1$ standard handles.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tsh_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C6.4: re-attach $H$ to obtain the full standard form]
\label{lem:tsh-r4}
\uses{lem:tsh-r5}
Concatenating $H$ with the inductively-derived form gives the full standard relator $\prod_{i=1}^{g} a_{i}b_{i}a_{i}^{-1}b_{i}^{-1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tsh_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass C6.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:tsh-r5}
Inductive proof using \code{Nat.rec}; relator decomposition is not in Mathlib.  Mathlib status: partial (only the induction primitive is present).
\uses{lem:tsh-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tsh_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain D1: Cut along a spanning tree of the 1-skeleton (lem:polygonal-model-cut-along-tree)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass D1.1: spanning tree exists in any connected finite graph]
\label{lem:pct-r1}
\uses{lem:pct-r2}
Take a maximal acyclic subgraph of the 1-skeleton; this is a spanning tree.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.pct_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass D1.2: cutting along the tree produces a topological disk]
\label{lem:pct-r2}
\uses{lem:pct-r3}
Removing a spanning tree from a triangulated 2-manifold and taking the dual gives a topological disk.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.pct_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass D1.3: Euler-formula check on the disk]
\label{lem:pct-r3}
\uses{lem:pct-r4}
$V - E + F = 1$ for a disk; verifying this on the cut produces consistency.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.pct_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass D1.4: disk has length-$4g$ boundary edge word]
\label{lem:pct-r4}
\uses{lem:pct-r5}
For a genus-$g$ surface, the dual disk has $2 \cdot 2g$ boundary edges in a four-letter alphabet.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.pct_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass D1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:pct-r5}
\code{SimpleGraph.spanningTree} (planned) for the spanning tree.  Cutting argument is not in Mathlib.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:pct-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.pct_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain E4: Mayer--Vietoris exact sequence (both theories) (lem:deRham-mayer-vietoris)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E4.1: MV for de Rham via short exact sequence of complexes]
\label{lem:dmv-r1}
\uses{lem:dmv-r2}
For an open cover $\{U, V\}$ of $X$, $0 \to \Omega^{*}(X) \to \Omega^{*}(U)\oplus\Omega^{*}(V) \to \Omega^{*}(U\cap V) \to 0$ is short-exact.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dmv_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E4.2: MV for singular via barycentric subdivision]
\label{lem:dmv-r2}
\uses{lem:dmv-r3}
Singular MV is established via small simplices: every chain in $X$ is chain-homotopic to a small chain, decomposable into $U$- and $V$-pieces.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dmv_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E4.3: snake lemma gives the long exact sequence]
\label{lem:dmv-r3}
\uses{lem:dmv-r4}
Both short exact sequences yield long exact sequences in cohomology via the snake lemma.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dmv_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E4.4: comparison map is a chain map]
\label{lem:dmv-r4}
\uses{lem:dmv-r5}
The integration map $\Omega^{*} \to S^{*}$ commutes with the MV connecting morphism, giving a comparison of long exact sequences.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dmv_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E4.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:dmv-r5}
\code{CategoryTheory.Abelian.SnakeLemma} for snake lemma; MV for singular cohomology partially present in \code{AlgebraicTopology}.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:dmv-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dmv_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain E5: Five-lemma induction over a finite good cover (lem:deRham-five-lemma-induction)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E5.1: base case: one chart]
\label{lem:dfl-r1}
\uses{lem:dfl-r2}
On a contractible chart, both de Rham and singular cohomology are trivial in positive degrees, so the integration map is trivially an iso.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfl_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E5.2: inductive step: combine two covers]
\label{lem:dfl-r2}
\uses{lem:dfl-r3}
Given covers of size $n$ and 1 covering $X$, combine via Mayer--Vietoris and the five lemma.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfl_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E5.3: five lemma for chain map between long exact sequences]
\label{lem:dfl-r3}
\uses{lem:dfl-r4}
If 4 of 5 maps in a ladder of long exact sequences are isos, so is the 5th.
\lean{CategoryTheory.Abelian.fiveLemma}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E5.4: induction on cover size]
\label{lem:dfl-r4}
\uses{lem:dfl-r5}
By induction on the size of a finite good cover, the comparison map becomes an iso globally.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfl_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass E5.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:dfl-r5}
\code{CategoryTheory.Abelian.FiveLemma}.  Mathlib status: present (in homological-algebra section).
\lean{CategoryTheory.Abelian.fiveLemma}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain F1H: Laplacian is elliptic (lem:hodge-laplacian-elliptic)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1H.1: symbol of $\Delta$]
\label{lem:hle-r1}
\uses{lem:hle-r2}
In local coordinates, the principal symbol of $\Delta$ is $|\xi|^{2}$, a positive-definite quadratic form.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.hle_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1H.2: ellipticity = invertible principal symbol]
\label{lem:hle-r2}
\uses{lem:hle-r3}
An operator is elliptic iff its principal symbol is invertible for every nonzero $\xi$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.hle_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1H.3: $|\xi|^{2} > 0$ for $\xi \neq 0$]
\label{lem:hle-r3}
\uses{lem:hle-r4}
Positive-definiteness of the standard inner product on $T^{*}M$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.hle_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1H.4: local representation of the Laplacian on $\R^{n}$]
\label{lem:hle-r4}
\uses{lem:hle-r5}
$\Delta = -\sum_{i,j} g^{ij}\partial_{i}\partial_{j} + \text{lower order}$.  The principal part is $-\partial_{i}\partial_{j}$, with symbol $\xi_{i}\xi_{j}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.hle_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass F1H.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:hle-r5}
\code{LinearPDE.Symbol} and \code{LinearPDE.Elliptic} are not in Mathlib.  Closest: \code{ContinuousLinearMap}.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:hle-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.hle_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain H1: Sheaf cohomology computed via fine resolution (lem:dolbeault-fine-resolution-cohomology)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.1: a fine resolution computes sheaf cohomology]
\label{lem:dfr-r1}
\uses{lem:dfr-r2}
For a sheaf $\mathcal{F}$ with fine resolution $0\to\mathcal{F}\to\mathcal{F}^{0}\to\mathcal{F}^{1}\to\cdots$, $H^{q}(X,\mathcal{F})$ equals the $q$-th cohomology of the global sections.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfr_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.2: fine sheaves have trivial higher cohomology]
\label{lem:dfr-r2}
\uses{lem:dfr-r3}
For a fine sheaf $\mathcal{G}$, $H^{q}(X,\mathcal{G}) = 0$ for $q \geq 1$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfr_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.3: derived functor argument]
\label{lem:dfr-r3}
\uses{lem:dfr-r4}
Sheaf cohomology is the right-derived functor of global sections; vanishing on fine resolves the spectral sequence.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfr_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.4: partition-of-unity argument for fine sheaf vanishing]
\label{lem:dfr-r4}
\uses{lem:dfr-r5}
$\check{H}^{1}(X,\mathcal{G}) = 0$: any cocycle splits via the partition of unity that defines fineness.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfr_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:dfr-r5}
\code{AlgebraicGeometry.SheafCohomology} for sheaf cohomology; fine sheaves and partitions of unity are not yet in Mathlib.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:dfr-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfr_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain H2: Each $\Omega^{p,q}$ is a fine sheaf (lem:dolbeault-fine-sheaves)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.1: smooth manifold has smooth partitions of unity]
\label{lem:dfs-r1}
\uses{lem:dfs-r2}
On a smooth paracompact manifold, every locally finite open cover admits a subordinate smooth partition of unity.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfs_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.2: sheaf of smooth $(p,q)$-forms is a $C^{\infty}$-module]
\label{lem:dfs-r2}
\uses{lem:dfs-r3}
$\Omega^{p,q}$ is a sheaf of $C^{\infty}(X)$-modules: smooth functions act on smooth forms.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfs_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.3: a $C^{\infty}$-module sheaf is fine]
\label{lem:dfs-r3}
\uses{lem:dfs-r4,lem:dfs-r6}
Any sheaf of $C^{\infty}$-modules is fine: multiplication by a smooth partition of unity gives the splitting.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfs_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.4: paracompactness of compact 2-manifolds]
\label{lem:dfs-r4}
\uses{lem:dfs-r5}
Compact manifolds are paracompact, providing the locally-finite cover hypothesis.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dfs_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass H2.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:dfs-r5}
\code{SmoothPartitionOfUnity.exists\_isSubordinate} on a smooth paracompact manifold.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{SmoothManifoldWithCorners.SmoothPartitionOfUnity.exists_isSubordinate}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain I1: Trace map: $H^{1}(X,K_{X})\cong\C$ via residues (lem:serre-trace-iso)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.1: residue map on Cech cocycles]
\label{lem:sti-r1}
\uses{lem:sti-r2}
For a covering $\{U_{i}\}$ with local trivializations, a Cech 1-cocycle for $K_{X}$ pairs with a residue $\sum_{p}\mathrm{Res}_{p}$ to give a complex number.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sti_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.2: residue is independent of cocycle representative]
\label{lem:sti-r2}
\uses{lem:sti-r3}
Coboundary $\eta_{ij} = \eta_{i} - \eta_{j}$ contributes $\mathrm{Res}(\eta_{i}) - \mathrm{Res}(\eta_{j}) = 0$ (Stokes-type cancellation).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sti_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.3: residue is non-zero on generators]
\label{lem:sti-r3}
\uses{lem:sti-r4}
For the standard cocycle $1/z$ near a single point, $\mathrm{Res} = 1 \neq 0$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sti_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.4: residue + sum-zero theorem]
\label{lem:sti-r4}
\uses{lem:sti-r5}
$\sum_{p}\mathrm{Res}_{p}\omega = 0$ for global meromorphic 1-forms (Lemma~\ref{lem:serre-residue-theorem}); the trace is well-defined.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sti_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:sti-r5}
\code{SheafCohomology.Cech} + residue theorem (cf.\ chain D).  Mathlib status: ABSENT (residue infrastructure for Riemann surfaces).
\uses{lem:sti-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sti_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain I2: Cup product on Cech cohomology (lem:serre-cech-cup-product)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.1: Cech cup product on cocycles]
\label{lem:scc-r1}
\uses{lem:scc-r2}
$(\alpha\smile\beta)_{i_{0}\cdots i_{p+q}} := \alpha_{i_{0}\cdots i_{p}}\cdot\beta_{i_{p}\cdots i_{p+q}}$ defines a chain-level cup product.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.scc_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.2: descent to cohomology]
\label{lem:scc-r2}
\uses{lem:scc-r3}
The Leibniz rule $d(\alpha\smile\beta) = d\alpha\smile\beta\pm\alpha\smile d\beta$ ensures cup product descends to cohomology.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.scc_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.3: graded-commutativity of the cup product]
\label{lem:scc-r3}
\uses{lem:scc-r4}
$\alpha\smile\beta = (-1)^{pq}\beta\smile\alpha$ on cohomology, via a chain homotopy.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.scc_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.4: comparison with derived-functor product]
\label{lem:scc-r4}
\uses{lem:scc-r5}
The Cech cup product agrees with the derived-functor cup product on a paracompact space.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.scc_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I2.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:scc-r5}
\code{CategoryTheory.Sheaf.CupProduct} (planned).  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:scc-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.scc_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain I3: Harmonic representatives realise the Serre pairing (lem:serre-l2-realisation)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.1: Hodge representatives in $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}$ and $\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$]
\label{lem:sl2-r1}
\uses{lem:sl2-r2}
Use Hodge decomposition to pick harmonic representatives $\omega \in \mathcal{H}^{1,0}$ for $H^{0}(X,K_{X})$ and $\eta \in \mathcal{H}^{0,1}$ for $H^{1}(X,\mathcal{O})$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sl2_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.2: $L^{2}$-pairing on $X$]
\label{lem:sl2-r2}
\uses{lem:sl2-r3}
The pairing $\langle\omega,\eta\rangle := \int_{X}\omega\wedge\eta$ is well-defined on harmonic representatives.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sl2_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.3: Hodge $\star$ exchanges $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}$ and $\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$]
\label{lem:sl2-r3}
\uses{lem:sl2-r4}
$\bar\star : \mathcal{H}^{1,0} \to \mathcal{H}^{0,1}$ is an antiholomorphic isomorphism.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sl2_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.4: non-degeneracy from $L^{2}$-positivity]
\label{lem:sl2-r4}
\uses{lem:sl2-r5}
For nonzero $\omega$, $\langle\omega,\bar\star\omega\rangle = \int|\omega|^{2}_{L^{2}} > 0$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sl2_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass I3.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:sl2-r5}
\code{InnerProductSpace} + Hodge $\bar\star$.  Hodge $\bar\star$ is currently absent from Mathlib.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:sl2-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sl2_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Chain J1: $\Omega^{k}(M)$ is an $\R$-vector space and $C^{\infty}(M,\R)$-module (lem:bundled-forms-algebra)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.1: sections of a vector bundle form a module]
\label{lem:bfa-r1}
\uses{lem:bfa-r2}
Smooth sections $\Gamma(M,E)$ of any smooth vector bundle $E\to M$ are a $C^{\infty}(M)$-module.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfa_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.2: $\Omega^{k}(M) = \Gamma(M,\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M)$]
\label{lem:bfa-r2}
\uses{lem:bfa-r3}
Differential $k$-forms are smooth sections of the alternating bundle $\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfa_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.3: $\Lambda^{k}T^{*}M$ is a smooth vector bundle]
\label{lem:bfa-r3}
\uses{lem:bfa-r4}
The $k$-th exterior power of $T^{*}M$ inherits a smooth vector bundle structure from $T^{*}M$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfa_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.4: alternating product as a smooth functor on vector bundles]
\label{lem:bfa-r4}
\uses{lem:bfa-r5}
The functor $E \mapsto \Lambda^{k}E$ is a smooth construction preserving smooth bundle structure.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfa_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:bfa-r5}
\code{VectorBundle} + \code{ExteriorAlgebra}.  Bundled forms package not yet integrated; closest is \code{Mathlib.Geometry.Manifold.VectorBundle.SmoothSection}.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:bfa-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfa_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain J2: $d^{2} = 0$ (lem:bundled-forms-d-sq-zero)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.1: local coordinate expression of $d$]
\label{lem:bfd-r1}
\uses{lem:bfd-r2}
In a chart, $d\omega = \sum\partial_{i}f_{I}\,dx_{i}\wedge dx_{I}$ for $\omega = \sum f_{I}dx_{I}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfd_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.2: $d^{2}\omega$ in coordinates]
\label{lem:bfd-r2}
\uses{lem:bfd-r3}
$d^{2}\omega = \sum_{i,j}\partial_{j}\partial_{i}f_{I}\,dx_{j}\wedge dx_{i}\wedge dx_{I}$, with $dx_{j}\wedge dx_{i}$ antisymmetric and $\partial_{j}\partial_{i}f_{I}$ symmetric.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfd_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.3: symmetric times antisymmetric is zero]
\label{lem:bfd-r3}
\uses{lem:bfd-r4}
$\sum_{i,j}A_{ij}B_{ij} = 0$ when $A$ symmetric and $B$ antisymmetric.  This is the algebraic identity behind $d^{2} = 0$.
\lean{AlternatingMap}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.4: symmetry of partial derivatives (Schwarz)]
\label{lem:bfd-r4}
\uses{lem:bfd-r5}
For $f \in C^{2}$, $\partial_{i}\partial_{j}f = \partial_{j}\partial_{i}f$.
\lean{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv_symm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J2.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:bfd-r5}
\uses{lem:bfd-r6}
\code{ContDiff.deriv\_symm} for Schwarz; \code{AlternatingMap} for the antisymmetric structure.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv_symm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain J3: Pullback by smooth maps commutes with $d$ (lem:bundled-forms-pullback-compat)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.1: local coordinate expression of $f^{*}$]
\label{lem:bfp-r1}
\uses{lem:bfp-r2}
For $f: M\to N$, $\omega = g\,dy_{I}$, $f^{*}\omega = (g\circ f)\,d(y_{I}\circ f)$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfp_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.2: $d$ commutes with pullback locally]
\label{lem:bfp-r2}
\uses{lem:bfp-r3}
$d(f^{*}\omega) = d((g\circ f))\wedge d(y_{I}\circ f)$ and $f^{*}(d\omega) = f^{*}(dg\wedge dy_{I}) = d(g\circ f)\wedge d(y_{I}\circ f)$.  Equal.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfp_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.3: chain rule applied to $g\circ f$]
\label{lem:bfp-r3}
\uses{lem:bfp-r4}
$d(g\circ f) = dg|_{f(p)}\circ df = (f^{*}dg)$ on tangent vectors, so
the two expressions match.  Project-side dispatch for 0-forms:
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.exteriorDerivativeZero\_pullbackZero},
which proves
$d(\varphi^{*}\omega)\,x\,[v] = d\omega\,(\varphi\,x)\,[D\varphi\,x\,v]$
via Mathlib's \code{fderiv\_comp}.  $k\geq 1$ remains pending on
R9-sub-A.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.exteriorDerivativeZero_pullbackZero}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.4: naturality of the de Rham complex]
\label{lem:bfp-r4}
\uses{lem:bfp-r5}
The de Rham complex is functorial: $f^{*}$ commutes with the
differential at the level of functorial constructions.  Project-side
dispatch for the $0\to 1$-form layer:
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.OneForm.pullback}
(chart-local complex 1-forms),
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.OneForm.pullback\_add}
and \code{pullback\_smul} ($\C$-linearity), and
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.OneForm.lineIntegral\_pullback}
(integral-side substitution rule).  Together with
\code{exteriorDerivativeZero\_pullbackZero} from Pass J3.3, this
gives a closed sub-chain on the 0/1-form layer; $k\geq 2$ remains
pending on R9-sub-A.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.OneForm.pullback}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass J3.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:bfp-r5}
\code{ContMDiff.fderiv} for the chain rule; pullback-of-forms is partial.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:bfp-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.bfp_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain K1: Garding inequality (lem:sobolev-garding)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.1: Fourier characterization of $H^{s}$-norm]
\label{lem:sgd-r1}
\uses{lem:sgd-r2}
$\|u\|_{H^{s}} = \|(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s/2}\hat u\|_{L^{2}}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sgd_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.2: symbol of an elliptic operator $T$ is $|\xi|^{m}$-bounded]
\label{lem:sgd-r2}
\uses{lem:sgd-r3}
$T$ elliptic order $m$ $\Rightarrow$ $|\sigma_{T}(\xi)| \geq c|\xi|^{m}$ for $|\xi|$ large.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sgd_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.3: $L^{2}$-estimate from symbol bound]
\label{lem:sgd-r3}
\uses{lem:sgd-r4}
$\|Tu\|_{L^{2}} \geq c\|(1+|\xi|^{2})^{m/2}\hat u\|_{L^{2}} - C\|u\|_{L^{2}}$ via Plancherel.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sgd_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.4: rearrange to obtain Garding form]
\label{lem:sgd-r4}
\uses{lem:sgd-r5}
$\|u\|_{H^{s+m}} \leq C(\|Tu\|_{H^{s}} + \|u\|_{H^{s}})$ from the previous bound.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sgd_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K1.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:sgd-r5}
\code{MeasureTheory.FourierTransform} for Plancherel.  Sobolev space and Garding inequality are absent.  Mathlib status: ABSENT.
\uses{lem:sgd-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sgd_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Chain K2: $\Delta$ is elliptic (lem:sobolev-laplacian-elliptic)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.1: principal symbol of $\Delta$]
\label{lem:sle-r1}
\uses{lem:sle-r2}
$\sigma_{\Delta}(\xi) = -|\xi|^{2}$ in local coordinates.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sle_r1}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.2: symbol invertibility for $\xi \neq 0$]
\label{lem:sle-r2}
\uses{lem:sle-r3}
$|\xi|^{2} > 0$ for $\xi \neq 0$, so the symbol is non-zero (and invertible as an endomorphism).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sle_r2}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.3: ellipticity in the operator-theoretic sense]
\label{lem:sle-r3}
\uses{lem:sle-r4}
$\sigma_{\Delta}(\xi)$ invertible for all $\xi \neq 0$ means $\Delta$ is elliptic.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sle_r3}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.4: metric-induced inner product is positive-definite]
\label{lem:sle-r4}
\uses{lem:sle-r5}
$|\xi|^{2}_{g} = g^{ij}\xi_{i}\xi_{j}$ is positive-definite on $T^{*}_{p}M$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sle_r4}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass K2.5: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:sle-r5}
\code{InnerProductSpace} for positive-definite inner product; \code{LinearPDE.Elliptic} not yet in Mathlib.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:sle-r6}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sle_r5}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{layman}
Across all 48 frontier leaves, the gap-to-Mathlib distribution is
clear: roughly half the chains terminate at a named Mathlib
declaration in pass 5 (categorized below as ``present''),
about a quarter end on a partial Mathlib match (some pieces
present, but the full statement requires a small wrapper or
upstream PR), and the remaining quarter end on truly absent
infrastructure --- almost all of which clusters in a small
number of categories: piecewise-linear topology (chains B2,
B3, B4, B6, D1, D2), surface-classification combinatorics
(chains C2, C3, C4), bundled differential forms (chain J1)
and Sobolev/elliptic infrastructure (chain K1).  These four
clusters collectively account for the bulk of the project's
remaining classical-analysis distance from Mathlib.
\end{layman}


% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine rk-r5-tail-decay into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.6: integrand decomposition]
\label{lem:rk-r6}
\uses{lem:rk-r7}
Write the integrand as $(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s-s'}\cdot(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s'}|\hat u(\xi)|^{2}$.  The first factor tends to $0$ as $|\xi|\to\infty$ (since $s<s'$); the second is integrable (in $L^{1}$ globally).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rk_r6}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.7: dominated convergence on the tail]
\label{lem:rk-r7}
\uses{lem:rk-r8}
For each $N$, $\mathbf{1}_{|\xi|>N}\cdot(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s-s'}\le 1$ pointwise and $\to 0$ a.e.  Apply dominated convergence with envelope $(1+|\xi|^{2})^{s'}|\hat u|^{2}\in L^{1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rk_r7}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.8: setIntegral on $\sigma$-finite measure]
\label{lem:rk-r8}
\uses{lem:rk-r9}
\code{MeasureTheory.tendsto\_setIntegral\_compl} gives $\int_{|\xi|>N}f\,d\mu\to 0$ for $f\in L^{1}$ on a $\sigma$-finite measure.
\lean{MeasureTheory.tendsto_setIntegral_compl}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.9: Fourier transform restricts $L^{1}$]
\label{lem:rk-r9}
\uses{lem:rk-r10}
\code{MeasureTheory.Lp.measurable} ensures $\hat u$ measurable, so the integrand is measurable and the setIntegral lemma applies.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rk_r9}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rk.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rk-r10}
\code{MeasureTheory.tendsto\_setIntegral\_compl} on a $\sigma$-finite measure space.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{MeasureTheory.tendsto_setIntegral_compl}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine ctp-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.6: open quotient projection inherits ChartedSpace from base]
\label{lem:ctp-r6}
\uses{lem:ctp-r7}
For an open quotient $\pi : V \to V/\Lambda$ that's a local homeomorphism, $V/\Lambda$ inherits a charted-space structure: each chart on $V$ projects to a chart on $V/\Lambda$ via $\pi^{-1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ctp_r6}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.7: local homeomorphism gives chart compatibility]
\label{lem:ctp-r7}
\uses{lem:ctp-r8}
$\pi$ is a local homeomorphism (since $\Lambda$ is discrete), so every chart pulls back uniquely; the pulled-back charts inherit smooth compatibility from $V$'s smooth structure.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ctp_r7}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.8: complex structure transfer along a local biholomorphism]
\label{lem:ctp-r8}
\uses{lem:ctp-r9}
A local biholomorphism between charted complex manifolds transfers complex structure: the holomorphic transition maps remain holomorphic on the quotient.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ctp_r8}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.9: ChartedSpace.compChartedSpace functoriality]
\label{lem:ctp-r9}
\uses{lem:ctp-r10}
\code{ChartedSpace.comp} composes charts; for a local homeomorphism cover, this gives the quotient charted-space structure.
\lean{ChartedSpace.comp}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ctp.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:ctp-r10}
\code{ChartedSpace} + \code{IsLocalHomeomorph}.  The full open-quotient charted-space transfer is partial in Mathlib; closest is \code{ChartedSpace.compHomeomorph} for a single homeomorphism, requiring a small extension to local-homeomorphism covers.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:ctp-r11}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ctp_r10}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine trf-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.6: formal power series symmetric functions]
\label{lem:trf-r6}
\uses{lem:trf-r7}
For convergent power series in variables $w^{1/k}\zeta_{k}^{j}$ ($j=0,\ldots,k-1$), elementary symmetric polynomials in the $\zeta_{k}^{j}w^{1/k}$ are formal power series in $w$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tracePowerSeries_symmetricFunctions}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.7: Newton identities at the formal-series level]
\label{lem:trf-r7}
\uses{lem:trf-r8}
$p_{m} = \sum (-1)^{i+1} e_{i} p_{m-i}$ (Newton) holds in the ring of formal power series; analytic + symmetric implies polynomial in elementary symmetric functions.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.newtonIdentities_formalSeries}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.8: convergence of the power-series substitution]
\label{lem:trf-r8}
\uses{lem:trf-r9}
Replacing $w^{1/k}$ by a small disk $|w|<\rho$ gives convergent expansion; the symmetric polynomial in $\zeta_{k}^{j}w^{1/k}$ converges as a power series in $w$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.powerSeriesSubstitution_converges}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.9: upgrade to AnalyticAt via Mathlib's symmetric polynomial API]
\label{lem:trf-r9}
\uses{lem:trf-r10}
Mathlib has \code{MvPolynomial.symmetric\_subalgebra} (polynomial level); the analytic upgrade combines this with \code{FormalMultilinearSeries.symmetric}.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.MathlibEndpoints.mem_symmetricSubalgebra_iff_isSymmetric}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass trf.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:trf-r10}
\code{MvPolynomial.symmetric\_subalgebra} + \code{FormalMultilinearSeries.symmetric}; combined with \code{AnalyticAt.compFormalMultilinearSeries}.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:trf-r11}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.symmetricPowerSeries_analyticEndpointPartial}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine rgb-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.6: disjoint-overlap argument via cover-with-cocycle]
\label{lem:rgb-r6}
\uses{lem:rgb-r7}
Two points map to the same image iff they're related by the cocycle (transition map).  Outside transition overlaps, charts are disjoint by construction.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgb_r6}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.7: global injectivity via cover-of-fibres]
\label{lem:rgb-r7}
\uses{lem:rgb-r8}
For each fibre $\pi^{-1}(y)$, exactly one point of one chart is selected.  Reduces to selection-axiom-free finite combinatorics over the open cover.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgb_r7}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.8: Equiv from finite cocycle data]
\label{lem:rgb-r8}
\uses{lem:rgb-r9}
\code{Equiv.coe\_iUnion} composes: given an equivalence on each chart and compatibility on overlaps, glue to a global equivalence.
\lean{Equiv.coe_iUnion}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.9: global Equiv on a paracompact space]
\label{lem:rgb-r9}
\uses{lem:rgb-r10}
For a paracompact space, the cocycle data over a finite cover yields a global equivalence; this is the manifold gluing lemma.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgb_r9}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass rgb.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:rgb-r10}
\code{Equiv.iUnion} for global equivalences; cocycle gluing on a paracompact space is partial.  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:rgb-r11}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.rgb_r10}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine tcr-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.6: free-group word reduction terminates]
\label{lem:tcr-r6}
\uses{lem:tcr-r7}
FreeGroup word reduction is monotone-decreasing in length, so it terminates.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r6}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.7: cyclic conjugacy class is reduced word + rotation]
\label{lem:tcr-r7}
\uses{lem:tcr-r8}
Two cyclically-reduced words in the same conjugacy class differ by a rotation; this is a finite-orbit calculation.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r7}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.8: rotation as conjugation by a single letter]
\label{lem:tcr-r8}
\uses{lem:tcr-r9}
Rotating $a_{1}\cdots a_{n}$ to $a_{2}\cdots a_{n} a_{1}$ is conjugation by $a_{1}^{-1}$.  Iteration covers all rotations.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r8}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.9: conjugacy in FreeGroup decidable]
\label{lem:tcr-r9}
\uses{lem:tcr-r10}
Conjugacy of cyclically-reduced words in a free group is decidable by direct comparison of rotations.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r9}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tcr.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:tcr-r10}
\code{FreeGroup.reduce} + \code{FreeGroup.IsCyclicallyReduced} (planned).  Mathlib status: partial.
\uses{lem:tcr-r11}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tcr_r10}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine ths-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.6: any permutation as product of adjacent transpositions]
\label{lem:ths-r6}
\uses{lem:ths-r7}
Symmetric group $S_{n}$ is generated by adjacent transpositions $(i, i+1)$; this is a standard combinatorial fact.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ths_r6}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.7: adjacent swap of handle blocks via Tietze move]
\label{lem:ths-r7}
\uses{lem:ths-r8}
Swapping $H_{i}H_{i+1} \to H_{i+1}H_{i}$ is a single Tietze move (handle commutation in the free product).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ths_r7}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.8: induct on permutation length]
\label{lem:ths-r8}
\uses{lem:ths-r9}
Apply induction on the length of the swapping permutation: each adjacent swap is one Tietze move.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ths_r8}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.9: conjugation commutes with adjacent swap]
\label{lem:ths-r9}
\uses{lem:ths-r10}
Conjugation in FreeGroup commutes with adjacent-swap action via \code{Equiv.Perm.symm\_swap}.
\lean{Equiv.Perm.symm_swap}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass ths.10: Mathlib endpoint]

\uses{lem:ths-r11}
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.ths_r10}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine tsh-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.6: induction on the genus parameter]
\label{lem:tsh-r6}
\uses{lem:tsh-r7}
$g \mapsto $ number of handles; base case $g=0$ trivial, inductive step strips one handle.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tsh_r6}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.7: decompose word as $H \cdot W'$ with $|W'|$ shorter]
\label{lem:tsh-r7}
\uses{lem:tsh-r8}
After cyclic rotation, the word starts with a handle block; the rest has $g-1$ handles and shorter length.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tsh_r7}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.8: apply induction hypothesis to $W'$]
\label{lem:tsh-r8}
\uses{lem:tsh-r9}
By induction, $W'$ is in standard form $\prod_{i=2}^{g}H_{i}^{\mathrm{std}}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tsh_r8}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.9: re-attach $H$ to obtain full standard form]
\label{lem:tsh-r9}
\uses{lem:tsh-r10}
$W = H \cdot W' = H_{1}^{\mathrm{std}} \cdot \prod_{i=2}^{g}H_{i}^{\mathrm{std}}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.tsh_r9}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass tsh.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:tsh-r10}

\lean{Nat.rec}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine dss-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.6: FTC on the unit interval]
\label{lem:dss-r6}
\uses{lem:dss-r7}
$\int_{0}^{1}f'(t)\,dt = f(1) - f(0)$ for $f \in C^{1}([0,1])$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dss_r6}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.7: Fubini reduces $\Delta^{k}$-integral to nested 1D integrals]
\label{lem:dss-r7}
\uses{lem:dss-r8}
For the standard simplex $\Delta^{k}$, integration over $\Delta^{k}$ is nested integration over the slices, by Fubini.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dss_r7}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.8: inductive Stokes via slicing]
\label{lem:dss-r8}
\uses{lem:dss-r9}
$\int_{\Delta^{k}}d\eta = \int_{\Delta^{k-1}}\left[\int_{0}^{t_{k}}\partial_{k}\eta\,dt_{k}\right]\,d\bar t = \int_{\Delta^{k-1}}\eta(t_{k}=1) - \eta(t_{k}=0)\,d\bar t = \int_{\partial\Delta^{k}}\eta$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dss_r8}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.9: face-orientation signs from the alternating boundary]
\label{lem:dss-r9}
\uses{lem:dss-r10}
$(-1)^{i}$ signs in $\partial\Delta^{k} = \sum(-1)^{i}\partial_{i}$ come from orientation of the slicing.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dss_r9}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dss.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:dss-r10}
\code{intervalIntegral.integral\_deriv\_eq\_sub} (FTC) + \code{MeasureTheory.integral\_prod} (Fubini).  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{intervalIntegral.integral_deriv_eq_sub}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dsq.6: smooth approximation via mollifiers in chart-local]
\label{lem:dsq-r6}
\uses{lem:dsq-r7}
In a chart, convolution with a smooth bump function $\phi_{\varepsilon}$ smooths a continuous map; uniform convergence as $\varepsilon\to 0$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dsq_r6}

\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dsq_r7}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dsq.8: approximation is homotopic to the original]
\label{lem:dsq-r8}
\uses{lem:dsq-r9}
The straight-line homotopy $(1-s)f + s\tilde f$ is well-defined on a tubular neighborhood and lands in $M$ for small $s$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dsq_r8}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dsq.9: uniform-on-compact smooth approximation]
\label{lem:dsq-r9}

On a compact set, smooth approximations exist with uniform $C^{0}$ small error.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dsq_r9}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dmv.6: identify cohomology theories abstractly]

\uses{lem:dmv-r7}
Both de Rham and singular cohomology are derived functors of global-section-like functors on appropriate sheaves of $\R$-modules.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dmv_r6}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\uses{lem:dmv-r8}
Both theories are contravariant functors on the open-set category; Mayer--Vietoris is the snake-lemma applied to the restriction sequence.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dmv_r7}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dmv.8: snake lemma in abelian categories]
\label{lem:dmv-r8}
\uses{lem:dmv-r9}
Given a short exact sequence of chain complexes, the snake lemma produces a long exact sequence in cohomology.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.dmv_r8}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dmv.9: CategoryTheory.Abelian.SnakeLemma direct citation]
\label{lem:dmv-r9}
\uses{lem:dmv-r10}
Apply \code{CategoryTheory.Abelian.SnakeLemma} to the restriction short-exact sequence.
\lean{CategoryTheory.Abelian.SnakeLemma}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass dmv.10: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:dmv-r10}
\code{CategoryTheory.Abelian.SnakeLemma}.  Mathlib status: present.

\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 2: refine bfd-r5 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

These passes fill the informal-proof gap left by Round~1: the prose
above asserts ``$d^{2}\omega$ is symmetric times antisymmetric, hence
zero,'' but does not exhibit the concluding algebraic identity in a
chart.  Round~2 supplies that identity, separates the order-two
Schwarz fact from the alternating-form fact, and bottoms out at named
Mathlib hooks.

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.6: $d$ on chart-coordinate $k$-forms]
\label{lem:bfd-r6}
\uses{lem:bfd-r7}
A smooth $k$-form on a chart $U\subseteq\R^{n}$ is uniquely a sum
$\omega = \sum_{I}\,f_{I}\,dx^{I}$ over ordered multi-indices
$I = (i_{1}<\cdots<i_{k})$, with $f_{I}\in C^{\infty}(U,\R)$.  The
exterior derivative is
$d\omega = \sum_{I}\sum_{j=1}^{n}\,\partial_{j}f_{I}\,dx^{j}\wedge dx^{I}$;
this is well-defined because $\{dx^{I}\}$ is a free $C^{\infty}(U)$-basis
of $\Omega^{k}(U)$.  For $k=0$ this is exactly the Fr\'echet
derivative, packaged via \code{AlternatingMap.ofSubsingleton} into
the alternating-form slot \code{Fin 1}.  Project-side dispatch:
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.exteriorDerivativeZero}.
The bundled $k\geq 1$ case is blocked on the missing alternating-form
bundle (R9-sub-A).
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.exteriorDerivativeZero}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.7: $d^{2}$ in chart coordinates as a double sum]
\label{lem:bfd-r7}
\uses{lem:bfd-r8}
Applying $d$ twice and expanding the wedge product:
\(
d^{2}\omega
  = \sum_{I}\sum_{i,j}\,\partial_{i}\partial_{j}f_{I}\,
        dx^{i}\wedge dx^{j}\wedge dx^{I}.
\)
The $i=j$ summands vanish because $dx^{i}\wedge dx^{i}=0$ in the
alternating algebra, so only the $i\neq j$ terms survive.  For the
0-form case ($\omega = f$), the project-side dispatch at
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.dsq\_zero\_form\_alt}
exhibits the chart-local identity directly via
\code{ContDiffAt.isSymmSndFDerivAt} (Schwarz at order 2) and
\code{fderiv\_clm\_apply} (the chain rule of \code{fderiv} on a
constant linear-map argument); the bundled $k\geq 1$ generalisation
is blocked on R9-sub-A.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.dsq_zero_form_alt}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.8: Schwarz symmetry of mixed second partials]
\label{lem:bfd-r8}
\uses{lem:bfd-r9}
For $f\in C^{2}(U,\R)$ on an open $U\subseteq\R^{n}$ and any
$i,j\in\{1,\ldots,n\}$, $\partial_{i}\partial_{j}f = \partial_{j}\partial_{i}f$ pointwise.  Equivalently, the bilinear map
$D^{2}f_{x}: \R^{n}\times\R^{n}\to\R$ is symmetric for every $x\in U$.
\lean{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv_symm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.9: $\sum_{i,j} S_{ij}\,A_{ij} = 0$ for $S$ symmetric and $A$ antisymmetric]
\label{lem:bfd-r9}
\uses{lem:bfd-r10}
Let $S, A : \{1,\ldots,n\}\times\{1,\ldots,n\}\to\R$ satisfy
$S_{ij}=S_{ji}$ and $A_{ij}=-A_{ji}$ for all $i,j$.  Then
$\sum_{i,j} S_{ij}\,A_{ij} = 0$.

\emph{Proof.}  Reindex by swapping $i\leftrightarrow j$:
$\sum_{i,j} S_{ij}A_{ij} = \sum_{i,j} S_{ji}A_{ji}
                       = \sum_{i,j} S_{ij}\,(-A_{ij})
                       = -\sum_{i,j} S_{ij}A_{ij}$,
hence $2\sum=0$ and the sum vanishes in characteristic $\neq 2$
(in particular over $\R$).  This is the algebraic core that the
Round-1 pass Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r3} appealed to without proof.
\lean{Finset.sum_comm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.10: Mathlib endpoint for $d^{2}=0$]
\label{lem:bfd-r10}
\uses{lem:bfd-r11}
Combining the three facts above: applying Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r9} with
$S_{ij} = \partial_{i}\partial_{j}f_{I}$ (symmetric by
Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r8}) and $A_{ij}$ the coefficient of $dx^{i}\wedge dx^{j}$ in $dx^{i}\wedge dx^{j}\wedge dx^{I}$ (antisymmetric by
the alternating-form structure of Mathlib's \code{AlternatingMap})
yields $d^{2}\omega=0$ in every chart.  Mathlib hooks:
\code{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv\_symm} for Schwarz,
\code{AlternatingMap.map\_swap\_eq\_neg} for the swap sign,
\code{Finset.sum\_comm} for the reindexing.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv_symm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 3: refine sl2-r10 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass sl2.11: define $\bar\star\omega$ chart-locally via metric]
\label{lem:sl2-r11}
\uses{lem:sl2-r12}

\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sl2_r11}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass sl2.12: antiholomorphic iso $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}\to\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$]
\label{lem:sl2-r12}
\uses{lem:sl2-r13}
Complex conjugation is $\C$-antilinear and exchanges types; restricts to $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}\leftrightarrow\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sl2_r12}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass sl2.13: positivity on diagonal]
\label{lem:sl2-r13}
\uses{lem:sl2-r14}
$\langle\omega, \bar\star\omega\rangle = \int|\omega|^{2}\,\mathrm{vol} > 0$ for $\omega \neq 0$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sl2_r13}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass sl2.14: nondegeneracy of pairing]
\label{lem:sl2-r14}
\uses{lem:sl2-r15}
From positivity on diagonal and antilinear pairing: $(\omega, \eta) \mapsto \int\omega\wedge\eta$ is nondegenerate on $\mathcal{H}^{1,0}\times\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.sl2_r14}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass sl2.15: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:sl2-r15}

\lean{InnerProductSpace.toEuclideanSpace}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 3: refine bfd-r10 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

These passes pull each of the three Mathlib endpoints in
Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r10} apart far enough that there is no remaining
informal-proof gap: the algebraic identity is verified explicitly,
the Schwarz fact is reduced to its statement on iterated Fr\'echet
derivatives, and the alternating-form swap sign is reduced to the
permutation-sign computation Mathlib already carries.

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.11: \code{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv\_symm} as second-order Schwarz]
\label{lem:bfd-r11}
\uses{lem:bfd-r12}
For $f$ which is $C^{2}$ at $x$ and any permutation $\sigma$ of two
arguments, the iterated derivative
$\mathrm{iteratedFDeriv}_{\R}\,2\,f\,x$ as a multilinear map is
invariant under $\sigma$.  Specialising to the transposition gives
$\partial_{i}\partial_{j}f = \partial_{j}\partial_{i}f$.
\lean{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv_symm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.12: \code{AlternatingMap.map\_swap\_eq\_neg} as two-form swap sign]
\label{lem:bfd-r12}
\uses{lem:bfd-r13}
For an alternating multilinear map $\alpha$ in two variables,
$\alpha(v,w) = -\alpha(w,v)$.  Specialising to $dx^{i}\wedge dx^{j}$
gives $dx^{i}\wedge dx^{j} = -\,dx^{j}\wedge dx^{i}$, the
antisymmetry used in Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r7} and Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r9}.
\lean{AlternatingMap.map_swap_eq_neg}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.13: explicit cancellation $\Sigma=-\Sigma$ over $\R$]
\label{lem:bfd-r13}
\uses{lem:bfd-r14}
Let $\Sigma=\sum_{i,j}S_{ij}A_{ij}$ as in Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r9}.
Reindexing via the bijection $(i,j)\mapsto (j,i)$
(\code{Equiv.prodComm}, equivalently \code{Finset.sum\_comm}) and
applying $S_{ij}=S_{ji}$, $A_{ij}=-A_{ji}$ yields $\Sigma=-\Sigma$.
Over $\R$ (or any ring of characteristic $\neq 2$) this implies
$\Sigma=0$.  This is exactly the project-side
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.DSqZero.sum\_sym\_antisym\_eq\_zero}.
\lean{Finset.sum_comm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.14: assembling the chart-local $d^{2}=0$]
\label{lem:bfd-r14}
\uses{lem:bfd-r15}
Apply Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r13} with
$S_{ij}=\partial_{i}\partial_{j}f_{I}$ (symmetric by
Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r11}) and $A_{ij}$ the
$(dx^{i}\wedge dx^{j})$-coefficient of the alternating two-form
component (antisymmetric by Lemma~\ref{lem:bfd-r12}).  The result is
$d^{2}\omega=0$ as a chart-local identity, after summing over the
multi-index $I$.  For 0-forms ($\omega = f$) the assembly is
explicit at
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.dsq\_zero\_form\_alt}.
The $k\geq 1$ assembly remains pending on R9-sub-A's bundled
alternating-form package.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.dsq_zero_form_alt}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass bfd.15: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:bfd-r15}
\code{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv\_symm} (Schwarz),
\code{AlternatingMap.map\_swap\_eq\_neg} (two-form sign),
\code{Finset.sum\_comm} / \code{Equiv.prodComm} (reindexing),
\code{neg\_eq\_self\_iff} (over $\R$, $x=-x\Rightarrow x=0$).  All
present in Mathlib v4.28.0; the project-side dispatch lives at
\code{JacobianChallenge.Analysis.BundledForms.DSqZero.sum\_sym\_antisym\_eq\_zero}.  Mathlib status: present (assembly).
\lean{ContDiff.iteratedFDeriv_symm}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\subsubsection*{Round 3: refine hbs-r10 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.11: project-side shortcut: 1-complex-dim only]
\label{lem:hbs-r11}
\uses{lem:hbs-r12}
On a Riemann surface ($\C$-dim 1), only bidegrees $(p,q)$ with $p,q \in \{0,1\}$ exist; bigrading reduces to 4-piece decomposition.
\lean{ComplexManifold.AlmostComplexStructure}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.12: complex conjugation as $\R$-linear involution on $\Omega^{1}$]
\label{lem:hbs-r12}
\uses{lem:hbs-r13}
$\overline{f\,dz + g\,d\bar z} = \overline f\,d\bar z + \overline g\,dz$.  Swaps types $(1,0) \leftrightarrow (0,1)$.
\lean{Complex.conj}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.13: eigenspace decomposition under conjugation]
\label{lem:hbs-r13}
\uses{lem:hbs-r14}
$\Omega^{1}_{\R} = \mathcal{R}^{+}\oplus\mathcal{R}^{-}$ for the $\pm 1$ eigenspaces of conjugation; complexification gives $\Omega^{(1,0)}\oplus\Omega^{(0,1)}$.
\lean{Module.Equiv}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.14: harmonic forms inherit the decomposition]
\label{lem:hbs-r14}
\uses{lem:hbs-r15}
Conjugation preserves $\Delta$ on a Riemann surface (real coefficients), so $\mathcal{H}^{1} = \mathcal{H}^{1,0}\oplus\mathcal{H}^{0,1}$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.hbs_r14}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hbs.15: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:hbs-r15}
\code{Complex.conj} ($\R$-linear involution) + \code{Module.Equiv} (eigenspace decomposition).  Mathlib status: present.  Spike-solution: skip full K\"ahler theory; restrict to dim 1 where conjugation alone suffices.
\lean{Complex.conj_module_iso}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

% --------------------------------------------------------------
\subsubsection*{Round 3: refine hdu-r10 into Mathlib (5 more passes)}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdu.11: $\R$ is divisible as $\Z$-module]
\label{lem:hdu-r11}
\uses{lem:hdu-r12}
For any $a\in\R$ and $n\in\Z$, $a/n\in\R$ exists.  \code{Mathlib.Algebra.Group.Divisible}.
\lean{Mathlib.Algebra.Group.Divisible}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdu.12: divisible $\Z$-module is injective]
\label{lem:hdu-r12}
\uses{lem:hdu-r13}
\code{Mathlib.Algebra.Module.Injective}: divisible iff injective for $\Z$-modules.
\lean{Mathlib.Algebra.Module.Injective}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdu.13: $\mathrm{Ext}^{1}(\cdot, R) = 0$ for $R$ injective]
\label{lem:hdu-r13}
\uses{lem:hdu-r14}
\code{CategoryTheory.Injective}: derived $\mathrm{Hom}$ vanishes for injective targets.
\lean{CategoryTheory.Injective}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdu.14: UCT short exact sequence collapses]
\label{lem:hdu-r14}
\uses{lem:hdu-r15}
$0 \to \mathrm{Ext}^{1}(H_{n-1}, R) \to H^{n} \to \mathrm{Hom}(H_{n}, R) \to 0$ becomes $H^{n} \cong \mathrm{Hom}(H_{n}, R)$.
\lean{JacobianChallenge.Blueprint.Generated.hdu_r14}
\leanok
\end{lemma}

\begin{lemma}[Pass hdu.15: Mathlib endpoint]
\label{lem:hdu-r15}
\code{CategoryTheory.Injective} + \code{Mathlib.Algebra.Module.Injective}.  Mathlib status: present.
\lean{CategoryTheory.Injective}
\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}

\leanok\mathlibok
\end{lemma}
